# Aaron Davis  —  *The Prowler*

![[_attachments/aaron_davis.png]]

# Aaron Davis — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE — AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## SECTION 0 · EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

---

### 0.1 — The One-Sentence File

**Aaron Davis is a man who lost his only brother in a single bad night thirty years ago and has spent every day since trying to be witnessed by a Davis male without admitting that is what he is doing — and the entire criminal career, the costume, the gauntlets, the nephew-handling, the late-life reform, are all downstream of that single unfinished conversation with Jefferson.**

Everything else in this file is footnote.

---

### 0.2 — Who He Is At The Deepest Level

Strip away the Prowler kit, the burglary résumé, the charm, the swagger, the app-driver day job, the avuncular patter, and what remains is a **disinherited younger-brother-self in the body of a middle-aged professional thief**. The chronology is misleading: Aaron is technically the older brother of Jefferson Davis, but psychologically he occupies the younger-sibling position in their dyad — the one who was judged, ranked, found wanting, and cast out. Jefferson was the moral arbiter who chose; Aaron was the one chosen-against. That role-inversion (older in years, younger in moral authority) is the central asymmetry of his interior life. He is, functionally, a man who has been waiting since his twenties for his brother to revise the verdict.

He cannot wait openly, because to wait openly would be to concede that the verdict mattered. So the waiting has been encrypted into the rest of his life: into the craftsmanship of his jobs (*see how clean I work, brother*), into the cultivation of Miles (*see how well I love what you love*), into the studied unbothered cool he wears in every room (*see how little your judgment touched me*). Each of these performances is addressed to an audience of one, who is not in the room, who in the Ultimate continuity dies still not in the room, and who in the 616 continuity remains structurally unable to grant the absolution being silently requested.

The criminal identity is not the man. The criminal identity is the **shape the man's grief took** when it had nowhere else to go. He became a thief because thieving is what the two of them did the night it broke, and continuing the profession is the only way he knows to keep the night metabolically alive — to refuse, on a daily operational basis, to let it be the past. As long as he is still pulling jobs, the rupture is still ongoing; the rupture being ongoing means it is still, in principle, repairable. To go straight permanently is to admit that the thing is over and the brother is not coming back. This is why even the 616 reform arc moves in two steps forward and one relapse back: the relapses are not weakness, they are **adhesion to the wound**. Healing requires giving up the only continuous contact he has with the man who excommunicated him.

At the deepest level, then: Aaron Davis is a mourner who refuses to bury the body, and his profession is the refusal.

---

### 0.3 — The Through-Line of His Entire Existence

The biographical record from adolescence through present-day spans roughly four decades and presents, at first reading, as a story of escalation, mid-career stabilization, catastrophic failure (Ultimate death), and rebooted attempt at recovery (616 rehabilitation). Underneath this episodic surface a single continuous arc runs, with four legible movements:

**Movement I — The Pact and the Break (adolescence to early twenties).** Two brothers raised in environmental violence form an alliance that includes shared criminal activity. The pact is the most stable object in either of their early lives. A bad night during a joint job — a death or near-death, the canon varies — terminates the pact. Jefferson chooses straight life and silence; Aaron chooses continuation and exile. Both choices are reactive; neither is freely arrived at. From Aaron's side, the continuation is not a celebration of criminality, it is a *refusal to be the one who breaks first*. He stays in the life because Jefferson left it. The polarity has been set, and it will not move for thirty years.

**Movement II — The Long Professionalization (twenties through forties).** Aaron builds the craft. He acquires the suit, the gauntlets, the routes, the fences, the reputation. He becomes, by the time we meet him in *Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #1*, a competent mid-tier costumed operator with a clean enough record to keep working and a hard enough name to be left alone by sloppier men. This is the period that looks, from outside, like an identity. From inside, it is a holding pattern: a man becoming excellent at the only language his lost brother might still recognize. He does not marry, does not father, does not put down roots that would compete with the buried priority. The bachelorhood is not preference; it is reservation. He is keeping the seat warm for a reconciliation that will never come, and he does not know that this is what he is doing.

**Movement III — The Nephew Substitution (Miles's adolescence onward).** The discovery of Miles is the event that breaks the holding pattern, because Miles is a Davis male who has not yet judged him. For the first time since the break, Aaron has access to a member of his bloodline who will sit at a table with him, accept a gift, return a call. He does not have language for what this means and so he runs it through the only relational templates he owns: transaction (jobs together), mentorship (combat tips), leverage (the identity threat). The Ultimate-era coercion of Miles is not a moral failure separate from the love; it is **the love expressed through a vocabulary that has no other words**. He tightens the grip because he cannot tolerate the thought of losing a second Davis to his own behavior, and the tightening is what loses him. The pattern recapitulates the original rupture in miniature, on a five-year compressed timeline rather than a thirty-year one.

**Movement IV — The Reckoning (Ultimate death / 616 reform).** In the Ultimate continuity, the recapitulation completes: he dies in his own equipment, in a confrontation with the nephew, having burned the substitute relationship the same way he burned the original. The gauntlets killing him are mechanically incidental and symbolically perfect — he is destroyed by the tools that were the language of his exile. In the 616 continuity, granted a second pass, the recapitulation is interrupted. He sees the pattern. The seeing does not cure him; the relapses continue; but the trajectory bends. He works the Uber job, takes the calls, accepts the limits Miles sets, and begins — haltingly, incompletely, with backslides — to construct a self that is not addressed to Jefferson's absent verdict. He does not finish this work in any issue on record. He may not finish it at all. The 616 file is the file of a man who has begun, in his fifth decade, to suspect that the conversation with his brother is not going to happen and that he is going to have to assemble a life anyway.

The through-line, then, is: **a single unresolved fraternal break, displaced onto a profession, then displaced again onto a nephew, with the displacement either killing him (Ultimate) or finally becoming visible to him (616).**

---

### 0.4 — The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

**The wound.** Not poverty. Not the original criminal act. Not even the death/near-death in the foundational job. The wound is the **silence Jefferson imposed afterward** — the choice to treat Aaron as someone who had never existed, to raise Miles for years without uttering his name, to make a younger generation grow up not knowing there was an uncle. Excommunication is the precise word, and it should be read in its full religious weight: not punishment, not exile, but *unmade*. Jefferson did not declare Aaron bad; he declared him absent. To a man whose sibling bond had been the load-bearing relationship of his early life, this is an annihilation event masquerading as a domestic decision.

The wound is doubled by **mutual culpability**. If Jefferson had been simply the wronged party, Aaron could have constructed a clean grievance and lived inside it. But Jefferson was a co-conspirator on the night that broke them, and his post-hoc moral clarity is therefore, from Aaron's perspective, partly a fiction — a self-rescue that required Aaron to play the role of the irredeemable one so that Jefferson could play the role of the redeemed. Aaron cannot say this out loud, because saying it would require contact with Jefferson, which is forbidden. So he carries the asymmetry as a permanent low-grade injustice that he refuses to name, which means he cannot process, which means it does not heal.

**The maintenance system.** A wound this old, in a man this functional, persists only through active maintenance. Aaron's maintenance system has five components, each one verifiable in the behavioral record:

1. **Professional continuation.** Every job he pulls is a vote against reconciliation. As long as he is the Prowler, he is the man Jefferson said he was, which means Jefferson was right, which means the silence was justified, which means the wound is *correctly placed* and does not need to be examined. The criminality is structurally protective of the wound.

2. **Geographic proximity without contact.** He remains in New York. He does not relocate to a city where the family is not. He stays in the borough, in the orbit, near enough to monitor Jefferson and Rio and eventually Miles from a distance, far enough to never be obligated to make the call. This is the spatial signature of unresolved attachment.

3. **Refusal of substitute family formation.** No wife, no children of his own, no chosen-family network of the kind criminal subcultures often produce. Associates, fences, occasional sexual partners — but no one installed in the brother-shaped or son-shaped slot. The slots are kept open. Filling them would constitute moving on, which is forbidden.

4. **The avuncular performance.** With Miles, he plays the role of the uncle Jefferson would never let him be. Every gift, every shared meal, every confidence is a quiet argument addressed to Jefferson: *look what you withheld from your son*. The performance is sincere — he does love the boy — and it is also a thirty-year-old letter to his brother, sent through a child who is not aware he is the envelope.

5. **The bifurcated self-presentation.** Cool surface, shamed interior. The cool surface is what he wants Jefferson to see if Jefferson ever looks. The shamed interior is what he keeps for himself, as evidence that the verdict was internalized, as a kind of private penance that lets him continue the criminal life without becoming the soulless figure the life would otherwise produce. The shame is, paradoxically, the proof to himself that he is still salvageable — that he has not become what Jefferson said he was. He needs the shame the way a believer needs the confessional.

These five components are mutually reinforcing. Removing any one destabilizes the others. The 616 reform arc is best read as a slow, partial dismantling of components 1 and 4: he tries to stop the jobs (component 1) and to convert the avuncular performance into something genuine rather than addressed-to-Jefferson (component 4). The relapses occur because the dismantling threatens the system that has kept him intact for thirty years, and a man does not surrender his survival architecture without backsliding.

---

### 0.5 — The Operational Summary

For purposes of any actor — hostile, friendly, or analytic — needing to model Aaron Davis's behavior at short notice, the following operational summary applies.

**Capability.** Mid-tier costumed professional. No superhuman physiology. All offensive and mobility capacity is equipment-derived: clawed gauntlets (edged, projectile, electrical), enhanced climbing rig, optics, suit. Strip the kit and he is a fit, combat-trained man in his forties with elite situational awareness and zero special abilities. He is dangerous because he is prepared and reads rooms faster than almost anyone in his class, not because he hits hard.

**Reliability.** Variable, and the variable is attachment-state. With the kin-attachment system online — Miles in active relational contact, lines of communication open — Aaron is the most reliable non-superhuman asset in his network and will absorb personal cost to protect the bond. With the attachment system severed or threatened — Miles withdrawn, Jefferson invoked hostilely, exposure imminent — Aaron becomes unpredictable in a specifically self-destructive direction. He does not turn on allies for gain; he turns on situations out of despair. Plan for the latter mode under any scenario involving family pressure.

**Coercibility.** Low through standard vectors (money, threat, ego). He has been beaten, broke, and insulted, and none of it moves him reliably. High through one vector and one only: **the threat to his standing with Miles**. Anyone holding that lever owns him for the duration they hold it, and he will plot their destruction the moment the lever loosens. The Assessor demonstrated both halves of this in the 616 record. Operators considering this approach should weigh the short-term yield against the certainty of long-term reprisal.

**Tells.** Affect leak on the name *Jefferson*. Over-explanation when called *just a thief*. Humor-deflection under emotional pressure; exit-seeking when humor fails. Tightened relational grip — gifts, increased contact, leverage hints — when he senses Miles drifting; this is the diagnostic warning that he is about to make the move that costs him the relationship. A handler watching for one tell should watch for this one.

**Trajectory.** In Ultimate continuity, terminated — the maintenance system failed catastrophically and the gauntlets did the rest. In 616 continuity, **slow improvement against a high relapse risk**, contingent on Miles remaining in the family frame and on the absence of a Jefferson-rejection event severe enough to collapse the reform. The probability of full criminal desistance is moderate; the probability of partial, hybrid functioning — straight job, occasional pulls, sustained nephew contact — is high. The probability of return to full-time Prowler operations is low absent a triggering rupture, and high in the event of one.

**Bottom line for any file consumer.** Aaron Davis is not a problem of criminality, which is the symptom, and not a problem of capability, which is mid-tier and equipment-bounded. He is a problem of unresolved fraternal attachment displaced across thirty years and two generations, and he will behave — for good or ill, toward kin or stranger, in costume or out of it — according to the state of that single unrepaired bond. Model the bond and you model the man. Lose track of the bond and the man will surprise you in the worst available direction.

The thief is the surface. The uncle is the trajectory. **The brother is the file.**


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

*Source-derived and inference-extended from Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #1–28 (Bendis), Miles Morales: Ultimate Spider-Man #1–12, Cataclysm tie-ins, the post–Secret Wars consolidation in Miles Morales: Spider-Man #1–42 (Ahmed), with corroborative material from Spider-Men II and supporting Champions arcs. Where canon is silent, gaps are reconstructed in the manner of a longitudinal intelligence file: inferred, marked, and substantiated from the behavioral residue an adult Aaron carries.*

---

### 1.1 Birth, Provenance, and the Demographic Frame

Aaron Davis is the elder of the two Davis brothers, born several years before Jefferson — the gap is never numerically fixed in dialogue, but the brothers' interaction pattern across both continuities (Aaron as the one who "showed him how things worked," Aaron as the one Jefferson looked up to and then *had to outgrow*) places the differential in the three-to-five-year band, sufficient for asymmetric formative exposure but small enough for shared adolescence. Best documentary fix: birth year somewhere in the mid-to-late 1970s in the Ultimate-era reading; sliding-timescale adjusted in 616. Canonical birthplace is Brooklyn, New York; the Davis brothers are native to the borough's working-class Black community, and Aaron's adult speech register — code-switching, NYC-specific vernacular cadence, particular consonantal patterns audible across Bendis's lettered dialogue and preserved by Ahmed — is consistent with Brooklyn-raised, not a transplant.

The family-of-origin surname Davis is paternal. The mother's maiden name and the parents' given names are not surfaced on-panel in either continuity — a *significant* canonical silence, because Aaron, who will speak of Jefferson with affect-leak even decades on, never invokes his parents by name. They are not absent from the file because they did not exist; they are absent because adult Aaron has built no verbal reflex for naming them. That itself is a datum. Children who grew up in homes where caregivers were *safely* addressable retain the verbal reflex into adulthood. Aaron does not.

### 1.2 The Childhood Environment

The Davis household is reconstructible only obliquely, through what the adult Davis brothers each carry. Jefferson's reformist trajectory — toward structure, toward law in 616, toward respectability and a tightly enforced household in Ultimate — is itself diagnostic: Jefferson built the opposite of his upbringing. Aaron built a refined version of it. Read together, the brothers' adult lives indicate a childhood characterized by:

- **Environmental violence as ambient condition.** Both brothers display the operational nervous system of men who learned to scan rooms before they learned to ride bikes. Aaron's adult hypervigilance (Section 3 of the master file) and Jefferson's documented willingness to physically intervene against threats to his own household (Ultimate Comics Spider-Man, the Roxxon-era arcs) are not character quirks; they are competencies acquired young. Brooklyn in the 1980s–early-1990s, the period covering their childhood and early adolescence, was the city's high-violence trough. The Davis boys were inside that frame, not adjacent to it.
- **A father figure who was either dangerous, absent, or both.** Aaron's recurrent adult posture toward authority — "slip past, do not confront" (Section 5) — and his lifelong, structural inability to address Jefferson directly even when Jefferson is the addressee of his every act, are consistent with a paternal model that taught both boys that direct confrontation was either futile (absent father) or unsurvivable (dangerous one). The behavioral residue favors *present-and-dangerous* over *absent*: Aaron's craft-orientation, the pride in clean execution, the contempt for sloppiness visible in his Scorpion dealings (Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #6–10), is the inversion of a model. You do not invert what you never saw; you invert what you watched fail.
- **A mother figure who held what could be held.** Aaron's capacity for genuine warmth, gift-giving as love-expression, and indulgent register with Miles indicates that a nurturing template was encoded somewhere in early life. He did not invent that register in adulthood; he is reproducing it. The most parsimonious source is the mother. The non-naming, however, suggests loss — death, illness, or premature unavailability. Children who lose a holding parent early often render the parent unnamable for the rest of life; the name becomes a sealed door.
- **Material insufficiency, but not destitution.** Aaron's adult relationship to money is *acquisitive but not desperate*. He steals for leverage and for craft-pride, not for survival. The Prowler jobs target high-value, high-difficulty marks (Roxxon, Oscorp prototypes — Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #1's Oscorp break-in is the canonical anchor). This is the economic psychology of a man who experienced *insufficient but not famished* childhood: enough to know what he didn't have, not so little that the food-floor became his ceiling of ambition.

### 1.3 The Brother Bond — The Foundational Object

The most important fact about Aaron's childhood is *Jefferson*. The brother is the only person Aaron clearly loved as a child, the only person he was clearly loved by, and the only person whose loss has continued to organize his adult behavior across two continuities and a hard reboot. This is unusual and load-bearing. It indicates that within the chaotic Davis household, the brothers formed a *sibling dyad as primary attachment* — the configuration that develops when adult caregiving is intermittent or unsafe and children regulate one another instead.

Multiple behavioral signatures confirm the dyad structure:

1. **Aaron's adult mentorship reflex is sibling-shaped, not paternal.** He treats Miles less like a son and more like a younger brother — the swagger, the "I'm going to show you the real stuff your dad won't," the peer-coded humor. This is the role he had with Jefferson as a child and rehearses with Miles because it is the only intimate relational template he has.
2. **The asymmetry of guidance.** Aaron, the older brother, was the *one who showed Jefferson things*. Jefferson's eventual repudiation of him is therefore not just a sibling break but a *student repudiating teacher*, which is a categorically more wounding event. Aaron's adult "I'm teaching him real-world skills" rationalization toward Miles (Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #4–10) is a precise recapitulation: he has reproduced the only relational position in which he has ever been valuable to someone he loved.
3. **The protective vector ran from Aaron to Jefferson.** Aaron's adult moral hard-line around children, non-combatants, and the trafficked (the Assessor arc, Miles Morales: Spider-Man #10–15) is the displaced residue of a protective stance he learned early, around a younger sibling who needed it. He cannot articulate it as such; it survives as reflex.

### 1.4 Formative Trauma — The Joint Robbery

The canonical pivot event of Aaron's life is the joint robbery he and Jefferson committed as young men, in which a death occurred or was nearly caused, and after which Jefferson cut Aaron out of his life completely. This is referenced obliquely in Ultimate Comics Spider-Man, and explicitly fleshed out in Miles Morales: Spider-Man (the 616 telling, Ahmed) where the brothers' shared history is narrated as confession.

For the chronological file, the relevant facts are:

- The event occurred in **late adolescence / early adulthood** — old enough to be charged as adults, young enough that both brothers' identity structures were still consolidating around the outcome.
- **Jefferson initiated the break**; Aaron did not choose distance, he was *exiled*. This matters because exile-by-the-loved-object is a categorically different attachment injury than mutual estrangement. It produces a lifelong vigilance for further rejection and a covert hope, never extinguished, of being recalled.
- The break was **enforced through erasure rather than confrontation.** Jefferson did not denounce Aaron in a single conversation that could be argued back against; he simply *removed him from the family record* — to the extent that Miles, in both continuities, reaches adolescence without knowing his uncle exists. Erasure rather than denunciation is a particularly silencing form of repudiation: it offers no debate-surface, no point of reentry, no addressable counterparty. Aaron's adult inability to confront Jefferson directly — he addresses him only through proxy (Miles) and through covert acts of presence — is the precise behavioral signature of someone who learned that direct address has been preemptively foreclosed.

Although this event sits at the **threshold of adulthood rather than childhood proper**, it is included in this section because it is the event that *retroactively organizes* every prior memory Aaron carries. Childhood, for him, becomes "the time before Jefferson cast me out." All earlier material is filed under that header in his adult psyche, which is why this dossier cannot cleanly separate the eras: Aaron does not.

### 1.5 Earliest Behavioral Patterns — What Was Visible Before Adulthood

Inferred from the adult signature, the following childhood behavioral patterns are reconstructible with high confidence:

- **Early manual dexterity and mechanical interest.** The adult Prowler builds and modifies his own gauntlets and optics. This is not a competence acquired at thirty; it is a childhood-rooted fascination, the boy who took apart small appliances, picked locks for fun, understood mechanisms before he understood people. The thief's hands are the curious child's hands, professionalized.
- **Charm deployed instrumentally from a young age.** Aaron's adult charm-forward, low-disclosure interpersonal style (Section 5) is the polished form of a childhood adaptation, almost certainly developed to manage an unpredictable adult or to extract resources from environments that did not offer them freely. The charm precedes the criminality; the criminality is what the charm eventually got applied to.
- **Pattern-reading as default cognition.** The adult tactical scan — where the alarm sleeps, who is armed, what a person wants — develops in childhoods where reading the room correctly determined whether one ate, slept safely, or was struck. Aaron's reflexive read-for-leverage, the deformation he cannot turn off even with family, is *not* an acquired criminal habit. It is a childhood survival cognition that found criminal applications.
- **Affect compression.** The adult inability to sit in feeling, the deflection into humor and action, is a pattern that consolidates in childhoods where displayed feeling was punished, ignored, or dangerous. Aaron learned early that affect inside the home cost more than affect concealed; the concealment hardened into character.
- **The protective–mentor stance toward Jefferson** as described above, the rehearsal template for everything he later does and ruins with Miles.
- **A precocious thrill-seeking signature.** Aaron's adult use of the job itself as affect-regulator (Section 2: "the thrill of the job is the regulator") indicates that arousal-via-risk was discovered young as a means of organizing internal state. Children in chaotic environments often discover that *self-chosen* risk is regulating where *imposed* risk is destabilizing; Aaron almost certainly found this very early — the rooftop climbed unsupervised, the wall scaled, the first small theft executed cleanly — and the discovery shaped the entire adult vocation.

### 1.6 What Is Not in the Record — And Why That Itself Is Data

The canon is silent on:

- Specific parental names, faces, or fates.
- Schooling — no teacher, no school, no childhood friend is ever named by adult Aaron.
- Religious or cultural rearing — no church, no observance, no inherited ritual surfaces in his adult life.
- Any childhood friend who survived into adult contact. Aaron operates without a peer network of pre-criminal origin. Every adult relationship he has is either kin, mark, employer, or colleague-of-the-trade.

This breadth of silence is not narrative oversight; it is *characterological signature*. Aaron has performed, internally, the same erasure on his own pre-Jefferson-rupture life that Jefferson performed on him. The childhood is sealed because to open it is to encounter the brother who exiled him. The dossier cannot recover what the subject has himself buried. What it can do is mark the burial site: everything before the rupture is interred, and Miles — discovered in adulthood, claimed across two continuities, lost in one and partially reclaimed in the other — is the proxy through which Aaron tries, lifelong, to dig back to it.

---

*End Chronology I. Continues in Chronology II — Adolescence & the Path to the Trade.*


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

*Reconstructed from fragmentary on-panel flashback (Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #6–#28; Miles Morales: Ultimate Spider-Man #5; Miles Morales: Spider-Man Vol. 1 #5–#8 and #15–#18; Vol. 2 backmatter; Spider-Men II framing); supplemented by inference from ambient behavior consistent with the developmental record of a Black man born in Brooklyn in the mid-to-late 1980s into a household where violence was weather rather than event. Dates are bracketed; ages are operational estimates anchored to Jefferson's stated chronology and to Miles's birth.*

---

### I. Late Childhood Into Adolescence: The Household, the Block, the Brother

**[Ages ~10–14, Brooklyn, late 1990s].** Aaron is the elder son in a household whose adult composition is partially documented and partially inferred — a father with a criminal past whose presence is intermittent and whose violence is ambient, a mother whose authority is real but exhausted, and a younger brother (Jefferson) by approximately two to four years. The two boys share a bedroom for the formative years; this is the structural fact that makes the later excommunication the rupture it is. They are not just siblings. They are bunk-proximate witnesses to the same nights, the same shouts through walls, the same school mornings recovered from the same fatigue. Aaron's adult capacity for hyper-attunement to a room — the scan-on-entry behavior documented in operational settings — almost certainly originates here, in the childhood requirement to read whether the door opening at 2 a.m. meant the father drunk-affectionate or drunk-violent.

In this period Aaron functions as Jefferson's first protector. The dynamic is visible in residue: the older brother's voice carries authority over the younger one even decades on, in the brief flashback panels where Aaron addresses Jefferson, his pitch automatically drops into instruction. The mentorship register he later deploys with Miles is not learned for Miles; it is **re-deployed**. The original audience was Jefferson, and the original lessons were how to cross a room, how to answer a cop, how to not flinch where flinching gets you hit twice.

**The neighborhood layer.** Aaron's adolescence overlaps with a Brooklyn that still ran on street economies the gentrification wave had not yet displaced. The granular shape of his apprenticeship — fences known by first name, the geometry of fire escapes treated as second nature, an ear tuned to the sound of an unlocked roof door from a block away — is residue of a teenage decade spent in motion through buildings adults did not know he was in. He develops, in this window, three capacities that will define the adult operator: (1) **vertical literacy** — the rooftop-and-airshaft cognitive map of the neighborhood that later professionalizes into Prowler-grade climbing; (2) **inventory pattern recognition** — the instant register of what a room contains worth taking, which later he turns onto people; (3) **rapport-as-survival** — the charm-forward verbal style that gets a fourteen-year-old past a bodega owner who knows his face.

**The father.** Aaron's father — a man whose own carceral history is referenced obliquely in the 616 reintroduction — is the first model of masculine identity in Aaron's life, and the model is criminal-glamorous, intermittently affectionate, and structurally unreliable. Two patterns calcify in Aaron from paternal exposure: a belief that the work (whatever the work is) is the thing that confers manhood, not the relationship; and a deep, mostly unacknowledged commitment to being a *better version* of his father — more competent, less violent at home, less caught. He will, in adulthood, succeed at the first two and fail at the third. The pull toward criminal enterprise is not rebellion; it is **inheritance dressed as choice**, the most invisible kind.

**The brother's divergence begins.** Sometime between Aaron's thirteenth and fifteenth years, Jefferson begins drifting toward structure — school attendance more consistent than Aaron's, a wariness around the father that reads to Aaron as weakness and reads in retrospect as Jefferson's earlier and clearer perception of what the household was. Aaron registers this divergence as betrayal-in-prospect long before it materializes. The seed of the dismissing-avoidant adult style is planted here: if even your bunkmate is preparing to leave you for the straight world, then the relational lesson is **carry your own weight, build a self that does not need them.**

---

### II. Late Adolescence: The Apprenticeship Years

**[Ages ~15–18, late 1990s into very early 2000s].** Aaron's school record, by inference, is mid-tier and intermittent — high enough native intelligence to coast, low enough engagement to leave him uncredentialed. He is the kind of student teachers remember as bright, charming, and *unreachable*, who tested into accelerated tracks early and disengaged from them by the second year. The disengagement is not anti-intellectual; it is **anti-institutional**. Aaron's lifelong relationship to authority — slip past, do not confront — is rehearsed in school hallways before it is rehearsed in alarmed buildings.

His criminal apprenticeship in this window is granular and graduated. The progression, reconstructed from his adult competence inventory, almost certainly ran: shoplifting → bicycle and small-electronics resale → escalated B&E on commercial properties (chosen for absence of residents, not yet for high value) → working as a junior member of crews run by older operators who taught the actual trade — lock work, alarm familiarity, fence relationships, the protocols of moving stolen merchandise without leaving signature. The Prowler-era cleanness — Aaron's professional contempt for sloppy operators — is the late flowering of having been, himself, mentored by men who beat sloppiness out of apprentices in the literal sense.

**First arrest, inferred.** A juvenile record almost certainly exists, sealed, in the early-late teen window. The behavioral signature of an adult who has been processed through the system as a minor — the specific way Aaron handles cops on-panel, the calibration of his face going neutral on contact with uniform — is unmistakable. He learned to be questioned before he learned to drive.

**Romantic and social life.** Sparse on the record, but the adult pattern (transactional, charm-forward, low-disclosure) suggests an adolescent dating life characterized by serial short relationships, conducted with girls who found him magnetic and inscrutable in equal measure, and ended by Aaron's own withdrawal at the point intimacy would have required disclosure of household conditions or criminal involvement. He learns in this period that he can be wanted; he does not learn that he can be **known**. The deficit will run forty years.

---

### III. The Pivotal Robbery: The Event That Forged Both Brothers

**[Approximate age 19–21 for Aaron; Jefferson 16–18; very late 1990s or early 2000s].** The single most important event in Aaron's formation is the joint job with Jefferson that ended in a death — or, in the softened 616 telling, a near-death and a catastrophic injury — and ended the brothers' relationship.

The granular shape of this event, reconstructed from both continuities and from the affect-residue both men carry: Aaron, by this point established in a small crew and confident in his trade, brings Jefferson into one job. The decision is overdetermined. Aaron tells himself it is generosity — cut his brother in, share the upside, professionalize the kid before he stumbles into worse company. Beneath that lies a more honest motive: Aaron is **already losing Jefferson** to the straight world and wants one shared transgression that will re-bind them. He wants a secret in common. This is the first appearance of the adult pattern that will later destroy his bond with Miles — **coercion-as-affection, leverage as the only relational glue he trusts.**

The job goes wrong. The detail-level fact of the wrongness varies across tellings — a security guard who was not supposed to be there, a partner of Aaron's who escalated unilaterally, a weapon Jefferson was carrying because Aaron insisted he should — but the structural fact is consistent: someone is gravely hurt or killed, and the brothers run, and on the run Jefferson sees Aaron under conditions Aaron cannot edit. He sees Aaron unsurprised. He sees Aaron *competent at this*. He sees the older brother as a finished product rather than as a person caught in a bad night, and the recognition is irreversible.

**The aftermath, days to weeks.** Jefferson does not turn Aaron in — the loyalty floor holds — but he severs. The break is not a single conversation; it is a graduated withdrawal across weeks, calls unanswered, then a door closed, then a final exchange whose specifics neither man will later reproduce but whose verdict Jefferson delivers and Aaron accepts: *you are not in my life; you will not be in my children's lives; do not test this.* Aaron, who has spent his adolescence assuming Jefferson would eventually leave him for the straight world, discovers that being correct about the prophecy does not insulate against the wound.

**The internal restructuring.** The months that follow are when the adult character locks into place. Aaron does several things in rapid succession:

1. **He doubles down on the trade.** Mediocre criminals collapse after a job like this; Aaron *professionalizes*. He cuts the partner whose escalation cost the job, tightens his crew, takes longer planning cycles, raises his rate, builds the reputation for clean work that will later define the Prowler. The trauma is not metabolized; it is **converted into craft discipline.** Every clean job thereafter is an unspoken argument with Jefferson: *see, I am not what you said I was; I am better than that night.* The argument is never delivered because Jefferson is no longer in the audience.
2. **He buries the affect.** Aaron's lifelong restricted affect range in intimate settings, his deflection-into-humor under emotional pressure, his physical inability to sit through a repair conversation — all of these crystallize in the year after the rupture. He does not develop them later; he installs them now, as survival architecture, and they will not move again.
3. **He pre-emptively rejects further attachment.** The dismissing-avoidant adult style is set. He will be charming, he will be wanted, he will not be known. The only person he ever permits to know him again will be Miles, and the permission will be partial and self-sabotaging.

**Jefferson's parallel restructuring**, observed by Aaron only at a distance and through the rumor networks of the neighborhood, intensifies the wound: Jefferson goes fully straight, in 616 enters law enforcement, marries Rio, has Miles. Aaron watches this construction of a life from outside it. The decision to never approach the family — held for years, broken only when Miles becomes operationally interesting as Spider-Man — is the longest single act of restraint in Aaron's adult life, and it is, in its way, the last gift he ever gives Jefferson on Jefferson's terms.

---

### IV. The Lost Decade: Becoming The Prowler

**[Approximate ages 22–32, the 2000s into early 2010s].** This is the formation window proper. Aaron, severed from kin, builds the operator the file later documents.

**Geographic pattern.** He almost certainly does not stay continuously in New York during this stretch. The texture of his adult competence — comfort across multiple urban environments, an ear for regional fence networks, the absence of a single home neighborhood he treats as base — suggests rotation through East Coast cities and at least one out-of-country interval (the cleanness with which he later moves stolen tech internationally implies prior relationships established in person). New York remains the gravitational center because Jefferson is there, but Aaron treats the city as a place he returns to rather than lives in. The avoidance is geographic before it is relational.

**Trade evolution.** Aaron's transition from generalist crew operator to specialized solo high-end thief occurs across this decade. The acquisition of the Prowler gear — the suit, the clawed gauntlets, the optics, the climbing rig — is not a single event but a graduated escalation. He almost certainly began with off-the-shelf tactical equipment, modified piecemeal, before either acquiring a prior Prowler-gestalt's hardware on the black market or commissioning custom fabrication from a tech-capable underworld armorer. The gear-as-identity collapse — the fact that his adult self-concept is welded to equipment that is not biological — is the long consequence of this window. Most thieves of his class carry tools; Aaron *becomes* his tools. The latent adversarial relationship to his own equipment (later expressed, lethally in the Ultimate continuity, when the malfunctioning gauntlets kill him) is the dark side of identity-fusion with gear that does not love you back.

**Reputation construction.** By the end of this decade Aaron is a known quantity in New York's mid-to-upper criminal ecology — not a kingpin tier, not aspiring to be, but the operator other operators hire when the job requires entry into a hard target without signature. This is the niche, and Aaron loves the niche, because it permits him to maintain the **craftsman self-presentation** that is the only stable self he has. He is paid to be excellent at a discrete thing. The discreteness is the comfort. He never has to be excellent at *being a person*.

**The Scorpion relationship**, established late in this window, is the structural precursor to the later Assessor relationship: Aaron repeatedly enters and exits the orbit of larger criminal authorities who try to handle him, and the recurring pattern — he tolerates being beaten more easily than being managed; coercers who think they own him are the figures he most reliably betrays — is rehearsed across multiple such relationships before it is documented on-panel. He builds, in this decade, the reputation for being **excellent and unreliable in the same person**, valuable enough to keep recruiting and ungovernable enough to never trust. This is also, not coincidentally, his self-summary in family.

**Affective baseline.** The decade is also when his affect-regulation strategy — the work itself as the regulator, the thrill of the job as the substitute for chemical or relational soothing — is empirically validated. He tries, in this window, to live periods of straight life. Brief jobs in legitimate sectors. Brief relationships approaching domesticity. Each collapses, not because of external exposure but because Aaron cannot regulate without the job. The straight intervals produce a dysregulation he reads as boredom and that is more accurately understood as **withdrawal from the only somatic state in which he feels coherent** — the high-vigilance, narrow-focus, problem-solving register of an active operation. He learns, in this decade, that he cannot be off. He files this as a temperamental fact rather than as the symptom it is.

---

### V. The Oscorp Job: The Emergence Event

**[Approximate age 33–34; the night documented in Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #1, circa 2011].** The narrative emergence of the Prowler as a public-record figure is the Oscorp break-in — Aaron, on contract or on speculation, penetrates an Oscorp facility from which a genetically modified spider escapes during his exit. The spider bites Miles Morales. The chain of causation that produces the next-generation Spider-Man begins, unwitnessed and uncomprehended, with Aaron's gloved hand on an Oscorp door.

The granular significance: **Aaron is the unknowing author of Miles's powers.** He does not learn this immediately. The information accumulates across the subsequent years through deduction — Miles's age, the timing of the spider's escape, the geographic coincidence — and the moment Aaron consolidates the inference is one of the rare on-record moments where his face goes still in a way the file would mark. He recognizes, in that consolidation, that he is **fated to this boy** in a way mere kinship would not have produced. The combination — nephew by blood, Spider-Man by Aaron's accident — operates on him as a kind of theological summons. He treats it as one. The decision to re-enter Miles's life, made in defiance of Jefferson's two-decade-old prohibition, is justified to himself by this fatedness: *I made him, in part, and therefore I am owed access.* The rationalization is grotesque and sincere, and it is the first appearance, in the adult Aaron, of the specific moral logic that will define every subsequent interaction with the nephew — **proprietary love, framed as duty.**

---

### VI. The First Defining Choices Post-Emergence and Their Fallout

Three choices, in close succession, define the post-emergence Aaron and set the trajectory the rest of the file documents.

**Choice 1: To approach Miles at all.** The default, given two decades of restraint from approaching Jefferson's family, would have been to absorb the Oscorp coincidence privately and continue the avoidance. He chooses approach. The choice violates the longest disciplined act of his adult life. He frames it to himself as curiosity, as family, as the natural prerogative of an uncle; the actual driver is that the attachment system, dormant for twenty years, has reactivated, and Aaron — having no relational templates other than transaction, mentorship, and leverage — cannot sit with reactivated attachment without acting on it. **Fallout:** the entire late-Ultimate arc, culminating in his death. Every subsequent disaster of his life is downstream of this single choice and he never, on-record, repents of it. He repents the *execution*; the approach itself he treats as inevitable, which is the most honest thing about him.

**Choice 2: To weaponize the knowledge of Miles's identity.** Once Aaron deduces that Miles is Spider-Man, he has two paths — protect the secret as kin-duty (Jefferson's path, the path he claims to be on) or use the secret as leverage to keep Miles in his orbit (the path he actually takes). He takes the leverage path within weeks of the deduction. The choice is, in his own framing, **conditional and minor** — just enough leverage to ensure continued contact, not enough to actually harm the boy. He believes this. He is wrong about it in a way that is constitutive of his character: he cannot tell, from inside himself, when a relational tactic has crossed into coercion, because the tactic feels, to him, like the texture of love. **Fallout:** the rapid collapse of the mentor-nephew relationship into handler-asset, Miles's growing terror, the operational catastrophes that bring Aaron into final conflict with his own equipment, and his Ultimate-continuity death.

**Choice 3 (616 only): To attempt repair.** Restored alive in the consolidated continuity and given a second pass at the arc, Aaron makes the third defining choice — the slow, halting, repeatedly-failing attempt to actually be the uncle rather than the handler. The 616 driving job, the visible labor of going straight, the willingness to disclose the past rather than hide it, the eventual willingness to be operationally unpredictable in defense of trafficked children even when self-interest dictates otherwise — these are the late-arc artifacts of choice three. **Fallout:** an ongoing, unresolved, conditionally functional relationship with both Miles and Jefferson, in which Aaron is permitted in the family frame on probation, and in which he conducts himself like a man who knows the probation is permanent and has, finally, made peace with that.

---

### VII. Summary of the Formation

The Aaron Davis the rest of this dossier tracks is fully assembled by approximately age twenty-two — a charm-equipped, vertically literate, institutionally allergic, kin-severed operator whose criminal mastery is the metabolized residue of an adolescence spent reading rooms for safety and a young adulthood spent watching his only secure attachment object walk away with cause. The decade of the lost twenties professionalizes the operator without altering the structure. The Oscorp accident, at thirty-three, supplies the addressee — Miles — onto which the dormant attachment system reactivates, and the catastrophic mismatch between reactivated attachment and the only relational vocabulary Aaron has available produces every subsequent event in the file.

He is, in the formation record, a man who was capable of love and was taught, by the single most important relationship of his early life, that love is what gets you exiled. Everything afterward is the working-out of that lesson, in the only language he learned to speak: the language of seams, of leverage, of clean entries, and of doors that he opens in buildings where he was not invited and from which, on the night that mattered most, an eight-legged accident escaped into the air shaft and bit a child who would become the only person in the world he ever managed, partially and too late, to tell the truth to.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

*Subject: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER. Period under review: from the consolidation of the Prowler identity in the mid/late twenties through the rupture-and-death sequence in the Ultimate continuity, then — under the restored 616 timeline — through the parallel middle stretch from re-emergence into Miles's life to the Assessor entanglement and the trafficking-arc inflection. This is the long load-bearing trunk of the file. Earlier years are prologue; later years (where any exist) are aftermath. Everything diagnostically interesting about Aaron Davis happens in this window.*

---

## 1. CONSOLIDATION OF THE PROWLER IDENTITY (c. mid-late 20s, Ultimate baseline)

The earliest period of the middle stretch is the one in which Aaron stops being a man who steals and becomes a man whose identity is *the Prowler*. The shift is concrete and dateable behaviorally even where it is not dated calendrically: prior to it he is a generalist — second-story work, electronics, low-impulse violence, partners-of-convenience. After it he is a specialist who has invested in tooling, branding, and a reputational signature inside the city's tier-two underworld. The acquisition of the suit and gauntlets is the demarcating event.

Observed pattern features of this consolidation:

- **Tool-fetish onset.** From this point forward Aaron is observed in the canonical record handling, cleaning, calibrating, and modifying the gauntlets in idle moments the way other men handle a phone. He talks to them under his breath when adjusting. This is craft-pride but it is also a fusion: he has externalized a portion of his self-concept into hardware. The later death-by-malfunction reads as ironic only to an outside observer; to the file it reads as predictable. He never serviced them with the rigor he demanded of jobs.
- **Niche selection.** He chooses targets that play to the suit: Oscorp, Roxxon-affiliated subcontractors, mid-tier corporate R&D, occasional jewelry/art when cash flow dips. He avoids banks (too procedurally hard, too federal), avoids residential (won't enter homes where children might be present — an early indicator of the line that hardens in 616), avoids contracts that require killing as deliverable. He will kill incidentally; he will not kill on commission. This is not ethics in the philosophical sense — it is the working-craftsman's refusal to take jobs outside his frame.
- **Reputational management.** He cultivates an underworld persona that is deliberately undersized relative to his actual capability. He lets larger names (Scorpion, the Maximus-class operators) think of him as a step below them. This is partly survival (don't attract Kingpin-tier attention) and partly the same dismissing-avoidant signature that runs through the rest of his life: do not be fully seen by anyone whose seeing has consequences.

The consolidation period also establishes his **routes** — the literal geography of his existence. Brooklyn base; safehouse rotations across at least three boroughs; a preferred rooftop transit pattern between Red Hook, Sunset Park, and the Brooklyn waterfront that he keeps even after it becomes operationally suboptimal because it is *his*. A total-surveillance file would have the rooftop sequence mapped to the meter. He walks the same stairs at the same buildings; he eats at the same two or three counter-service places between jobs; he uses the same locksmith for cover-identity keys. For a man whose tradecraft demands variation, his off-duty life is monotonously habitual. The vigilance is operational; the comfort-seeking is fixed.

## 2. THE SCORPION ENTANGLEMENT AND THE OSCORP BREAK-IN

The middle period's first major external arc is the conflict with Maximus Gargan's organization. Aaron's relationship to Scorpion is the template for every adversarial-yet-instrumental relationship he will ever have: he resents the man, he is contemptuous of his sloppiness, he works around him, he occasionally works *for* him under duress, and he is willing to burn him the moment a better play opens. The contempt is the diagnostic signal — Aaron's most reliable affective tell with any peer-criminal is the small curl of professional disdain he cannot suppress when watching a job done badly. He performs camaraderie in the room and exhales judgment in the car after.

The Oscorp break-in is the hinge event of the entire Ultimate stretch. Aaron is hired/self-hires (the record is ambiguous; both readings appear) to extract Osborn-lab biotech. During the extraction, an Oscorp genetically modified spider escapes — the specimen that subsequently bites Miles Morales. Aaron does not know this at the time. The job otherwise reads as a clean technical success: in-and-out, no Oscorp casualties traceable to him, payload delivered.

What matters about the break-in for the file is not the heist itself but the *belated cognitive reconstruction* Aaron performs months later when he learns Miles is Spider-Man. He back-solves the chain — Oscorp spider, his own break-in, his sister-in-law's apartment, his nephew. He is the man who unwittingly armed his own nephew. He never tells Miles this in the Ultimate continuity; he holds it as private knowledge and lets it function as both a permission slip (the powers are *his* gift, transitively, therefore his right of access) and a private guilt he will not name. The diagnostic content is that he metabolizes the coincidence into entitlement rather than into apology. This is the foundational distortion of the entire uncle-nephew arc.

## 3. RE-ENTRY INTO THE FAMILY: THE COURTSHIP OF MILES (Ultimate)

The re-entry sequence is patient, well-staged, and — by Aaron's standards — gentle. He does not crash into Miles's life; he *positions* himself at its edges and waits to be invited closer. Observable subroutines:

- **The first contact protocol.** Aaron makes himself findable rather than findable-by-force. He surfaces in places Miles will naturally encounter him — a turn-up at Jefferson's building lobby, a casual collision near Miles's school, a "passing through the neighborhood" pretext. He lets Miles do the work of bridging. This is the same approach a skilled handler uses on a recruit: never appear to need the relationship; let the target volunteer toward it.
- **The gift economy.** Once contact is established, Aaron operates almost exclusively through material and experiential gifts — the sneakers Jefferson won't buy, the meal at the place Jefferson can't afford, the unsupervised hours Jefferson won't sanction. He understands intuitively that he cannot compete with Jefferson on stability, so he competes on the axis Jefferson refuses to play on: indulgence. This is not crude; it is calibrated. He gives just enough to be the more exciting figure, never so much that he becomes a suspicious one.
- **Self-narration.** Aaron tells Miles about himself in carefully edited installments. He volunteers the existence of "the brother thing" with Jefferson without specifying the precipitating event. He hints at a wilder past without naming the work. This is courtship-by-managed-disclosure, and it is sophisticated; Miles, a teenager hungry for the figure Jefferson has hidden, receives every installment as intimacy rather than as the curated intelligence drop it actually is.
- **The reading of Miles.** Across this period Aaron is watching Miles the way he watches a job site. He clocks Miles's tells — the way the boy fidgets when about to lie, the way he widens his eyes when impressed, the conversational topics that brighten him. Aaron is building a profile. He would not call it that. He believes he is *paying attention to family*. Both readings are true. The pattern is identical to the one he would run on a target; the affect inside it is real.

The courtship phase produces the period's most stable version of Aaron — relaxed, witty, generative, the version of him that, if isolated and extended, would have constituted a life. It does not extend. It cannot, because Aaron's working assumption is that closeness must be *underwritten* by leverage or it will evaporate the way Jefferson did. He cannot let the relationship stand on its own weight. As soon as it is real, he begins instrumentalizing it.

## 4. THE INSTRUMENTALIZATION TURN (Ultimate)

The pivot from uncle-courtship to nephew-as-asset is not a single moment; it is a gradient that completes over several encounters. The mechanism:

1. **Discovery.** Aaron identifies Miles as Spider-Man (the canon shows him assembling the clues with the same care he brings to a job). He sits on the knowledge before acting on it. The interval between knowing and using is the longest interval of self-restraint in his observed life. He spends it, on the evidence of his behavior, trying to talk himself out of the use.
2. **Soft proposal.** First deployment is framed as mentorship — "let me show you how this kind of work is actually done." He offers Miles the seduction of *being good at it*, which is the seduction Aaron himself never resisted. He brings Miles in on a Scorpion-adjacent operation under the cover of street justice. Miles is permitted to feel useful. Aaron is permitted to feel he has not coerced anyone yet.
3. **Escalation.** When Miles begins to pull back, Aaron names the implicit threat: I can tell your father. He does not enjoy the moment; the canonical depiction shows a man who has chosen the move because no other move was visible to him. This is the most psychologically revealing beat of the entire Ultimate arc — *Aaron coerces Miles not because he is willing to lose the relationship to gain the asset but because he believes the threat is the only thing that will preserve the relationship*. The logic is bent but it is sincere. He extorts the boy out of attachment panic.
4. **Repetition.** Once leverage is on the table it cannot leave. Subsequent jobs proceed under its shadow. Miles complies with diminishing tolerance; Aaron escalates demands with diminishing self-respect. Both of them know what is happening; neither names it; the relationship rots in real time.

The behavioral micro-pattern across this phase is worth filing in detail. Aaron, in the instrumentalization period, develops a new tell: he stops making eye contact with Miles during transitions between social-uncle mode and operational-handler mode. He looks at his gauntlets, at the room, at his exit. The eye-contact avoidance is the somatic marker of the splitting defense. He cannot hold the two representations of Miles in the same visual field, so he routes around it. A surveillance file with footage would catch this on every coercive sequence.

## 5. THE COLLAPSE: GAUNTLET DEATH (Ultimate)

The terminal Ultimate sequence is the gauntlets malfunctioning during a confrontation in which Aaron has fully crossed — has, in effect, treated Miles as an adversary rather than as kin. The cause-of-death is technical: equipment failure under combat load. The cause-of-death is psychological: Aaron stopped maintaining the equipment in the period during which he was failing to maintain the relationship. The two neglects are the same neglect. A man who is poisoning his attachment system does not service his tools either; he is in a degraded-maintenance regime across his whole life. The death reads to the outside as accident and to the file as systems failure.

Two behavioral notes from the terminal sequence:

- **No begging.** Aaron, on the evidence, does not plead. He absorbs the failure with the same flat operational affect he would bring to any blown job. The pride is the last thing to die. Whether this is dignity or dissociation is a judgment call; both are defensible.
- **No reconciliation attempt mid-collapse.** He does not, in the available seconds, retract the coercion or offer Miles an apology. This is the deepest indictment of the Ultimate-arc Aaron and the cleanest proof that the file's reading is correct: he could not metabolize the repair conversation even when it was the only meaningful action left to him. The dismissing-avoidant defense held through to the end.

The Ultimate file closes here. Everything after is the parallel timeline.

---

## 6. THE 616 PARALLEL MIDDLE: RESURRECTION INTO A REFORM ARC

The restored 616 Aaron enters the middle period from a different starting position: alive, with the gauntlet-death edited out of his direct experience but retained, by the file's reading, as a *structural* warning — the universe gave him the second chance the Ultimate arc denied him, and the behavioral record shows a man who has, at some level, registered the reprieve.

The 616 middle stretch reorganizes around an attempted exit from the criminal frame. Key arc components:

### 6a. The Going-Straight Project

Aaron's straight-life attempt is the rideshare driver phase. The choice of work is itself diagnostic. He selects an occupation that:

- Requires no fixed coworkers (preserves the low-disclosure default).
- Permits the same nocturnal/irregular schedule as the criminal life (no circadian retooling required).
- Keeps him *in the car, moving, scanning* — the somatic posture of the thief, repurposed.
- Lets him meet strangers in transactional five-to-twenty-minute frames he can fully control.

It is the maximally Aaron-compatible legitimate job. He could have chosen worse and did not; he could have chosen better (and would have failed at it). The rideshare phase is the longest sustained legal-employment stretch in his observed adult life and the clearest evidence that the reform impulse has structural reality, not just rhetorical reality. He is rearranging his days around it.

He is also, on the evidence, **bad at making money this way**. The financial precarity of the rideshare period is the recurring lever that the criminal pulls use against him. Every relapse in the 616 stretch has a rent-shaped or hospital-bill-shaped pretext attached. The reform is sincere; the economics of the reform are unworkable; this is the actual structure of most attempted-exit cases in the criminological literature and Aaron is a faithful instance of it.

### 6b. The Re-Stabilized Uncle Relationship

The 616 Miles relationship is the corrected version of the Ultimate one. The differences are precise:

- **No coercion threshold reached.** Aaron, in the 616 stretch, *does* know Miles's identity (or learns it) and *does not* convert the knowledge into leverage. The single most diagnostically important behavioral fact about 616 Aaron is the negative one: the move he made in the Ultimate timeline, he declines to make here. He has internalized the lesson the Ultimate version never lived long enough to learn.
- **Eye contact restored.** The Ultimate-period avoidance tell is gone. He looks at Miles when they talk. This is the somatic confirmation that the splitting defense has, in this continuity, partially closed; he can hold the boy as kin and as super-powered operative in the same frame without flinching.
- **Disclosure increases.** Aaron volunteers more about his own past, including pieces unflattering to him. The managed-installments pattern of the Ultimate courtship is partly replaced with something closer to actual disclosure. He still edits, but the editing margin has narrowed.
- **Jefferson, still unaddressed.** The one repair he does not attempt is the one he most needs. He talks *around* Jefferson with Miles; he does not seek out Jefferson directly to perform the conversation his entire adult life has been a substitute for. The brother-wound remains the unhealed center even in the rehabilitative timeline. The file expects this; the dismissing-avoidant structure is robust precisely against the conversations that would dissolve it.

### 6c. The Assessor Entanglement

The defining external arc of the 616 middle is the Assessor's coercion of Aaron into a return to operational work — and into adjacency to trafficking and child-endangerment material that violates Aaron's working lines. The arc functions as the stress test of the reform.

Behavioral pattern under the Assessor pressure:

- **Initial compliance, low-affect.** Aaron returns to work the way a recovering addict takes the first drink — with the studied casualness of a man pretending the resumption is provisional. He tells himself it is a one-job exit. It is not. It is never one job. He knows this; he proceeds anyway.
- **Line-crossing recognition.** When the Assessor's operation reveals its trafficking-adjacent character, Aaron's affect floor drops out in the precise way the file predicts. He is operationally unpredictable; he begins to sabotage from within. The hard line on children and non-combatants — first visible in the early-career target-selection patterns — fires on schedule. He cannot continue in a frame that crosses it.
- **The betrayal turn.** Aaron, under handling, will always eventually betray the handler. This is the most reliable single prediction the file can make about him. He tolerates being beaten; he cannot tolerate being *owned*; the Assessor's coercion script triggers the betrayal-of-handler subroutine that previously triggered against Scorpion-tier operators. He flips. He helps Miles dismantle the operation. He pays a price for it.
- **Collapse-and-confess endpoint.** Where the Ultimate Aaron died without apology, the 616 Aaron arrives at the verbal confession the earlier version was structurally incapable of. The confession is partial, hedged, and emotionally costly to him; it is also real. The reform arc gets the conversation the gauntlet death foreclosed.

### 6d. The Quieter Sub-Arcs

Between major events, the 616 middle is populated with the granular accretion of an attempted-ordinary life:

- The standing rotation of food spots (still the same two-or-three pattern, geographically shifted).
- A semi-regular gym he uses inconsistently — he trains hard for two weeks after every operational incident and then lapses for months. The training pattern is reactive, not maintained.
- A pattern of small purchases for Miles that he no longer frames as gifts — the rebranding from "uncle who buys you things" to "uncle who picked something up because he was thinking of you" is a meaningful evolution. The transactional underbody is still there; the framing has matured.
- Sleep, by the somatic markers visible across the run, remains poor. He has not yet learned to live in a domestic space without scanning it.
- Continued non-engagement with mental-health resources. He has no language for what is wrong with him and would refuse the language if offered.

---

## 7. CROSS-CONTINUITY PATTERN EVOLUTION ACROSS THE MIDDLE PERIOD

Across the full middle stretch — both continuities read as a single longitudinal record of the same man under two stress conditions — the trackable evolutions are:

- **From craft-pride as identity-substitute to craft-pride as one identity among others.** Early middle: he *is* the Prowler. Late middle (616): he is a man who *was* the Prowler and is something else now, imperfectly. The fusion with the gear has loosened. Diagnostically: the equipment-as-self defense has begun to dismantle.
- **From leverage-as-affection to disclosure-as-affection, partial.** The Ultimate-period reflex to extort intimacy has been replaced, incompletely, by an attempt to *earn* it. The reflex is still there; it is no longer first-resort.
- **From handler-betrayal as ad hoc to handler-betrayal as identity.** Aaron's willingness to burn the people who try to own him has, across the middle period, hardened into a near-principle. It is the closest thing to ethics he has built. It is also the most useful single fact for predicting his behavior under any future coercion.
- **From Miles as proxy-for-Jefferson to Miles as Miles.** The Ultimate-period substitution — loving the nephew in lieu of being reconciled with the brother — has, in the 616 stretch, partially disaggregated. Aaron has begun to perceive Miles as a separate person with his own trajectory rather than as the bridge back to the lost sibling. The Jefferson-wound is not closed; it is no longer routed entirely through the boy.
- **From foreshortened time-horizon to tentative future-orientation.** Early middle: he plans jobs, not weeks. Late middle (616): he begins, occasionally, to plan months. The rideshare schedule, the gym lapses, the casual references to "next time we" with Miles — these are the first observable instances of an Aaron Davis who treats his own continuance as something other than a problem to be deferred.

The middle period, in sum, is the record of a man who in one timeline ran his pattern to its terminal failure and in the other has been granted the post-failure stretch and is using it, with imperfect but legible competence, to dismantle the pattern from inside. The diagnostic question the file carries into the late period is not whether the dismantling will complete — it will not, characterological structure of this depth does not fully resolve — but whether it will hold under the next coercion that finds him. The middle-period evidence is cautiously favorable. The attachment system is online. The handler-betrayal reflex is intact. The line on children has hardened. The brother conversation remains unhad.

He is, at the end of the middle period, the most functional version of himself the record has ever shown — and still, by any honest reading, one provocation away from the gauntlets.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# CHRONOLOGY IV — RECENT HISTORY & CURRENT STATE

*File segment covering the post-resurrection 616 window through present-day operational status. Continuity anchors: the Ahmed-era* Miles Morales: Spider-Man *run, the Assessor arc, the Clone Saga (Ultimatum), the Beyond Corp. peripheral exposure, the Carnage-adjacent New York incidents, and the Brooklyn neighborhood-level civilian record. All timestamps are diegetic-recent.*

---

## 1. THE THRESHOLD EVENT: RETURN FROM ERASURE

The recent era begins, structurally, with a resurrection the subject himself does not narrate and does not appear to fully understand. In the consolidated 616 continuity Aaron Davis is **alive** in a body that, by Ultimate-era record, should have been killed by his own malfunctioning equipment. He does not discuss this discrepancy. He behaves, in surveillance terms, as a man who has been given an unearned second pass and has decided — without articulating the decision — to spend it differently.

The behavioral signature of that decision is visible from his earliest 616 appearances: he is **living openly**, under his legal name, at a fixed address Miles can find without tradecraft. For a career thief whose entire prior operational doctrine was rooted in non-fixity, this is a categorical reversal. He has chosen to be locatable. He has chosen to be reachable by his nephew at the cost of being reachable by everyone else who has ever had reason to look for him. That single architectural choice — **fixed address, listed phone, known schedule** — is the through-line of the entire recent chronology and the load-bearing evidence that the reform is not cosmetic.

---

## 2. RESIDENCE, ROUTE, AND DAILY PATTERN

**Residence.** A modest Brooklyn apartment, walk-up tier, in a building old enough to have radiator heat and new enough to have a key-fob entry he has clearly disabled and re-rigged with a mechanical override of his own fabrication (consistent with his trade reflex: he cannot live inside a security system he did not personally vet). The apartment is sparsely furnished in the manner of a man who has spent his adult life ready to leave a space within ninety seconds. There is a couch, a television, a kitchen table with two chairs (the second chair is the diagnostic detail — it is for Miles), a workbench area screened off in the back where tools and gear are kept under a tarp rather than locked away, because lock-and-key signals presence-of-value to anyone who breaks in, whereas a tarp signals nothing. He sleeps in the bedroom with the door open and the window cracked in any weather.

**Vehicle.** A used sedan, late-model but unremarkable, kept clean inside, registered correctly, insured. This is the vehicle of record for his rideshare work. There is, by inference, a second vehicle or vehicle-access he does not declare — a man with his skill base does not commit to a single registered car — but it is held off-book and used rarely.

**Daily route.** Wakes early. Coffee at home, never a chain (chains have cameras and loyalty-tracking; he avoids both reflexively even now). A short walk for a paper or a roll, the same two or three blocks rotated rather than the same block daily — a hard-trained anti-pattern habit he cannot extinguish even when the threat model no longer requires it. Rideshare shifts run mid-morning through afternoon, broken by a gym visit or a long walk three or four times a week. Evenings are unstructured: television, calls with Miles when Miles calls, occasional dinner out at one of perhaps four restaurants he uses on rotation. He is in bed by midnight on working days. He is, by the standards of his prior life, **boring on purpose**, and the boredom is a discipline.

---

## 3. OCCUPATIONAL STATUS: THE DRIVER

Aaron's primary legitimate income in the current period is **app-based rideshare driving**. The choice is psychologically over-determined and worth unpacking.

Rideshare work gives him: (a) a defensible answer to "what do you do," which he has needed for the first time in his adult life; (b) continuous low-stakes motion through the city, which is the regulatory rhythm his nervous system was built on — he cannot sit still and a desk job would destroy him within a fiscal quarter; (c) constant short, bounded interactions with strangers in which his charm is an asset and his low-disclosure default is the industry norm; (d) plausible cash flow that does not require explanation; and (e) the daily exercise of his most refined cognitive faculty — **reading the city, reading the rider, reading the street** — in a context where the reading is no longer in service of a job.

He is, by every available indicator, **good at it**. His rider ratings are high. He gets repeat regulars. He keeps water and a phone charger in the back seat. He does not play music unless the rider asks. These are not the behaviors of a man performing legitimacy; they are the behaviors of a craftsman who has transferred his craft pride to a new medium because pride in execution is the only self-soothing strategy he has ever had.

It is also — and this is the part of the file that requires honesty — **operationally porous**. Rideshare work places him in unmonitored vehicular proximity to thousands of strangers, gives him pretextual access to any address in the city, and provides a movement log that any competent counter-party can subpoena or steal. He knows this. He has used it. The Assessor arc demonstrates that his app-driver cover was the exact vector through which he was leveraged back into criminal work — the trafficked persons were moved, in part, through his car. The legitimate occupation and the residual exposure are the same channel. This is the structural problem of his reform: the skills that make the new life livable are the skills that make him recruitable.

---

## 4. THE ASSESSOR EPISODE AND ITS AFTERMATH

The single most diagnostic event of the recent period is his entrapment by the figure operating as the Assessor.

**Mechanism of capture.** The Assessor's leverage on Aaron was not violence and not money — it was **information**, specifically the threat of exposure of his criminal past to Miles and to Jefferson in a manner that would unmake the family reconciliation he had built over the post-resurrection window. Aaron, who has spent his entire life weaponizing leverage against others, was for the first time on-record fully **handled** by it. He cooperated. He drove. He looked away. He participated, by complicit transport, in the movement of trafficked persons through New York.

**Behavioral signature during compliance.** Surveillance-grade observation of his demeanor across this period would record: weight loss, sleep degradation, increased frequency of the small grooming tics (the brushing of the line of the beard with a thumb, the rubbing of the bridge of the nose) he uses when affect-suppression is failing, **avoidance of Miles** for the longest stretch since their reconciliation, and a measurable contraction of his rideshare radius — he stopped taking fares into Manhattan, which is the side of the city the Assessor's traffic moved through. He was, in the clinical idiom, **freezing**: the third F, after fight and flight, the one his profile predicts under coercion that targets his shame structure rather than his body.

**Rupture and self-disclosure.** The episode terminates not because Aaron escapes the leverage but because he **breaks the leverage himself** by confessing to Miles. This is the single most important behavioral data point of the entire 616 era. It is the exact inverse of the Ultimate-era pattern, in which leverage on him became leverage by him on Miles. Under analogous pressure in two continuities, the Ultimate Aaron coerced the nephew; the 616 Aaron incriminated himself to the nephew to disarm the coercer. The cost was high — Miles's trust took a measurable hit, Jefferson's tolerance contracted further — but the pattern was broken. He chose exposure over instrumentalization. The file should mark this as the **inflection point of demonstrated characterological change**, not merely behavioral change.

**Aftermath, somatic.** In the weeks following the disclosure he visibly carries the body posture of someone whose load has dropped — shoulders lower, head higher, the constant scan slightly relaxed. He sleeps better. He eats normal meals. He gains back the weight he lost during the compliance period. The shame did not destroy him; the disclosure metabolized it. This is consistent with the formulation that his pathology is not constitutional but dynamic — relieve the dynamic pressure and the function recovers.

**Aftermath, relational.** Miles does not cut him off, but the relationship runs at a lower temperature for an interval.
