Aaron does this both vocationally (case the building, walk the route) and relationally (he has answers prepared for questions Miles has not asked yet; he knows what he will say to Jefferson if he ever sees him again, though he will never volunteer the conversation).

*Behavioral tells:* Arrives to all meetings early. Sits with sightlines to all exits — the seat selection is automatic and unremarked. When asked an unexpected personal question, there is a micro-pause of half a second; this is not searching for the answer, it is searching the *list* of prepared answers for the one that fits.

*Failure mode:* Over-anticipation crowds out spontaneity. With Miles, the prepared-answer reflex is detectable to a perceptive teenager, and reads as performance rather than presence.

#### 7.2.4 Suppression (partial)

He can consciously set aside affect to complete a task. This is genuine suppression, not repression — he knows what he is putting down and intends to pick it back up later, though he frequently does not. After the Ultimate-arc death of his criminal contacts or the 616-era confrontations with the Assessor, he displays the operational calm of a man who has *parked* his feelings rather than escaped them.

*Failure mode:* The parked material accumulates. Suppression that is never followed by processing becomes, over years, a low-grade reservoir of unmetabolized affect that leaks at unrelated moments — typically when something domestic and minor (a meal with Miles, a passing radio song) cracks the lid.

---

### 7.3 Neurotic Defenses

#### 7.3.1 Rationalization

The most frequently deployed defense in his entire repertoire. Every coercive move against Miles in the Ultimate arc is preceded or followed by a rationalization: *I'm teaching him real-world skills. Better he learns from me than the street. His father coddles him. He needs to know what he's capable of.* These are not lies — Aaron half-believes them in the moment of utterance — but their function is to make exploitation feel like pedagogy.

*Behavioral tells:* The rationalizations come in three- or four-clause stacks rather than single statements. The voice loses its usual economy and becomes wordier. He repeats the same justification with minor variations across an encounter, as though the repetition will install belief in the listener and, secondarily, in himself.

*Failure mode:* Miles, by the late Ultimate arc and throughout 616, becomes immune. Once the rationalizations stop landing on their primary audience, Aaron is forced to direct them entirely inward, where they degrade into self-disgust rather than self-justification — one of the precipitants of the 616 reform attempt.

#### 7.3.2 Intellectualization

Closely paired with rationalization but distinct. Where rationalization manufactures *reasons*, intellectualization manufactures *frames* — Aaron talks about crime as economics, family as systems, betrayal as game theory. It is the move he makes when an emotional question has been put to him and he needs to answer without entering the emotion. Conversations about Jefferson, when forced, are conducted at this altitude: he will speak of "what my brother believed" or "the choice he made" as if delivering an after-action report on a third party.

*Failure mode:* Audible flattening of vocal affect. Miles, who is increasingly emotionally literate across his published arc, learns to recognize the register and to press through it.

#### 7.3.3 Reaction Formation

Operational primarily in the 616 reform arc. The gentleness, patience, and self-deprecation he displays as the reformed uncle are pitched at an intensity that exceeds what mere reform would produce; they are **counter-formations** against the live, ongoing pull of the part of him that still wants to use Miles. The give-away is the *emphasis*: a man who has genuinely integrated his criminal impulses does not need to be quite that consistently kind. The kindness is real, but it is also a barricade.

*Behavioral tells:* In the Ahmed run he over-apologizes for small things. He volunteers favors he was not asked for. He brings food. The behavior is correct but slightly amplified — a tell that the suppressed impulse is still alive and being actively counter-pressed.

*Failure mode:* When the Assessor's coercion overwhelms him, the reaction-formation collapses and the underlying impulse reappears uncamouflaged. This is the diagnostic value of those sequences — they show what is being defended *against*.

#### 7.3.4 Displacement

Aaron displaces aggression from its true targets — Jefferson, the dead younger self who chose the wrong road, the version of himself that took Miles on jobs — onto operationally legitimate targets: rival criminals (the Scorpion), institutional figures, equipment he then mishandles. The Scorpion confrontations carry more heat than the strategic situation warrants; he is fighting the wrong man with the right fury.

*Behavioral tells:* Disproportion. The intensity of his response to a relatively minor provocation, when it exceeds tactical sense, is a displacement marker. Watch for the moment in any fight where his economy of motion breaks and the strikes become heavier than necessary — that is the displaced target arriving.

#### 7.3.5 Isolation of Affect

The capacity to recall and recount disturbing material — the foundational robbery with Jefferson, the moment of estrangement, his own near-deaths — without the affect that should attend it. He can describe the rupture event in a flat, almost procedural voice. This is not because he does not feel it; it is because the feeling has been surgically separated from the memory and stored elsewhere, to be felt at less inconvenient moments (often somatically, as the chronic vigilance described in §2).

*Failure mode:* Isolation is fragile. A specific sensory cue — Jefferson's voice on a phone, a particular street block, a photograph — can rejoin the affect to the content abruptly, producing the rare on-panel Aaron tears.

#### 7.3.6 Undoing

In the 616 arc particularly, Aaron performs small acts of repair that are symbolically inverse to past offenses: he protects a trafficked youth (inverse of having instrumentalized his own nephew), he refuses a job he would once have taken, he tells Miles a small truth where he would once have told a strategic lie. These are *undoing* operations — the unconscious belief that the present act can retroactively cancel the past act. They are not cynical, but they are not, by themselves, sufficient for the integration the arc gestures toward.

---

### 7.4 Immature Defenses

#### 7.4.1 Splitting (interpersonally restricted)

The most operationally consequential of his immature defenses. Aaron splits Miles between two non-integrating representations — **kin-equal** (beloved nephew, blood, the only family that took him back) and **asset** (powered operator, leverage object, useful muscle). He cannot hold both representations in the same moment; he flips between them, often within a single conversation, with the toggle determined by his own anxiety rather than by anything Miles is doing.

The restriction is diagnostically important: Aaron does not split *generally*. His representations of Jefferson, the Scorpion, the Assessor, ordinary marks are stable and nuanced. The splitting is **Miles-specific** because Miles is the only object on which the full attachment system is mounted, and the attachment system is precisely where his integration failed.

*Behavioral tells:* Sudden register shifts mid-encounter — warmth giving way to instruction giving way to leverage, with no transition phase. The eyes briefly recalibrate during the toggle; observable as a half-second focal shift.

#### 7.4.2 Passive Aggression

Sparingly used and almost exclusively against Jefferson (in absentia, since they barely interact) and against authority figures he cannot openly defy. Manifests as missed appointments, ironic compliance, and the strategic forgetting of obligations.

#### 7.4.3 Acting Out

The criminal career, considered as a whole, has an acting-out dimension distinct from the sublimation dimension. The sublimation accounts for the *craft*; the acting-out accounts for the *recurrence*. He returns to jobs not merely because he is skilled at them but because the action discharges affect he has no other route to process. The 616 relapses under the Assessor are pure acting-out: the work is bad, the risk is poorly calibrated, the satisfaction is in the doing rather than the having-done.

*Behavioral tells:* Relapses are preceded by increased physical restlessness, sleep disruption, and a particular pattern of late-night driving routes that traverse old job sites without stopping. He is *casing himself* back into the work.

#### 7.4.4 Identification with the Aggressor

Foundational. The violence of his upbringing was absorbed and re-presented as professionalized competence rather than metabolized as victim-identity. He learned, very young, that the people who survived the environment were the ones who acted on it rather than the ones acted upon. The defense is adaptive in survival terms — it produced a man who functions — and pathological in relational terms, because the introjected aggressor speaks whenever closeness threatens.

The aggressor he identified with is not a single person but the *posture* of the predator: scanning, reading for leverage, exploiting seams. He carries this posture into rooms where it is not needed, including kitchens with his nephew. He cannot fully demobilize it. The 616 reform arc is, at the depth level, an attempt to *thank* the introject for survival service and ask it to stand down — a renegotiation rarely completed in life.

---

### 7.5 Primitive Defenses

#### 7.5.1 Denial (narrow band)

Aaron does not deny reality broadly; his reality-testing is excellent. He denies *significance*. Asked whether his coercion of Miles in the Ultimate arc constituted abuse, he would, in the moment, have said no — not because he believed Miles was unharmed, but because admitting the significance of the harm would require an internal reorganization he could not afford while still mid-action. The denial collapses once the action is over, which is why his post-arc affect — and the post-mortem 616 reckoning — carries the freight it does.

#### 7.5.2 Projective Identification (rare, Miles-specific)

In coercive sequences he attributes to Miles motives Miles does not have — *you want this, you want to be powerful, you want what I can teach you* — and then behaves toward Miles as if the attributed motives were real, sometimes successfully inducing fragments of them in the nephew. This is the most damaging operation he performs and the one for which the 616 reform arc most clearly tries to make amends.

#### 7.5.3 Pre-emptive Relational Sabotage

Not a classical defense but functions as one: when a relationship reaches a closeness threshold that activates the unmetabolized Jefferson rupture, Aaron breaks the relationship *first*, on terms he controls, to avoid being broken from. The Ultimate-arc coercion of Miles can be read partially through this lens — he was destroying the relationship before it could destroy him by going the way of Jefferson's. The defense succeeded operationally and catastrophically in the same motion.

---

### 7.6 Positive Compensatory Mechanisms

These are the adaptations that, even within a criminal life, function as net assets — to him, to those near him, and to the rare cases where he is mobilized in a prosocial direction.

- **Craft pride as identity scaffold.** The thief-as-artist self-concept gives him a stable internal reference point that does not require external validation to maintain. It is the reason he does not collapse into formless drift when straight options fail. A man with an identity, even an antisocial one, has something to renovate; a man without one has nothing to start from. The 616 reform is possible only because the craft-identity provides a platform on which a revised identity can be built.
- **Humor as social lubricant and self-regulator.** The same mature defense described above functions compensatorily as a generator of brief social warmth in environments otherwise structured by suspicion.
- **The capacity to mentor.** Real and transmissible, even when self-interestedly deployed. Aaron is genuinely good at teaching what he knows — combat economics, situational reading, the patience of the long approach. Miles, across both continuities, retains usable skills from this teaching. The mechanism is compensatory because it converts Aaron's accumulated criminal knowledge into something the next generation can deploy non-criminally; the knowledge outlives the application.
- **Refusal of self-pity.** He does not narrate himself as victim, even when the narration would be partly accurate. The refusal preserves agency and prevents the slide into the kind of grievance-organized identity that produces the most dangerous offenders.
- **Hard floor on non-combatants and the trafficked.** Especially crystallized in the 616 arc. This is compensatory because it provides him a non-negotiable moral reference point — a place where his behavior is not for sale — and the existence of even one such point is what distinguishes the rehabilitable offender from the irrecoverable one.
- **Loyalty discipline.** Once given, his loyalty is unusually durable. The same defensive narrowing of attachment that pathologically concentrates his affective life on Miles also makes the attachment, where it lands, extraordinarily resistant to ordinary corrosion. Loyalty is a finite resource in him, but the unit-quality is high.
- **Operational competence as crisis-utility.** In emergencies — kidnappings, structural collapses, citywide threats during crossovers — the same skills that serve burglary serve rescue. He is, when motivated, one of the most useful non-powered operators in Miles's circle.

---

### 7.7 Negative Compensatory Mechanisms

These are the maladaptive substitutions — the places where a missing capacity has been replaced by something that approximates its function while accruing damage.

- **Instrumentalization of intimacy.** The substitute for connection-through-disclosure is connection-through-utility. Aaron knows how to be useful to people and how to make them useful to him; he does not know how to be *with* them in a register that does not involve exchange. The compensation works (he is rarely lonely in the operational sense) and fails (he is constantly lonely in the relational sense).
- **Coercion-as-affection.** When the relational pull exceeds his disclosure tolerance, he reaches for control. Leverage substitutes for vulnerability. The mechanism is catastrophic in the Ultimate arc and visibly residual in 616.
- **Gift-giving as proxy for verbal intimacy.** He buys Miles things. The gifts are real, generous, and chosen with care — but they are also substitutions for the verbal contact he cannot perform. The compensation gives him a way to express love; it also trains the recipient to read love through transaction.
- **Avoidance of repair conversations with Jefferson.** The defense substitute for the actual reconciliation — which would require disclosure he cannot tolerate — is a permanent posture of *almost reaching out*. He has, in both continuities, the brother's contact information, knows the brother's location, and never makes the call. The avoidance is compensatory because it manages the affect (he does not have to feel rejection if he does not extend the hand) and pathological because Jefferson is, as observed in §5, the actual addressee of his entire adult life.
- **The Prowler suit as exoskeletal self.** He compensates for an under-armored interior with an over-armored exterior. The gear holds him together. It also, in the Ultimate arc, killed him — the compensation became the cause. The relationship to the suit is the relationship to all his compensations writ small: they keep him functional and they keep him from the work that would render them unnecessary.
- **Job-as-mood-regulator.** In the absence of chemical self-medication, the *work itself* is the regulator (see §2). The compensation prevents one disorder (substance dependence) by sustaining another (compulsive offending). It is the cleanest possible illustration of the symptom-substitution principle.
- **Sarcasm-as-discharge.** When humor brittles, sarcasm provides a low-cost discharge of aggression that does not require the operational risk of confrontation. It compensates for the absence of safe outlets for anger; it corrodes the relationships it is used within.
- **Hypervigilance as security substitute.** He has no secure base, so he manufactures security through perimeter scanning. The compensation works in the field and fails in the bedroom — it is the reason his sleep is light and his rooms are read on entry. The cortisol load is the long-term price.

---

### 7.8 Hierarchy at a Glance

Ranked from most primitive to most mature, with operational frequency in Aaron's behavior noted in brackets [low / moderate / high]:

1. **Projective identification** [low — Miles-specific]
2. **Denial of significance** [moderate]
3. **Pre-emptive relational sabotage** [moderate — attachment-triggered]
4. **Splitting** [high — Miles-specific only]
5. **Acting out** [high]
6. **Identification with the aggressor** [structural — always on, rarely surface]
7. **Passive aggression** [low]
8. **Displacement** [moderate]
9. **Isolation of affect** [high]
10. **Undoing** [moderate — predominantly 616]
11. **Reaction formation** [high — predominantly 616]
12. **Intellectualization** [moderate]
13. **Rationalization** [high — across both continuities]
14. **Suppression** [high]
15. **Anticipation** [high — constitutive]
16. **Humor** [high — constitutive]
17. **Sublimation** [high — constitutive]

The shape of the distribution is the shape of the man. The mature defenses are constitutive — they are who he is on a normal Tuesday. The neurotic defenses are frequent and used to manage the ordinary frictions of a double life. The immature defenses cluster around a single relational object (Miles) and reactivate under attachment load. The primitive defenses are rare, narrow, and surgically targeted at the places where his developmental arc snapped.

---

### 7.9 Diagnostic Use

For any observer or analyst working a live encounter with the subject, the defenses index the affective temperature of the room more reliably than his face does. The face is trained; the defense ladder is not. Read in this order:

- **If he is sublimating (talking craft, hand-tracing routes):** baseline. Safe to engage.
- **If he is using humor to close topics:** mild stress. He is managing distance.
- **If he is rationalizing in three-clause stacks:** moderate stress. He is justifying something to himself, which means he is about to do it.
- **If he is intellectualizing about family:** Jefferson has been activated. Do not press.
- **If the register to


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: AARON DAVIS

*Decade-by-decade clinical synthesis. Frameworks drawn from attachment theory (Bowlby, Main, Fonagy), object-relations (Kernberg, Fairbairn), Linehan's affect-regulation taxonomy, Beck/Young schema work, McWilliams's character diagnosis, and the developmental-trauma literature (van der Kolk, Herman). Behavioral citations from the published record indicated by arc.*

---

## DECADE ONE: CHILDHOOD (approx. ages 0–10)

### Affect regulation

The earliest stratum is reconstructive — Aaron is never depicted as a small child on-panel — but the somatic and relational signature of the adult is unambiguous about what the child must have organized around. The adult Aaron's baseline state is **alert quiet**: he enters rooms scanning, he sleeps thinly, he eats fast, he laughs on a delay of perhaps a half-second after the joke lands, as if checking the room before committing affect. This is not a learned professional skill; professional skills are bolted onto a substrate, and the substrate here is the **hyperaroused-but-controlled** profile of a child who learned early that the home environment was not a regulator but a stressor. Both continuities establish the Davis household as economically precarious and proximate to street violence; the boys' shared origin story is one of two children navigating a context in which adult co-regulation was sporadic at best.

What this produces, developmentally, is a child who **co-regulates laterally rather than vertically** — i.e., uses a sibling, not a parent, as the affective anchor. Jefferson, two years older or thereabouts, was almost certainly Aaron's primary regulator in this period. The intensity of the adult Aaron's brother-wound is incomprehensible unless the brother was load-bearing in early childhood; you do not mourn a sibling for thirty years over a single robbery. You mourn them that long because they were the secure base, and losing them collapsed the only attachment architecture that had ever worked.

### Cognitive style

The proto-form of the adult's tactical-exploit cognition is already visible in retrospect. Aaron thinks in **seams** — the place where the alarm sleeps, the half-second the guard looks away, the want in a stranger's face he can lever — and this is not a thinking style one acquires in adulthood. It is the cognition of a child who learned to read environments faster than the environments could read him, because being read first meant being hurt. Hypervigilance-as-intelligence: the same neural circuits that in a safer child would be running theory-of-mind for play are running threat-assessment for survival. The cost is a permanently **externalized cognitive style** — Aaron thinks *outward*, into the room, not *inward*, into himself. He has limited interoceptive vocabulary in every subsequent decade. He cannot tell you what he feels; he can tell you with surgical precision what *you* feel.

### Self-concept

Not yet stable. Best inference: a self organized around **being-with-Jefferson** — the younger-brother position, dyadic, derivative. The catastrophic implication of this is that when Jefferson later severs, Aaron loses not only a brother but the relational frame in which his self existed. He has to construct a new self from scratch in late adolescence, and the only materials available are the ones the street provides: competence, craft, the cool exterior.

---

## DECADE TWO: ADOLESCENCE AND EMERGING ADULTHOOD (approx. ages 11–20)

### Affect regulation

This is the decade in which the **action-as-regulator** strategy crystallizes. Both timelines reference the brothers' adolescent and young-adult drift into shared criminal activity — small jobs that escalate. The psychological function of this drift is not, primarily, economic. It is regulatory. Crime delivered to adolescent Aaron three things no other available activity could: a structured arousal curve (planning → execution → escape → debrief) that *contained* the chronic hypervigilance by giving it an object; a shared activity with Jefferson that maintained the dyadic regulation; and a competence-feedback loop in which Aaron's pre-existing scan-the-room cognition was finally being *rewarded* rather than merely surviving.

This is critical. Aaron did not become a thief because he was depraved. He became a thief because thieving was the first context in his life in which his existing nervous system was an **asset**. Linehan's framework would call this a near-textbook case of an emotionally vulnerable temperament finding an invalidating environment, with the twist that the eventual "validating" environment is itself criminogenic.

### Cognitive style

Tactical cognition matures into **craft cognition**. The seam-reading becomes systematized: routes, tools, fences, timing. Aaron starts to take pride in clean work — a pride visible decades later in his contempt for sloppy operators like the Scorpion's crew. The aesthetic dimension of this is important and underappreciated in the file: Aaron is a man with **taste in his own field**, and taste is the residue of love. He loved the work in this decade in a way he could not yet love people, because the work would not reject him.

### Self-concept

The Pivotal Event occurs in this window — the shared robbery in which violence (a death, or near-death) happens, after which Jefferson breaks. The exact mechanics differ between continuities but the structural fact is invariant: the dyad shatters under conditions of **mutual culpability**, and Jefferson resolves the shame by extruding Aaron from the moral universe. He does not merely stop speaking to him; he behaves as if Aaron does not exist, to the point that the next generation grows up unaware of the uncle.

The psychological event this constitutes, for Aaron, is **annihilation by the only person whose recognition constituted his self**. Fairbairn's schizoid-position language fits: the libidinal object becomes the rejecting object, and the self splits to manage the unmanageable. Aaron at twenty has two choices — collapse into shame-identity (become the cautionary tale Jefferson named him) or armor against it (become so competent that the verdict cannot reach him). He chooses the second, but the first is preserved underneath, undigested, and will leak through every subsequent decade.

This is the genesis of the **vulnerable-narcissistic** substrate. The grandiose surface — the cool professional, the man who made his own way — is not a personality; it is a **prosthesis** for a self that was supposed to be co-constructed with a brother who walked away.

---

## DECADE THREE: TWENTIES (the consolidation of the operator)

### Affect regulation

Action-based regulation becomes total. Aaron in his twenties is functionally **a man who feels by doing**. The somatic markers of this era — inferred backward from the early-Ultimate panels — are: low resting affect display, sharply elevated affect during operations (focus, mild euphoria, "flow"), and a hard crash in unstructured downtime that he manages by lining up the next job rather than by feeling it. There is no chemical signature; he does not drink to manage, does not use, does not appear to gamble compulsively. The job *is* the substance.

This is the decade in which the absence of substance use becomes diagnostic. A man carrying this much shame who is not self-medicating is a man whose primary defense is **so structurally sufficient** that chemistry would be redundant. The defense is the work, and the work scales.

### Cognitive style

Operator cognition fully matures. By the close of this decade Aaron is what the early *Ultimate Comics Spider-Man* arc shows him as: a credentialed professional in the New York criminal ecology, with relationships to fences, suppliers, information brokers, and rival crews. His thinking has acquired what intelligence work would call **target-package discipline** — he does not improvise into a job, he assembles it. The Oscorp break-in that incidentally produces the spider that bites Miles is, on Aaron's end, a clean piece of work; the failure cascade is Osborn's, not his.

What is being suppressed cognitively in this decade is any sustained **reflective function** in Fonagy's sense — the capacity to hold one's own mental states as objects of thought. Aaron mentalizes *others* with high precision (operator's necessity) and mentalizes *himself* with near-total impoverishment. Ask him in this decade what he feels about Jefferson and he would change the subject; not as evasion, but because the question has no internal address to which it can be delivered.

### Self-concept

Consolidated grandiose surface, suppressed shame core. The two are held apart by the work, which both performs the grandiosity and prevents the introspection that would touch the shame. He is, by the end of this decade, **stable in his pathology** — which is not the same as healthy, but is not nothing. Most men carrying his developmental load do not arrive at thirty with intact executive function, a marketable trade, and no addiction. Aaron does, and the cost is that he has built a self that cannot tolerate the conditions of its own repair.

---

## DECADE FOUR: THIRTIES (the discovery of Miles, the Ultimate-arc collapse)

### Affect regulation

This is the decade in which the regulatory architecture begins to fail, because something enters the system that the architecture was never designed to process: **a new attachment object**.

The discovery that he has a nephew, and then that the nephew is Spider-Man, and then that the nephew is Spider-Man *because of a spider Aaron himself stole*, is, in clinical terms, a perfect storm of reactivation. The attachment system, dormant since the brother-rupture, comes back online without warning. Aaron does not have the affect-tolerance to handle this. He compensates by **routing the new attachment through the only relational templates he has** — transaction (gifts), mentorship (training), leverage (the threat of exposure). Each of these is, from his side, an attempt at love. None of them is recognizable as love from the receiving side, which is the tragedy.

The Linehan-frame description: Aaron's emotional intensity in this decade exceeds his skill repertoire. He has the wanting; he does not have the words, the tolerance for vulnerability, or the practiced rituals of safe closeness that would let the wanting land. So the wanting comes out as control, because control is the only skill he has for managing intensity.

Affective dysregulation in the Ultimate arc is visible in escalating tempo of his Miles-directed behavior across the run: the visits get more frequent, the gifts more pointed, the leverage more explicit, the threats less veiled. This is not a man hardening into villainy. This is a man **panicking**, in the specific mode of someone whose only response to relational anxiety is to tighten the relational grip, and who is watching the grip destroy the thing it is meant to hold.

### Cognitive style

The operator cognition does not degrade in this decade — that is what makes the failure so legible. The same man who reads rooms with surgical precision *cannot read his own nephew*, because reading his own nephew would require turning the scan inward to see what he is doing. The cognitive deformation is exactly the one identified in the foundational analysis: Aaron cannot stop running the leverage-assessment on family. The automatic processing that kept him alive for twenty years is now metabolizing the one relationship he wants to preserve.

There is also, in this decade, the first sustained appearance of **rationalization at scale**. The "I'm teaching him real-world skills" framing recurs because it has to: it is the cognitive bridge that lets Aaron continue to do what he is doing while not knowing what he is doing. Beck's schema-language would identify this as a **compensatory belief** masking the core schema (defectiveness/abandonment) — *if I am useful to him, he cannot leave me the way Jefferson did*.

### Self-concept

Bifurcation deepens to the point of structural strain. The surface — cool uncle, competent operator, man-with-a-plan — runs at full capacity. Underneath, what the discovery of Miles has done is **resurrect the disinherited-younger-brother self** that was put in storage at twenty. Aaron is now, internally, simultaneously thirty-something and twenty, simultaneously the operator and the boy whose brother walked away. He cannot integrate these because integration would require contact with Jefferson, which he refuses.

The Ultimate arc terminus — death by his own malfunctioning gauntlets in the act of coercing Miles — is, read clinically, a **suicidal-by-recklessness** event in the sense that Shneidman would recognize. He does not consciously seek death. But the affect floor has dropped out; he is operating at a tempo and risk-tolerance that no sober operator of his caliber would accept; and the agent of his death is his own equipment, which is to say, the **instrument of his identity turning on him at the moment he most fully embodies it**. He dies as the thief, in the gear of the thief, killing the relationship that was the only argument against being just the thief. It is not suicide. It is what the older self-psychology literature called **disintegration anxiety enacted** — the self collapsing in the manner most consistent with its structure.

---

## DECADE FIVE: FORTIES (the 616 reform arc)

### Affect regulation

The 616 continuity grants Aaron the decade the Ultimate arc denied him, and the granted decade is, clinically, the most interesting period in the file. He is shown attempting **sustained affect tolerance** for the first time in his life — sitting with discomfort rather than discharging it through action. The driving job is the most underrated detail in the entire 616 portrayal: it is **structured, low-stimulation, low-stakes, lateral movement through the city**, which is to say, the exact opposite of the operational tempo that regulated him for two decades. He is, in choosing it, *deliberately removing his primary defense*. This is not a man hiding out. This is a man attempting exposure therapy on himself, without language for what he is doing.

The relapses — the leverage by the Assessor, the brief returns to old work — are not failures of will; they are predictable rebounds. A nervous system that has used the job as its regulator for twenty-plus years cannot be detoxed in months. The clinical-relevant fact is that the **return-to-baseline interval** shortens across the arc: each relapse is followed by faster self-correction, more articulate remorse, and more behavior consistent with the reform rather than the old pattern. This is what recovery looks like when it is real and not stylized — non-linear, with shrinking amplitude.

A second-order affect-regulation development: in 616, Aaron begins to use **verbal disclosure** in small doses with Miles. He talks about the past. He admits things. This is unprecedented in the Ultimate record and is the diagnostic marker of the reform's depth — he is acquiring, in his forties, the affect-regulation skill (use words, tolerate the listener's response) that most secure people acquire in childhood. He is bad at it. He gets better.

### Cognitive style

The exploit-scan does not turn off — that would be neurologically implausible — but the **inhibitory layer** thickens. He sees the leverage and does not take it; sees the seam and does not enter it; reads the room and uses the read to *withdraw* rather than to act. This is the operator's cognition placed under conscious veto, which is exhausting and inconsistent (hence the relapses) but represents real structural change.

Mentalization of self begins to come online. He can, in 616, **describe his own motives** with a degree of accuracy that the Ultimate-era Aaron could not approach. He understands that he uses Miles. He knows that he is afraid of Jefferson. He can name the shame. Fonagy would identify this as the developmental task he should have completed twenty years earlier, finally being undertaken under the pressure of a second chance.

### Self-concept

The grandiose surface thins. The vulnerable substrate becomes more available to consciousness — which is painful, and is the price of the integration. He begins, for the first time, to **describe himself accurately to himself**: a man who did real harm, who is trying not to do more, who does not deserve the trust he is being given but will try to earn it. This is the McWilliams-style movement from a primarily characterological organization to a more neurotic-level one — the defenses softening enough to let suffering through, which is what permits change.

The relationship with Jefferson does not fully repair in the 616 record. This is psychologically correct: the brother-wound is the oldest structure, and integrating it would require the brother's participation, which is not consistently available. What Aaron achieves instead is a **reorganization around Miles as the addressable kin-object** — the love that could not go to Jefferson goes to the nephew, and is now being delivered, fitfully and imperfectly, in a register the nephew can actually receive.

---

## DECADE SIX AND PROSPECTIVE (the fifties, projected)

The published record runs out here, but the trajectory permits inference. If the 616 arc holds — if Aaron does not catastrophically relapse, if Miles continues to extend the kin-frame, if Jefferson permits even minimal contact — Aaron in his fifties would be, clinically, **a partially-integrated late-onset reformer**: a man who has done most of his developmental work two decades behind schedule, whose affect-regulation skills remain effortful rather than automatic, who will need the relational scaffolding indefinitely but whose pattern of offending is broken.

The risk profile in this projected decade is not the old criminality — it is **depression**, late-onset, of the kind that surfaces when the defense (the work, the cool, the operator-identity) is finally fully relinquished and the underlying grief of the unlived life becomes available. Aaron at fifty-five, sober from his own pathology, may finally feel the full weight of what the brother-rupture cost him for thirty-five years. That is the bill that comes due when the defenses come down. Whether he can pay it depends on whether the kin-architecture around him — Miles, and through Miles perhaps Jefferson — holds.

---

## SYNTHESIS: THE LONGITUDINAL SHAPE

The decade-by-decade picture describes a single coherent psychological trajectory: a child whose only secure attachment was lateral (the brother), who lost that attachment under conditions of shared shame, who built a competent prosthetic self out of the criminal craft because the craft rewarded the very nervous-system features the lost attachment had failed to soothe, who maintained that prosthesis for two decades in stable but isolated pathology, whose attachment system involuntarily reactivated upon the discovery of the nephew, who in the first reactivation (Ultimate) lacked the skills to manage the intensity and died in the equipment of his own identity, and who in the second reactivation (616) is — slowly, imperfectly, with measurable backsliding — acquiring in middle age the affect-regulation and self-reflective capacities that the foundational developmental rupture prevented him from acquiring at the proper time.

The clinical headline across all six decades: **Aaron Davis is not, and has never been, a man whose primary problem is criminality. He is a man whose primary problem is a single severed attachment, around which an entire competent and dangerous adult was constructed as a way of surviving the severance.** The criminality is the scar tissue. The reform, when it works, is what happens when the original wound is finally addressed — not by the brother who made it, but by the nephew the brother accidentally provided.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: Davis, Aaron — Prowler designation
### File section 04 / longitudinal psychiatric workup

---

## 4.1 Framing the Assessment

Before any diagnostic label is advanced, the structural caveat: Aaron Davis has, to the best of the published behavioral record, never sat for a clinical evaluation, never been court-ordered to one despite a documented criminal career that would in most jurisdictions have triggered one, never voluntarily presented to a mental-health practitioner, and never been hospitalized for psychiatric reasons in either continuity tracked. The evaluative material is therefore entirely **observational and inferential**, drawn from behavioral records across the Ultimate arc (Bendis, *Ultimate Comics Spider-Man* through his on-panel death), the post-*Secret Wars* 616 reintroduction (Ahmed's *Miles Morales: Spider-Man*), and collateral appearances (*Spider-Men II*, *All-New Ultimates*, *Champions* tangentials). The two continuities must be read as parallel longitudinal courses of the same underlying structure under different environmental conditions — one in which the attachment-repair window closed, one in which it remained open. The diagnostic picture is consistent across both; only the **outcome trajectory** differs, and that difference is itself diagnostically informative.

The dominant impression on first review is one of a man who functions extremely well by every operational metric his world cares about and extremely poorly by every metric that would matter to a clinician. There is no acute syndrome to treat. There is a **characterological organization** that produces a recognizable life-course pattern: high-skill criminal occupation, narrow attachment surface, periodic relational catastrophe, no help-seeking. The work of this section is to specify that organization precisely and to defend the specification against the differentials it most resembles.

---

## 4.2 Primary Formulation

### 4.2.1 Antisocial Personality features — moderate severity, **non-psychopathic variant**

The most parsimonious primary formulation is antisocial personality structure of moderate severity, with the explicit qualifier that this is **not** psychopathy, and the further qualifier that the structure is dynamically rather than constitutionally driven — what the older psychoanalytic literature (Alexander, then Johnson and Szurek, then more rigorously Kernberg in his *Severity of Personality Disorders* spectrum work) would have called the "**neurotic character with antisocial features**," and what contemporary DSM-5-TR / ICD-11 dimensional frameworks would describe as **prominent traits of antagonism and disinhibition with retained empathy capacity and intact internalized object relations**.

Specific criterion-by-criterion accounting against DSM-5 ASPD (Criterion A, seven sub-items, three needed):

1. **Failure to conform to social norms with respect to lawful behaviors.** Met, robustly. Decades of B&E, theft, weapons offenses, and contracted criminal labor. Not contestable.
2. **Deceitfulness, repeated lying, use of aliases, conning of others for personal profit.** Met. The Prowler designation is itself an alias; he conceals his identity from his own brother for years; he conceals his identity from Miles initially even while cultivating intimacy; his operational mode is by definition deceitful.
3. **Impulsivity or failure to plan ahead.** **Not met in the conventional sense.** This is the first place the standard ASPD picture begins to fracture. Aaron's offending is highly planned, craft-organized, and tempo-controlled. What looks like impulsivity is more accurately **opportunism within a planning frame** — he improvises within prepared structures. The DSM item, drafted with chaotic-offender profiles in mind, fits him only weakly.
4. **Irritability and aggressiveness, repeated physical fights or assaults.** Partially met, but mediated. Violence is instrumental, not affect-driven. He does not start bar fights; he finishes operational confrontations. There is no record of recreational violence.
5. **Reckless disregard for safety of self or others.** Met in operational contexts; the gauntlet-failure death in the Ultimate arc is the apotheosis of own-safety disregard.
6. **Consistent irresponsibility.** Met in the conventional senses (no stable employment in Ultimate; financial precarity; family obligations abandoned). The 616 arc attenuates this — the rideshare work, the attempted reentry into the family — but does not erase the longitudinal pattern.
7. **Lack of remorse.** **Failed.** This is the criterion the diagnosis founders on. Remorse is documented, repeatedly, across both continuities. In Ultimate it surfaces too late and is overridden by the coercion pattern; in 616 it organizes substantial behavior. A man capable of the 616 reform arc cannot be classified as meeting the ASPD remorse criterion.

So: he meets four to five of seven, easily clearing the diagnostic threshold of three, with onset before age 15 inferable from the shared brother-backstory (the early robbery, the deaths-or-near-deaths in adolescence) and the conduct-disorder antecedent thereby established. **By the letter of DSM-5, he qualifies for ASPD.** The diagnosis is technically defensible.

It is also, by the standards of careful psychiatric work, **insufficient and partially misleading**, because ASPD as a category captures a wide and heterogeneous population — from the genuinely psychopathic to the criminally socialized to, as here, the dynamically antisocial — and Aaron sits at the far benign end of that distribution. The diagnosis must therefore be carried with the qualifier **"non-psychopathic, attachment-capable, dynamically organized,"** which is essentially a way of saying that the label is administratively correct and clinically inadequate. This is why the Hare PCL-R cross-check matters and is performed below.

### 4.2.2 Hare PCL-R cross-check

The Psychopathy Checklist-Revised separates the affective/interpersonal facet (Factor 1) from the lifestyle/antisocial facet (Factor 2). The crude empirical observation, repeatedly replicated, is that ASPD-positive individuals split into a large majority who score high only on Factor 2 (criminal-lifestyle) and a smaller, far more dangerous subset who score high on both. Aaron Davis is a textbook Factor-2-elevated, Factor-1-low presentation.

**Factor 1 items, scored against record:**
- *Glibness/superficial charm:* present in a non-malignant form; the charm is real, not predatory in its core register, and is deployed even where there is no instrumental payoff (e.g., with Miles in non-job contexts).
- *Grandiose sense of self-worth:* present but **vulnerable rather than primary**, a thin scaffolding over substantial shame (see §4.3 on narcissistic features).
- *Pathological lying:* present operationally; **absent intimately** — he lies about his work, not about who he is to the people who matter to him, and the failure to maintain even his work-lies to Miles is what eventually outs him.
- *Conning/manipulative:* present, with the critical qualifier that he manipulates **toward continued contact** as often as toward extraction; the manipulation serves attachment as well as gain.
- *Lack of remorse or guilt:* **absent.** Remorse trajectory is documented across both arcs.
- *Shallow affect:* **absent.** Affect with Miles is full-spectrum; affect with Jefferson, in flashback and inference, is the most reactive register he has.
- *Callous/lack of empathy:* **partially absent.** Empathy is present but **gated** — operative within a defined in-group (kin, non-combatants, the trafficked) and switched off in operational contexts toward defined opposition. This is not psychopathic acallousness; this is the moral architecture of a working-class criminal subculture with a robust in-group/out-group code.
- *Failure to accept responsibility:* mixed; he accepts operational responsibility (own his jobs) and avoids relational responsibility (won't talk to Jefferson) — a pattern more consistent with shame avoidance than with psychopathic responsibility-evasion.

The Factor-1 profile is, in aggregate, **non-psychopathic with mild trait coloration**. Hare-style total scoring would likely place him in the moderate range on Factor 2 and low on Factor 1, generating a composite well below the conventional psychopathy cutoff. This matters enormously for prognosis: psychopathy is treatment-refractory; the structure Aaron actually has is **treatment-responsive in principle**, and the 616 arc is the empirical demonstration.

### 4.2.3 Narcissistic Personality features — **vulnerable subtype**, secondary

A secondary characterological layer is required to account for the full presentation. Aaron displays a coherent set of narcissistic traits organized along the vulnerable rather than the grandiose pole — the Pincus / Cain / Wright differentiation, replicated in the Pathological Narcissism Inventory's bifactor structure.

The grandiose surface is real but **load-bearing rather than constitutive**: the craftsman-thief self-presentation, the cool-uncle performance, the contempt for sloppy operators (visible in his early Scorpion-adjacent dealings) all function to maintain a self that, beneath, knows itself as the brother who was thrown out. Diagnostic markers:

- **Disproportionate response to criticism**, especially from in-group figures. Jefferson's verdict (in inferred backstory) organizes decades of behavior. Miles's disapproval in late-Ultimate is destabilizing in a way that Miles's anger is not — contempt punctures, fury merely engages.
- **Over-explanation and over-justification** when the craftsman frame is challenged. The "I'm teaching him real-world skills" rationalization for using Miles on jobs is repeated to the point that it is plainly self-addressed.
- **Asymmetry between need-for-mirroring and capacity-for-mirroring**: he requires Miles to see him as more than a thief; he is correspondingly poor at seeing Miles as anything other than what Aaron needs him to be in the moment (kin / mentee / asset).
- **Shame as the dominant negative affect** rather than anger. Vulnerable narcissists collapse where grandiose narcissists rage; Aaron collapses, characteristically, into recklessness or confession depending on continuity.

The vulnerable-narcissistic layer is what makes the ASPD picture coherent. The criminality is not in service of a grandiose self that needs feeding; it is in service of a depleted self that needs occupation, mastery, and a story it can tell itself. This distinction is prognostically central.

### 4.2.4 Complex/relational trauma residue — **subclinical**, with structural sequelae

Aaron does not meet DSM-5 PTSD criteria. There are no documented intrusive re-experiencing phenomena, no flashbacks, no dissociative episodes, no exaggerated startle on the record (he is hypervigilant, but the vigilance is tonic and tactical, not phasic and reactive — a very different neurobiological signature). He does not meet ICD-11 Complex PTSD criteria either, lacking the three disturbances-in-self-organization clusters in full form: affective dysregulation is muted by his action-orientation, negative self-concept is present but compartmentalized rather than pervasive, and disturbances in relationships are present but, again, target-specific (Miles, Jefferson) rather than generalized.

What is present is **the structural residue of developmental trauma without the syndrome**: hypervigilance metabolized into vocational competence, foreshortened future-sense expressed as a planning horizon that runs job-to-job rather than year-to-year, restricted affect range in intimate settings, pre-emptive relational sabotage. This is the picture of someone whose survival strategy was so effective at organizing his trauma into productive function that the symptoms never crystallized into a discrete disorder. Clinically this is often **harder to treat than frank PTSD**, because there is no discrete symptom to which the patient is willing to attach treatment-seeking — the trauma has become the personality.

---

## 4.3 Etiology

The etiological model that best accounts for the convergent data:

1. **Environmental violence in childhood**, of a kind and duration that produced sustained autonomic activation and the development of vigilance and threat-reading as primary cognitive modes. Specific events are not on the record; the systemic pattern is.
2. **Identification with the aggressor** as the operative defensive solution, channeling absorbed violence outward as professionalized competence rather than inward as victim-identity. This is **adaptive in survival terms, deformative in relational ones**, and is the single most important formative move in his psychological development.
3. **Catastrophic rupture in early adulthood**: the shared crime with Jefferson, the death (or near-death) it produced, and Jefferson's subsequent excommunication. This is the trauma that the residue in §4.2.4 most precisely tracks. It is also the event that fixed his attachment style — having had a primary attachment severed under conditions of mutual culpability, the lesson encoded was *closeness ends in being thrown out*, and the behavioral response was to narrow the attachment surface to near-zero.
4. **Compensatory mastery in the criminal trade**, which provided the only stable self-concept (the craftsman) and the only consistent affect-regulation channel (the work itself — see §4.4 on substance use). The competence solved the immediate problem and locked in the long-term one: he became a man whose self-worth was contingent on continued offending.
5. **Reactivation of the attachment system** through the discovery of Miles. This is the **etiologically critical late event**, the one that determines which of the two continuity-trajectories he runs. The attachment system, having been offline for decades, comes back online with no updated templates — he reaches for Miles through the only relational modes he has (transaction, mentorship, coercion-as-contact), which produces the Ultimate-arc catastrophe. In 616, the same reactivation occurs with marginally more time, marginally more environmental support, and marginally more capacity for repair-work, and produces the rehabilitative arc.

The model is **diathesis-stress with a strong environmental loading** and no requirement to posit constitutional callousness. Everything in the presentation can be accounted for by ordinary developmental processes acting on extraordinary childhood and early-adult conditions.

---

## 4.4 Symptom Presentation in Behavior — Granular Mapping

The diagnostic features above are not abstractions; they are visible in the behavioral micro-record. The mapping:

- **The remorse criterion failure (against ASPD)** is visible in: the late-Ultimate scenes in which he attempts to back out of the coercion of Miles and cannot find a way; the 616 arc's voluntary disclosures to Miles about his past; the consistent inability to discuss Jefferson without affect leak; the documented refusal, across both continuities, to cross specific moral lines (children, non-combatants, trafficking victims) even at operational cost.
- **The vulnerable-narcissistic injury** is visible in: the over-explanation pattern when the craftsman frame is questioned; the disproportionate destabilization produced by Miles's contempt versus Miles's anger; the way he physically exits rooms when Jefferson is invoked rather than engaging.
- **The action-based affect regulation** is visible in: the absence of substance use (a man with this much shame would, on base rates, be a drinker; he is not); the way distress reliably converts to planning behavior rather than to expressive behavior; the gift-giving and shared-activity register of intimacy with Miles in place of verbal disclosure.
- **The hypervigilance** is visible in: room-scanning on entry (a tic so consistent it functions as a recognition signature); light sleep patterns; the never-fully-relaxed posture even in domestic settings; eating on the move.
- **The splitting defense around Miles** is visible in: the toggling between mentor and handler registers within single conversations; the affect-incongruence at the toggle-points; the inability to hold both representations simultaneously.
- **The instrumentalization-of-intimacy pattern** is visible in: the extortion sequence in late Ultimate; the way contact-frequency with Miles tracks Aaron's own anxiety level rather than mutual availability; the recurrent reach for leverage precisely when the relationship feels most precarious.

---

## 4.5 Comorbidity

The pertinent comorbidities — those that should be screened-for in any forward-looking assessment — are:

- **Persistent Depressive Disorder (dysthymia) — not currently met, monitor.** The shame load and the chronic relational deprivation are textbook setups for dysthymia. The absence of mood symptoms to date is attributable to the action-orientation; should the action-channel be removed (incarceration, injury, equipment loss), depression onset is a high-probability event. The Ultimate-arc reckless-final-confrontation pattern can be read as a depressive equivalent already breaking through.
- **Substance Use Disorder — not currently met, elevated lifetime risk.** No on-record pattern, which is itself diagnostically informative. The risk window is the post-criminal phase, where the work-as-regulator is no longer available.
- **Gambling Disorder / behavioral addiction features — subthreshold but suggestive.** The thrill of the job functions, mechanistically, the way a behavioral addiction functions; reward is intermittent, ritualized, escalating, and self-medicating. He is not a pathological gambler, but the reward-system organization is in the same family.
- **Antisocial-spectrum features in late life:** if attachment access to Miles is severed permanently, predicted trajectory is **deepening of the antisocial structure**, not into psychopathy (he cannot become what he constitutionally is not) but into a colder, more bitter, more nihilistic version of the same organization — the Ultimate-death precursor pattern, extended.
- **Suicidality — passive, situational, not chronic.** The Ultimate-arc final confrontation reads as suicide-by-circumstance more than as accident; the 616 collapse-and-confess pattern is the non-lethal equivalent. He is not a chronic suicide risk; he is an acute one at points of total relational rupture.

---

## 4.6 Course Over Time

Tracked longitudinally and integrating both continuities as parallel courses of the same structure:

- **Adolescence:** Conduct Disorder antecedent inferable from the brothers' shared backstory — early offending, in-group with Jefferson, the catastrophic shared crime as the terminal adolescent event.
- **Early adulthood (post-rupture):** Crystallization of the criminal-craftsman identity; attachment-surface narrowed to zero; affect-regulation via work fully installed; the structure stabilizes into its mature form.
- **Mid-career (pre-Miles):** Steady-state operation. Pure professional. Ego in craft, contempt for sloppy operators, no documented relational life of consequence. This is the longest phase of his life and the one with the fewest visible symptoms because the structure is functioning exactly as designed.
- **Discovery of Miles:** The destabilizing event. Attachment system reactivates with no updated templates; the entire subsequent trajectory is the working-out of that reactivation.
- **Ultimate trajectory:** The reactivation is metabolized through coercion and leverage; the structure cannot accommodate the new attachment without deforming the relationship that occasioned it; outcome is relational catastrophe and operational death.
- **616 trajectory:** The reactivation is metabolized through partial reform; environmental supports (Ahmed-era Miles's willingness to maintain contact, the slower-tempo rideshare work) hold long enough for new templates to begin forming; outcome is provisional rehabilitation, repeatedly threatened by relapse but not eliminated.

The two trajectories together form what is, in effect, a **natural experiment in attachment-rehabilitation under personality-structure constraint**. The structure is the same; the variable is whether the attachment object remains accessible. This is the prognostic finding that should organize any forward-looking risk assessment.

---

## 4.7 Differential — What He Is Not, and Why

A rigorous differential is the discipline that prevents the primary formulation from being lazy. Each of the following has been considered and is excluded; the grounds for exclusion are specified.

**Antisocial Personality Disorder, severe / psychopathic variant — EXCLUDED.** As detailed in §4.2.2, the Factor-1 PCL-R profile is non-psychopathic. Kin attachment is robust, remorse trajectory is documented, the 616 rehabilitative course is empirical disconfirmation. A psychopath does not reform under shame; he reforms under threat of consequence and reverts when consequence is removed. Aaron reforms under shame and sustains the reform partly in its absence.

**Borderline Personality Disorder — EXCLUDED.** The splitting defense is real but is **interpersonally targeted** (Miles-specific) rather than generalized across all close relationships; identity is stable rather than diffuse; affective lability in the BPD sense is absent (his affect is restricted, not labile); abandonment terror is target-specific and does not produce frantic-efforts-to-avoid behavior across the relational field; self-harm and parasuicidal behavior are absent (the Ultimate-arc death is reckless, not parasuicidal in the BPD signature sense). The structure is the wrong shape.

**Narcissistic Personality Disorder, full criteria — EXCLUDED as primary, retained as secondary feature set.** The vulnerable-narcissistic traits are present but do not organize the full presentation; they are a layer over the antisocial structure, not the structure itself. Full NPD would require a more consistently grandiose self-presentation, less in-group altruism, and absent capacity for genuine concern for others (he has the capacity; it is gated).

**Major Depressive Disorder, current or recurrent — EXCLUDED.** No anhedonia (he derives pleasure from craft, from Miles, from food and humor); no vegetative signs on record; no pervasive low mood; no diurnal pattern; no documented depressive episodes meeting duration criteria. The shame load is depressogenic in principle; it has not produced a syndrome. Monitor, do not diagnose.

**Persistent Depressive Disorder (Dysthymia) — EXCLUDED currently, on watch.** Absence of two-year sustained low-mood presentation. The chronic dysphoric undertone is real but is masked and channeled by the action-orientation; criteria are not met.

**Bipolar Spectrum Disorders — EXCLUDED.** No documented manic, hypomanic, or mixed episodes. The high-tempo operational behavior is goal-directed and sustainable, not energy-driven and unsustainable; sleep need is reduced by vigilance, not by mood; speech is not pressured; flight of ideas is absent.

**Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder — EXCLUDED.** As detailed in §4.2.4, the criteria fail in full. The trauma residue is present without the syndrome.

**Complex PTSD (ICD-11) — EXCLUDED.** Disturbances-in-self-organization clusters are present in attenuated and target-specific forms rather than pervasive forms. Subthreshold.

**Substance Use Disorder, any class — EXCLUDED on current record.** No sustained-use pattern documented; social drinking only. This is one of the more clinically interesting absences and is itself diagnostic.


## Behavioral Atlas

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — BEHAVIORAL ATLAS

*An exhaustive catalog of observable conduct, micro-tells, and decision habits across the full conditional range. Compiled from longitudinal observation across both continuities (Ultimate 2011–2014; 616 post-2015 through current solo material). Where the two records diverge, both are notated; where they converge, the convergence is itself a diagnostic finding.*

---

### 6.1 BASELINE / CALM STATE

The hardest state to catch him in, because it is rarely uninterrupted for long, but it has a clear signature.

**Postural baseline.** Aaron at rest carries his weight slightly forward on the balls of the feet even when seated — a thief's stance, the body permanently arranged for departure. When standing in a relaxed conversation he plants the dominant (right) foot and lets the left float, knee soft, so that one full step in any direction is already loaded. He leans on things rather than sits squarely against them: doorframes, counters, the hoods of cars, the railings of stoops. He does not occupy chairs deeply; he perches.

**Hand habits.** Hands stay visible and busy — keys turned in the palm, a phone tilted edge-to-edge between thumb and forefinger, the rim of a coffee cup traced clockwise. The hands are never both at rest simultaneously. When one stills, the other moves. This is not nervousness — it is the same low-amplitude motor channel a sniper uses to bleed off micro-tension before a shot.

**Gaze pattern.** A standing scan on entry to any room: corners first (clockwise from the doorframe), then exits, then weapons, then faces. Takes roughly two seconds and is invisible to people who do not know to look for it. Once cataloged, he relaxes the scan and settles into apparent inattention while continuing to track movement in his periphery — particularly hands and waistlines.

**Voice in calm.** Lower register than his stress voice, with a draw at the end of sentences — letting a phrase trail rather than punching it. He uses Miles's name often in calm conversation, sometimes once per exchange, as if confirming the relationship is still loaded. With strangers in low-stakes encounters (drivers, cashiers, building staff in 616) he is reflexively warm, asking small follow-up questions — "how long you been on this route?" — partly genuine sociability, partly habitual intelligence-gathering that has become indistinguishable from politeness.

**Decision habits in calm.** He overplans the trivial and underplans the existential. He will scout a route to a dinner he is not stealing from; he will not think a week ahead about his own life. Calm Aaron is the planner; stressed Aaron is the executor; there is almost no reflective Aaron in between. When he has nothing to do he gravitates to maintenance — cleaning gear, charging batteries, walking the perimeter of wherever he is staying. Idleness reads to him as exposure.

**Domestic micro-tells.** Keeps go-bags. Will not sleep with his back to a door. Pays cash where plausible even in 616 when he is ostensibly legitimate. Owns very little he could not replace in 48 hours. Photographs of Miles and (in 616) of Jefferson and Rio kept face-down or in a drawer when not being looked at — not hidden, but not displayed; the sentimentality is real and the exposure of it is unbearable.

---

### 6.2 MILD STRESS / OPERATIONAL TEMPO

Onset of a job, a confrontation pending, Miles late to a meet, a stranger in the building.

**Verbal change.** Sentences shorten and lose their trailing draw. The pet phrases ("alright, alright," "we good?") increase in frequency; they are self-soothing as much as social. Humor sharpens — he gets funnier under mild stress, not less funny, and the jokes are increasingly at his own expense. Self-deprecation is his preferred tension valve because it costs him nothing he values.

**Motor change.** The hands stop their idle motion and begin to *place* objects — sets the cup down deliberately, pockets the keys, removes rings (he has been seen to wear one or two; they come off before work). He squares his shoulders when standing, drops them when moving. There is a specific tell: a single quick exhale through the nose, audible only at close range, that punctuates the transition from "civilian Aaron" to "operating Aaron." Once you have heard it, it is unmistakable.

**Cognitive change.** Talks his plan aloud, sometimes to no one — narrates the next two moves under his breath. This is rehearsal, not anxiety; it externalizes sequencing so the body can run it without conscious load. He becomes pedagogical when stressed in Miles's presence: explains what he is doing, why, where the seam is, what the alarm will do. The teaching is genuine; it is also him steadying himself by performing competence to an audience he respects.

**Control behaviors.** Tightens grip on operational tempo — he wants to decide when the door opens, when the car moves, when the conversation ends. Resists being rushed by anyone, including allies. Will deliberately slow a hot situation by a half-beat to reassert his authorship of it, even at small tactical cost. This is one of his most reliable tells: when he becomes *slower*, he is not calmer, he is more stressed.

---

### 6.3 ACUTE STRESS / JOB GOING WRONG

A plan compromised, a partner failing, equipment misbehaving, leverage slipping.

**Voice.** Drops further in register and gains a flat affect — the warmth evacuates the tone and is replaced by a clipped, instructional cadence. He stops using names. Imperatives only: *move, down, here, now.* The Brooklyn cadence flattens toward a generic operational English; the regional music goes out of his voice and returns only when the situation resolves.

**Body.** The forward-weighted stance becomes a fighter's distribution — weight centered, slight bend in the knees, hands at hip-line and open. He gives ground readily in early acute stress (preferring to reposition than to clash) and only plants when there is an asset behind him worth holding ground for. With Miles behind him, he plants instantly and does not yield — this is one of the few unambiguous behavioral constants across both continuities.

**Decision habits.** Triages by exfil. The first question he answers internally is *how do we leave?* — not *how do we win?* He will abandon the take to preserve the route. He will not abandon a person he has decided is his. The hierarchy is: Miles > self > equipment > take > partner-of-convenience > take-from-take. He has demonstrably traded each level for the one above it on-panel.

**Improvisation pattern.** Reaches for environmental tools before weapon tools. A thrown bottle, a kicked-over rack, a sprayed extinguisher — the gauntlets come up last among options, not first. Partly because the gauntlets are loud and traceable; partly, by the late record, because he distrusts them after what they did to him in the Ultimate arc. (In 616 he is shown handling reconfigured gear with a slight pre-use hesitation absent from his earlier panels — a half-second of inspection that did not exist before the death-by-equipment incident in the other continuity. Whether the character "remembers" or not, the writer's hand records the residue.)

**Communication under fire.** He goes quiet on comms unless transmitting necessary information. Will not banter mid-action with anyone except, conspicuously, Miles — to whom he keeps talking even when tactically suboptimal, because the talking is reassurance for the boy and a tether for himself.

---

### 6.4 THREAT — INCOMING VIOLENCE DIRECTED AT HIM

**Pre-violence read.** He clocks aggression earlier than the room. The tell that he has read a threat: he stops drinking whatever he is drinking and sets it down with the rim aligned to a surface edge — a tiny placement, never spilled, always perfectly squared. The cup is now a thrown object in reserve. He then asks one redundant question of the threatener — *"You sure you want to do this in here?"* or its cognate — which serves three purposes: gives the threatener an off-ramp (he prefers to avoid violence on jobs where it costs operational signature), confirms intent, and buys him one breath of distance.

**Engagement style.** Economical. He does not throw combinations; he throws single decisive strikes and resets. Prefers to end an encounter in three motions or fewer. Targets the knee, the throat, the weapon hand, in that priority. Uses the environment as a second attacker — drives heads into countertops, doorframes, vehicle panels. Disinclined to ground fighting; will scramble back to standing aggressively because the ground costs him exfil options.

**Pain response.** Does not vocalize pain. Exhales it. When badly hit he goes briefly *more* composed, not less — the affect floor drops and he becomes uncannily still for a beat. This is dangerous to read as resignation; it is the opposite. It is the moment before his most committed counterattack.

**Weapon hierarchy in personal threat.** Hands → improvised → blade → gauntlet projectile → gauntlet claws. The escalation is reluctant. He prefers a thrown elbow to a drawn weapon because a thrown elbow does not get him remembered.

---

### 6.5 THREAT — VIOLENCE DIRECTED AT MILES OR KIN

A different organism. The threshold of restraint disappears.

**Behavioral signature.** He moves before he speaks. The redundant question that he offers to threats against himself is absent — kin-threats receive no off-ramp. He inserts himself bodily between Miles and the threat without ceding visual contact with either, a specific posture (chin over shoulder toward Miles, eyes locked forward on threat) that recurs across multiple incidents in both continuities.

**Tactical priorities invert.** Exfil drops below incapacitation. He will accept injury he would not accept on a job to keep the line held. The economy that governs his normal violence — three motions, reset, leave — extends into sustained engagement; he keeps hitting past the threshold where he would normally disengage.

**Verbal pattern.** Switches from clipped operational English to a specific, low, almost conversational threat tone — articulate, full sentences, often using the threatener's name if he knows it. He becomes *more* verbal, not less, because he is performing a willingness to follow through that he hopes will not require following through. When he goes silent in a kin-threat situation, the violence has already been decided on.

**Post-incident behavior.** Checks Miles physically before anything else — shoulders, ribs, head, hands — a quick competent assessment that he has done before, somewhere, on someone, long ago. (The inference: he learned this hand-check on his brother as a child. The choreography is too fluent to be improvised.) Will not discuss what happened in the moment; defers debrief; gets Miles moving and fed and somewhere safe before any conversation about it begins.

---

### 6.6 INTIMACY / CLOSENESS

The state in which he is least practiced and most legible.

**With Miles, low-stakes.** Generous physically: a hand on the back of the neck, a knock to the shoulder, a hand on the crown of the head when Miles sits and Aaron stands. The contact is brief and frequent rather than sustained — a man dosing himself with proximity in increments small enough to tolerate. He brings food and gifts compulsively; the gifts are nearly always *specific* (a thing Miles mentioned in passing weeks earlier, remembered and procured), which is the diagnostic detail — he listens at a level that exceeds what his surface manner suggests, and the listening is one of his most genuine acts of love.

**With Miles, high-stakes (emotional confrontation).** Deflects through humor first; if humor fails, deflects through action (proposes they go somewhere, do something, move); if action fails, deflects through a quasi-apology that does not quite admit the specific harm. He has, in 616, demonstrated the capacity to break this pattern and stay in the conversation — sit, absorb, acknowledge — but it visibly costs him; his hands grip whatever they can find, his jaw sets, and he speaks more slowly than usual. The slowness here is opposite to the operational slowness — it is not control, it is the body refusing to flee.

**With Jefferson (rare, mostly in flashback / brief 616 panels).** He cannot meet his brother's eyes for more than a beat. Looks at Jefferson's mouth, hairline, hands — anywhere but the eyes. Verbal output drops by an order of magnitude; he becomes nearly monosyllabic. The charm shuts off entirely. This is the only relationship in which the surface man is unavailable to him.

**With Rio (post-616, limited record).** Treats her with a careful, formal respect that suggests both genuine regard for the woman Jefferson chose and an awareness that her judgment of him is a referendum he cannot win. He does not joke with Rio. He listens to her with full attention. He does not initiate contact with her; he responds when she initiates.

**With sexual / romantic intimates.** The record is thin in both continuities — Aaron does not appear to maintain sustained romantic partnerships, which is itself data. The implied pattern: short, charm-driven encounters, low disclosure, exits managed. He does not appear to use sex as a regulator (the absence is notable in a profile that would predict its presence). The intimacy budget is spent on Miles; what remains is small.

**With operational partners.** First-name basis quickly, genuine warmth, no actual disclosure. He learns about them; they do not learn about him. Generous with operational credit, miserly with personal information. Partners who try to push intimacy on him (the Scorpion's attempts at fraternal bonding, the Assessor's at ownership) get the cold version of him within one conversation.

---

### 6.7 GRIEF

Aaron does not grieve out loud. The record contains several losses (operational partners, in 616 his own near-deaths and the deaths of those around him; in Ultimate the implied background grief over Jefferson's lifelong rejection) and in none of them does he weep on-panel. The grief manifests laterally.

**Behavioral signature.** Becomes a better worker. Sharper, more deliberate, longer hours on whatever the current job is. The grief energy is poured into competence. He drinks slightly more in the week after a loss but not enough to call a binge — one extra glass, two extra nights. He sleeps less and walks more; the night-walking habit intensifies under grief, sometimes for hours.

**Verbal signature.** Talks about the lost person in present tense for approximately one beat too long before correcting, then does not bring them up again for a long time. The correction is the tell. He does not memorialize aloud; he memorializes by carrying a small object — a lighter, a coin, a key — that belonged to or was associated with the lost person, in a specific pocket, for weeks.

**Relational signature.** Reaches for Miles within 48 hours of a loss, usually under a pretext (lunch, a favor, a check-in), and is gentler than usual during that visit. The pretext is for both of them; Aaron cannot ask for proximity directly, so he constructs an errand that requires it.

**Anniversary behavior.** No on-panel evidence of formal anniversary observance, but a pattern of unexplained mood shifts on dates that, in the longitudinal record, correlate with specific past events. Becomes quieter, more careful, more available to Miles, on what appear to be private commemorations. He does not name them.

---

### 6.8 VICTORY

A successful job, an outmaneuvered adversary, a moment with Miles that goes well.

**Immediate post-victory.** Quiet, not loud. Does not celebrate at the scene of a win — celebration on-site is, in his operational ethic, an amateur tell. The face stays neutral, the body stays composed, until distance has been opened. The celebration, when it comes, is small: a half-smile, a slow shake of the head, a single low laugh to himself in the car. He may buy himself something afterward — a meal, a piece of clothing — modest, ritualized, repeated.

**With Miles after a shared win.** The warmth is unguarded for a short window — full grin, the laugh that the surface man usually edits down, an arm around the shoulder that lingers a full beat longer than usual. He compliments Miles specifically and technically — *"that pull at the third floor, that was clean"* — not generically. The technical compliment is, in his vocabulary, the highest form of love; it is the language his brother once spoke to him before everything broke.

**Decision habits in victory.** *Does not press his luck.* This is one of the most stable rules in the entire Atlas. Aaron walks away from runs of success faster than most operators of his caliber, because his oldest formative lesson is that the win precedes the catastrophe.
