The Ultimate arc records the one major violation of this rule — the period in which he pushes the Miles-leverage past where his own instinct says to stop — and it kills him. The 616 arc reads as a man who has somehow learned the lesson without having lived the death; the writing implies the character knows, somatically, that escalation past the win is fatal.

**Tells of overconfidence.** When he *does* slip into hubris, the signature is verbal: he begins to monologue. The talkativeness extends past its useful function and becomes self-pleasure. This is the moment, in any given scene, where competent observers should reach for a weapon — he is about to lose something.

---

### 6.9 DEFEAT

Failed jobs, exposures, ruptures with Miles, capture, equipment failure.

**Immediate response.** Composure first. He does not curse, does not throw, does not vocalize. The face goes still in the specific way it goes still under heavy pain — a withdrawal of expression rather than an expression of distress. He removes himself from the scene of defeat as efficiently as possible; if he cannot remove himself, he removes his attention, going internal for a period of minutes during which he is verbally present but cognitively elsewhere, running an after-action review.

**Self-blame pattern.** Privately, brutal. He locates the failure precisely and assigns it to himself even when distributed causation is obvious. He does not extend the same brutality to operational partners — his judgments of others' failures are temperate; his judgments of his own are not. This asymmetry is the vulnerable-narcissistic structure in action: the harshness is not self-knowledge, it is self-punishment by a man who needs his self-image of competence and cannot survive its uncomplicated rupture.

**With Miles after a defeat.** Increased availability, decreased disclosure. He shows up more often, says less. The instinct is to repair the relational frame by presence rather than by conversation, because conversation requires him to articulate what happened and articulation is the thing he cannot do.

**Catastrophic defeat (kin-rejection, exposure, the unforgivable).** The affect floor drops out entirely. In the Ultimate record this manifests as recklessness escalating to the suicidal — he enters a final confrontation in a state that an experienced observer would recognize as not-trying-to-survive-it. In the 616 record the same affective collapse produces the opposite behavior: he confesses, sits down, lets the consequence land. The convergent finding is the floor-drop itself; the divergent finding is what he does with the room beneath the floor. The Ultimate man fills it with motion; the 616 man fills it with stillness. The difference is, almost exactly, the presence or absence of a viable repair object — Miles willing to remain in the frame.

---

### 6.10 ROUTINES, RITUALS, ROUTES

**Daily.** Wakes early, before he needs to. Coffee black, often more than one. Walks the neighborhood before settling into any work. Phone checked rarely but thoroughly — he reads texts in batches rather than at each ping. Eats one substantial meal a day, usually late; snacks otherwise. Showers at night, not morning — a thief's habit, residue removed before sleep, body presentable for emergency wake.

**Weekly.** A standing attempt to see Miles, usually framed as casual. Equipment maintenance, even in the 616 reform period (he keeps the gear functional regardless of whether he intends to use it — the unused readiness is itself a comfort). A circuit of certain neighborhoods, certain blocks, certain rooftops — partly nostalgia, partly intelligence-keeping, partly the same thing dogs do when they walk their territory.

**Routes.** Has memorized exits from every building he uses regularly, plural exits per building, with priority order. Does not take the same route to a recurring destination two days in a row. Parks facing out. Sits facing the door. Knows the schedules of doormen and superintendents in buildings he frequents and adjusts his comings accordingly. In 616 as an app driver, the routes are professionally sanctioned cover for the same compulsion — he is being paid to drive paths he would have driven anyway.

**Rituals around Miles.** Specific places they go (a diner, a roof, a corner). The food orders are fixed and Aaron orders for both without asking. He pays. He does not let Miles pay. Letting Miles pay would invert the frame in a way Aaron cannot tolerate; even in 616, even reformed, the uncle must be the provider in the small theater of the meal.

**Sleep.** Light, segmented, interrupted by perimeter checks if in an unfamiliar environment. In his own space, deeper but never full. He has the soldier's sleep — drops fast, surfaces fast, does not dream visibly on-panel (the absence of any dream-sequence content across his entire publication history is a writer's choice that doubles as a character fact: he does not appear to access his unconscious in any organized way, which is consistent with the affect-regulation-by-action profile).

---

### 6.11 MICRO-TELLS — THE FINE GRAIN

A list of the small, repeatable signatures that a longitudinal observer would catalog.

- **The squared cup.** Drinks set down with rim aligned to surface edge when he has clocked a threat.
- **The nose-exhale.** Single audible exhale through the nose marking the transition from civilian to operational mode.
- **Name-frequency with Miles.** Uses Miles's name more often when calm, less often when stressed, not at all when in acute combat — inverse to most speakers, who use names more under stress.
- **Ring removal.** Removes any rings before working. The replacement of rings is one of the markers that an operation is over.
- **The two-second scan.** Clockwise corner sweep on entering any room.
- **Pre-gauntlet hesitation (616 only).** Half-second inspection of equipment before activating, absent from the Ultimate record.
- **Eye avoidance with Jefferson.** Looks at mouth, hands, hairline — never eyes — and only with his brother.
- **Tense-slip in grief.** Present-tense reference to the lost, followed by a correction, then long silence on the topic.
- **The pocket object.** A small item carried for weeks after a loss, in a specific pocket, never displayed.
- **The technical compliment.** Specific, craft-grounded praise reserved almost exclusively for Miles.
- **The hand-check.** Quick competent physical assessment of Miles after any incident — a learned choreography from somewhere in his own childhood.
- **The monologue tell.** Extended verbal display in victory as the harbinger of his own coming loss.
- **Slower-equals-more-stressed.** Reduction of tempo under stress as a control assertion, not a calming.
- **The face-down photographs.** Sentiment present, exposure refused.
- **The pretext visit.** Constructed errand as the only available grammar for asking for proximity.

---

### 6.12 META-PATTERN

Across all conditions, one organizing r


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

*What a week of continuous surveillance would actually record. Compiled across both continuities; where the Ultimate-era and 616 patterns diverge, both are logged. Times are approximate, derived from on-panel circadian markers (light cues, when he texts Miles, when he is shown eating, when jobs occur).*

---

### 6.1 The Shape of a Day

Aaron does not live on a civilian clock. He lives on a **two-shift split** that has held across both continuities since first observation: a long sleep block of roughly four to five hours beginning between 0400 and 0500, and a shorter compensatory nap of forty to ninety minutes in the late afternoon, almost always taken on a couch or in a parked vehicle rather than a bed. The bed is for the long block; the couch is for the recovery block. He treats these as different categories of unconsciousness. The pattern is consistent with a working professional thief — jobs cluster between 2200 and 0330, the recovery nap is the buffer between the social-day and the operational-night — and it has carried over into his 616 driver-life even though the operational rationale has largely lapsed. The body has learned the schedule. He cannot sleep through a standard 2300 bedtime even when nothing is planned.

**Wake (0830–0930, Ultimate-era; 0700–0800, 616 driver-era).** No alarm visible on record in either continuity; he wakes to internal cue. First three minutes after waking are spent motionless, eyes open, scanning the ceiling and the room — a habituated threat-check that he himself almost certainly no longer registers as such. Then up in one motion, no sitting on the edge of the bed. He does not stretch. He goes immediately to a window and adjusts a blind by a finger's width — enough to see the street, not enough to be seen. This is the morning's first ritual and it has been observed in three separate residences across both timelines. He does not know he does it. If asked why the blind is always cracked exactly there, he would say he likes the light.

**Morning sequence.** Bathroom, then coffee, then phone — in that order, invariant. He drinks coffee black, prepared in a stovetop moka pot in the Ultimate apartment and in a single-cup drip in the 616 one; the through-line is that he does not own and will not use a machine with a timer or a wifi connection. He has a documented aversion to networked appliances in the home. Phone-check is done standing at the kitchen counter, not sitting: he reads texts and news in roughly ninety seconds, then puts the phone face-down and does not touch it again until he leaves the apartment. The face-down phone is another invariant. He does not eat breakfast in the conventional sense. He eats a banana, or a slice of toast, or nothing. Significant intake is deferred to a late lunch.

---

### 6.2 The Apartment

Aaron has lived in at least three documented residences across the published record, and the staging is consistent enough to constitute a signature.

- **Single bedroom, top floor or near-top, walk-up preferred over elevator building.** Top floor for roof access; walk-up because elevators are choke points and because he wants to hear who is on the stairs.
- **Two exits minimum.** In the Ultimate apartment, the fire escape was kept clear and the window unlocked. In the 616 apartment, a back-stair access reachable through a service hallway. He has never, on record, lived in a unit with only one egress.
- **Sparse furnishing, but not Spartan.** A couch, a television (rarely on), a low table, kitchen basics, one good chair. No clutter on horizontal surfaces — every visible flat is cleared, which is operationally legible (clutter hides things and slows movement) and which also reads as the residue of a man who has been raided before and learned not to leave anything readable.
- **The "civilian layer."** Books he has not finished, mail in a small stack, a houseplant that is alive in 616 and was a brown stalk in late-Ultimate. The houseplant index is a reliable marker of his current life-state: in periods of intentional living it survives; in periods of relapse-pressure it dies first.
- **The "operational layer."** A closet or wall cavity holding the Prowler kit — gauntlets, mask, boots, optics, two backup blades, currency in mixed denominations, two passports under work-names, a burner phone in a faraday pouch, and a small medical kit weighted toward burn dressings and topical anesthetic. The medical kit composition is its own diagnostic: he expects to be hurt by his own equipment more than by other people.
- **No photographs displayed.** None of Jefferson, none of Miles, none of his parents, none of women. This is not coldness; it is operational hygiene plus shame. Photographs name your hostages. A picture of Miles in the apartment is a photograph he cannot afford to have found.

He cleans the apartment on a six- to ten-day cycle, in one pass, with music on. Cleaning is not therapeutic for him; it is inspection. He is checking the spaces while wiping them.

---

### 6.3 The Driver-Day (616, Reformative Era)

The Uber/app-driving cover is not purely cover. It is also the architecture of his attempt to live straight, and the structure deserves logging in its own right.

- **Shifts 0900–1400 and 1900–2300, five to six days a week.** He skips the morning rush because he hates being yelled at by people late for work and because predictable bridge-and-tunnel routes bore him. He prefers midday airport runs (long fares, low conversation expectation) and late-evening Manhattan-to-outer-borough runs (good money, quiet passengers).
- **The car is meticulously clean.** Floor mats shaken weekly. Water bottles in the seatback. Phone charger of every common type. He keeps the rating above 4.9 deliberately — a low rating draws attention, and attention is the enemy of a man with a record. The high rating is camouflage.
- **He does not talk unless talked to first.** When a passenger initiates, he is warm, brief, funny on demand, and forgets the conversation by the next pickup. He has a small repertoire of safe topics: weather, the Knicks, the route. He does not discuss politics, family, neighborhoods he has lived in, or anything that could be triangulated later.
- **He keeps a notebook in the glove box.** Not a journal — a log. Mileage, expenses, a few names. The notebook is for the IRS, which he now genuinely fears, because the legitimate life has its own predators.
- **Between fares he parks rather than circles.** Circling burns gas and broadcasts his location; parking lets him watch a block, eat, text Miles, nap. He has three preferred parking nooks in Brooklyn and two in lower Manhattan, rotated by day of week.

The driver-life is not happy work for him. He does it because it generates verifiable income and because moving through the city in a vehicle satisfies the part of his nervous system that needs constant low-grade situational awareness. He is, while driving, doing the same scanning he did as a thief, monetized.

---

### 6.4 The Thief-Day (Ultimate-Era, and Relapse Episodes in 616)

On an active-job day the entire schedule re-orients around the window of execution. Logging the architecture:

- **Reconnaissance is done in daylight, in civilian clothes, on foot or by transit.** He has walked past targets three to six times before any approach. He prefers to make the first pass at a different hour from the eventual hit — to see the building's other face.
- **He carries a coffee on recon.** The cup is a prop. It explains why he is standing still. He has used the same brand of paper cup so often it constitutes a small but real forensic risk that he does not appear to have noticed.
- **Pre-job afternoon: the long nap, then a meal.** The pre-job meal is the largest meal of his day and is always carbohydrate-heavy. He eats it alone, usually at a counter, often Chinese or a bodega sandwich. He does not eat anything new before a job. Novelty is a variable; jobs require constants.
- **Gear-up is a 20- to 30-minute sequence, alone, with music off.** Order is invariant: under-layer, boots, harness, gauntlets-last. The gauntlets going on are the threshold ritual; once they are on, he is in operational mind, and he does not speak unless tactically necessary. He has been observed mouthing what may be a count or may be a prayer immediately before pulling the mask down. The published record does not resolve which.
- **Approach, execution, exfil.** He prefers rooftops to streets, service entries to lobbies, and stairwells to elevators in flight. He does not use the same egress as his ingress when avoidable.
- **Post-job decompression is rigid.** He returns to a location that is *not* his residence first — a stash spot, a car, a 24-hour diner — and waits a minimum of an hour before going home. He eats during this window, usually something hot, usually alone, and he does not speak. The post-job hour is when he is closest to a contemplative state; if he were ever going to journal or pray, it would be then. He does neither, on record. He simply sits.
- **Sleep after a job is poor.** He goes down hard but wakes inside two hours, usually once, sometimes twice. The long block is broken. The body knows.

---

### 6.5 The Miles-Day

When Miles is the day's organizing event — and across both continuities, Miles-days are the days Aaron most carefully orchestrates — the schedule is different in kind.

- **Aaron over-prepares.** He scouts the venue. He picks the restaurant in advance, often two days in advance. He arrives early and is already seated when Miles walks in. He has chosen a seat with sightlines to the door — this is operational habit, not performance — but he has also chosen the seat that gives Miles the better view of the room. He thinks about Miles's comfort in granular terms he would not extend to anyone else.
- **He buys something.** Almost every Miles-encounter on record involves a gift, a meal paid for, a piece of gear handed over, or an offered ride. The gift is the language. He does not know how to be present without a tendered object. This is legible against the attachment formulation in §3: he upregulates connection through transaction because he was not taught any other channel.
- **He uses humor at a higher density than in any other context.** Miles is the only person on record who consistently makes Aaron laugh, and Aaron is performatively funnier around Miles than around anyone else, including women he is trying to bed. The humor is partly genuine pleasure and partly a management strategy — keeping the conversation light keeps it from going to the topics he cannot survive (Jefferson, the past, what he actually does for money).
- **He watches Miles eat.** This is a behavior worth flagging in its own right. He himself eats less when with Miles; his attention is on the boy. He does not interrupt, does not rush, and is the first to refill the water glass. The pattern is parental in a way Aaron has no other outlet for. It is also, given the formulation, the closest Aaron gets to direct caregiving uncomplicated by leverage.
- **He lies frequently and casually about small things.** Where he was last week. Why he was late. Whose number that was. The lying is not strategic in these moments; it is reflexive, and he often forgets the lie within hours, which creates the slow consistency-erosion that Miles eventually notices.
- **The goodbye is the hardest part of the encounter.** He prolongs it — a walk to the train, an extra block, one more thing he wanted to say. The reluctance to terminate the contact is the most undefended affect in his entire week.

---

### 6.6 Habits of Place

He has territory. A surveillance week would map it.

- **A diner — booth in the back, faces the door.** He eats there one to three times a week, almost always alone, sometimes with a contact. The waitstaff know his order; he tips in cash, heavy.
- **A barber — every two and a half weeks, same chair if possible.** The fade is maintained tightly; the beard is shaped, never bushy. Grooming is high-priority across both continuities and across all financial states. He will skip a meal before he will skip the barber.
- **A bodega for cigarettes (occasional, social) and for lottery tickets (regular, ritualized rather than hopeful — he buys one Powerball a week, scratches it that night, throws it out).** The lottery purchase is interesting: a man whose entire trade is the manipulation of probability nonetheless performs this small surrender to chance once a week. It is the only luck-based act in his routine.
- **A gym, off-hours.** He trains alone, weights and bag work, no classes, no trainer, no app. Two to four sessions a week. He does not run outdoors — too visible, and bad on the knees that have taken a decade of rooftop landings.
- **A bar he goes to but does not drink seriously in.** One or two beers, conversation, leaves before close. He is not a closer of bars. Drunk is a state he cannot afford.
- **Rooftops.** Across both continuities, when distressed, he goes up. Not to jump, not to brood — to *sit*. The roof is his thinking-place. A surveillance team would lose him on roofs more often than on streets.

---

### 6.7 Habits of Time

- **He is early to everything that matters and late to everything that does not.** Earliness is operational; lateness is contempt or indifference. The asymmetry is diagnostic.
- **He checks the time on a wristwatch, not a phone.** Across both continuities, an analog watch is present on his wrist in the majority of panels. The watch is also a tell: he taps the face twice when impatient, a gesture so consistent it could be used to identify him in silhouette.
- **He has a Sunday.** Sundays are softer in both eras: later wake, longer breakfast, the only day he is reliably reachable by family-frame contacts. He treats Sunday as a kind of secular sabbath despite no observable religious practice. The origin is likely childhood — a Davis-family Sunday rhythm Jefferson presumably also kept — and Aaron retains it without acknowledging why.
- **Birthdays and holidays produce dysregulation.** He is observably worse on these days — drinks slightly more, jokes more sharply, makes contact attempts at odd hours. Christmas and Miles's birthday are the highest-load dates. Jefferson's birthday, if it can be identified from the record, is the date he is most likely to be alone and most likely to be unreachable.

---

### 6.8 Micro-Patterns, Tics, and Tells

A surveillance file should log the body. The following are repeat observations.

- **The double-tap on the watch face.** Impatience or low-grade anxiety.
- **The blind-crack at the window on entering any room with a window.** Habituated; unconscious.
- **The seat-with-sightlines choice in any room he enters.** He will move chairs if necessary, smoothly, framed as preference.
- **A slow exhale through the nose before saying something difficult.** The tell precedes every consequential disclosure on record.
- **A specific half-smile, mouth closed, when being lied to.** He registers deception faster than civilians and does not always conceal that he has registered it. The half-smile is the leak.
- **He touches the back of his neck when Jefferson is mentioned.** Soothing self-touch, brief, repeatable.
- **He does not initiate physical contact with adults.** Handshakes when offered; nothing offered first. With Miles he is the initiator — a hand on the shoulder, a one-arm hug, a knuckle to the chest. The asymmetry of touch-initiation is itself a map of who is inside the perimeter.
- **He whistles when working alone.** Quietly, no consistent tune. It stops the instant he is observed.
- **He carries cash in two locations on his person.** Wallet and a folded reserve in a sock or inner pocket. Old habit, never dropped.
- **He does not drink water from open containers he did not see poured.** A trade hygiene that has survived into a life that no longer requires it.

---

### 6.9 The Week, Compressed

If a surveillance team filed a seven-day summary, the report would read:

> *Subject maintains a stable daily architecture organized around two work blocks (driving, mid-morning and evening) and one private block (late afternoon, used for rest and personal errands). Sleeps short and split. Eats lightly in the morning, heavily once in the afternoon. Maintains rigorous grooming and gym routine. Three to five solo meals at known locations. One to two contacts per week with the nephew, M. Davis, prioritized over all other appointments and prepared for with disproportionate care. No observed romantic partner of duration during the reporting window. No religious observance. No documented substance issue. Equipment access maintained in residence despite stated cessation of criminal activity. Subject's routine is the routine of a man holding two lives in tension: the constructed civilian schedule sits cleanly on top of a deeper operational schedule that has not been decommissioned, only paused. Subject can return to active work within a single sleep cycle. Recommend continued passive observation; tripwires on the gear-cache and on the nephew.*

The dossier reads, accurately, as a man living the cover story he wants to be true while keeping the originals in the closet. The routines are real. The rituals are real. The closet is also real. None of these facts contradict any of the others, and the day-to-day of Aaron Davis is the steady, observable proof that he is, in the working hours of his life, exactly the man he is trying to become — and, in the four hours before dawn, still the man he was.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## SECTION 6 — RELATIONSHIPS I: FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Cross-continuity synthesis. Ultimate (Earth-1610) and 616 records treated as parallel admissible biographies of the same psychological subject; divergences flagged where they illuminate structure rather than contradict it. The family map is small. That smallness is itself diagnostic: Aaron Davis has fewer durable kin attachments at age forty-plus than most operators in his risk band, and the few he has carry the entire weight of his interior life.*

---

### 6.1 JEFFERSON DAVIS — Younger Brother (Estranged → Posthumously Reckoned With)

**The structural relationship of Aaron's entire adult life.** Every other bond in this file is, at some level of remove, a workaround for the absence of this one. Map Jefferson correctly and the rest of the file resolves.

**Origin.** Two boys, raised in the same household, in conditions of environmental violence (the published record is deliberately vague about parental composition - see §6.4 - but consistent about the neighborhood substrate). Aaron is the elder by a margin sufficient to have functioned as a protector-figure in childhood. There is recurrent evidence in Bendis's flashback work and Ahmed's expanded 616 backstory that young Aaron took hits intended for Jefferson, ran interference with adults, and modeled the older-brother-as-shield role with some genuine competence before he learned to monetize the same skills. This is critical: Jefferson's later rejection lands so hard because it is the repudiation of a role Aaron had been performing, with some success, since before he could articulate why.

**The Pivot Event.** A joint robbery in young adulthood. Details vary slightly across continuities but the structural beats are stable: the brothers commit a crime together, a death (or near-death) of a bystander occurs, the brothers escape, and in the aftermath Jefferson goes one way (legitimacy - eventually police work in 616, straight life and the Davis household in Ultimate) and Aaron goes the other (deeper into the craft). The decisive moment is not the crime; it is what Jefferson says or does in the hours and days after. The published record implies Jefferson assigned Aaron the blame - older brother, instigator, the one who "made" him do it - and Aaron, who carries the protector-imprint, did not fully contest the attribution. He accepted the role of the one who had ruined them both, and accepted the consequence: excommunication.

**The Erasure.** Jefferson's response is not estrangement in the ordinary sense - cooled relations, missed holidays, eventual reconciliation. It is *ontological denial*. Jefferson removes Aaron from the family narrative so completely that his own son grows up not knowing Aaron exists. This is the wound the entire dossier is organized around. It is not that the brother left; it is that the brother *unmade* him. For a man whose self-concept was load-bearing on being someone's older brother, this is an annihilating verdict, and Aaron - tellingly - never tries to contest it on its merits. He does not show up at Jefferson's door demanding rehearing. He absorbs the verdict and routes around it.

**Adult Dynamic (Ultimate).** Functionally none. Aaron and Jefferson do not share frame in the Ultimate run during Aaron's lifetime. The only "contact" is asymmetric and covert: Aaron knows where Jefferson lives, knows about Miles, has presumably surveilled the family for years before the spider-incident gives him pretext to surface. This is not stalking in the predatory sense; it is the behavior of a man who cannot bear to be in the room and also cannot bear not to know. He keeps tabs the way bereaved relatives keep tabs on cemeteries.

**Adult Dynamic (616).** Marginally more accessible because the timelines collapse and Aaron is given a rehabilitation arc, but the substance is the same. Even when Aaron is alive, sober-adjacent, and trying, he and Jefferson do not meaningfully repair. The few on-panel interactions are guarded, ritualized, and short. Jefferson's police-officer identity in 616 adds an institutional layer to a personal estrangement; the brother is now also the badge. Aaron's interpretive frame for this is, characteristically, ironic - the brother became the thing that hunts him - but the irony is a thin cover for grief.

**Trust / Safety.** Asymmetric to the point of vacuum. Aaron trusts Jefferson absolutely in the abstract - would not, in any plausible reading, betray him to harm - and not at all in the concrete, because he has no template for what a real conversation with Jefferson would look like. Jefferson does not trust Aaron at all, and Aaron has internalized this assessment so completely that he treats it as physics. He does not test it. The relationship is in a kind of permanent stasis-of-verdict.

**Failure Mode.** Aaron's relationship to Jefferson fails by *displacement*. Unable to address Jefferson directly, Aaron addresses every adjacent target: Miles (as proxy son and proxy younger brother both), his own criminal craft (as the proof Jefferson was wrong about him, or as the confirmation Jefferson was right - the same evidence serves both readings, which is why Aaron cannot stop producing it), and his own death-by-equipment in the Ultimate arc (which is legible as a final unconscious letter to a brother who will not read it). The mode of failure is that Aaron never sends the letter directly. He spends his adult life writing drafts.

**Leverage.** Catastrophic. The single highest-yield lever against Aaron Davis is anything that touches the Jefferson wound. A hostile actor who understood the file - the Assessor in 616 approximates this without ever quite naming it - could move Aaron toward almost any operational outcome by structuring the choice around brother-shame or brother-protection. Conversely, a benevolent actor (and Jefferson himself, had he ever chosen to use it) could move Aaron toward reform with a single sustained gesture of re-recognition. Neither continuity grants Jefferson the imagination to try.

**Diagnostic note.** Aaron's affect leaks most reliably when Jefferson is invoked obliquely. He can hear his brother named directly and hold his face; he cannot hear a stranger say *"a man like that wouldn't even know his own family"* without something behind the eyes shifting. The oblique reference bypasses the prepared defense. Surveillance teams should note: indirect invocation is the diagnostic instrument; direct invocation is the prepared performance.

---

### 6.2 MILES MORALES — Nephew (The Entire Attachment Budget)

**The relationship that carries everything Jefferson refused to carry.** Aaron does not have a son. He has, instead, a nephew who functions as son, as proxy-Jefferson, as proxy-younger-Aaron, and as the live audience for a redemption performance whose primary intended viewer is dead-to-him. Miles is asked, structurally, to be four people at once. He is twelve to fifteen years old across the relevant arc and does not know this is being asked of him.

**Initiation.** Aaron discovers Miles before Miles discovers Aaron. The Oscorp break-in that releases the spider is Aaron's job; when the powers manifest in his nephew, Aaron is the only adult in the world positioned to trace the causal line from his own crime to his nephew's body. He does the trace. The first contact is therefore not a chance reunion; it is an *investigated* reunion. Aaron walks into Miles's life having already done the homework. The boy never knows this. The asymmetry of information is the foundation of the relationship and never resolves.

**Operational Modes (concurrent, not sequential).**

- **The Cool Uncle.** Aaron buys Miles things Jefferson cannot or will not - sneakers, electronics, the small dignities of being treated as nearly-adult. Takes him places. Speaks to him without the parental edge. This mode is sincere. Aaron enjoys Miles's company without instrumentalizing it in the moment; the affection is real and the boy correctly reads it as real. If only this mode existed, Aaron would be a net good in Miles's life.
- **The Mentor.** Aaron is the only adult who treats the powers as a gift. Jefferson, in both continuities, has a structural objection to costumed activity; the family frame is *don't*. Aaron's frame is *let me show you how*. He offers technique - movement, situational awareness, how to read a room before entering it, how to make an exit before you need one. The mentorship is, on its own merits, *useful*. Miles is a better Spider-Man for having had it. This is the genuinely tragic dimension of Aaron: he is good at being an uncle, in the narrow sense of having something to teach a young man that the young man cannot get elsewhere.
- **The Handler.** Aaron uses Miles as muscle on jobs. Threatens to expose the Spider-Man identity to Jefferson if Miles refuses. Frames the coercion as bonding (*"we're a team now"*) and the exposure-threat as protection (*"I'm just keeping us safe"*). This mode is also sincere - Aaron does not experience himself as a villain in it - but it is the mode that destroys the relationship in the Ultimate arc and nearly destroys it in 616.

**The three modes coexist.** This is the most important behavioral fact in the entire Miles relationship. Aaron does not "turn" from cool uncle into handler; he is both, simultaneously, often within a single scene. He can buy a meal in genuine pleasure and across the same table issue a leverage-threat in genuine concern. He experiences no internal contradiction. The splitting (§3) is what permits this: Miles-as-kin and Miles-as-asset are stored as separate representations and Aaron can flip between them faster than the boy can track.

**The Boy's Read.** Miles is unusually emotionally literate for his age and reads Aaron more accurately than Aaron reads himself. The boy figures out, eventually, that the warmth is real *and* that the coercion is real *and* that both come from the same person. The intolerability of this knowledge is what drives Miles's refusal in the late Ultimate arc - not that he stops loving the uncle, but that he stops being able to absorb the contradiction. Aaron, who has never had this knowledge held up to him, experiences the refusal as betrayal rather than as accurate assessment.

**Trust / Safety.** Mutually high in the first arc, asymmetrically destroyed in the second, partially rebuilt in 616. Miles will let Aaron close to him physically (combat-close, training-close, sit-on-the-same-couch close) past the point where he should. Aaron, for his part, would absolutely take damage for Miles - this is uncontested across both continuities - and yet *causes* damage to Miles through the leverage-pattern. The safety violation is never the kind a surveillance file expects (Aaron does not strike the boy, does not endanger him gratuitously); it is the subtler harm of asking a child to carry an adult's unresolved sibling material.

**Failure Mode (Ultimate).** Terminal. Aaron coerces, Miles refuses, the confrontation escalates, the gauntlets malfunction, Aaron dies. The relationship ends with the boy watching his uncle die in equipment Aaron knew was unsafe. Miles's subsequent Spider-Man career is shaped by this scene in ways the boy himself takes years to process. From Aaron's side: he dies having confirmed Jefferson's verdict in front of the one witness whose opinion he actually wanted.

**Failure Mode (616).** Non-terminal but recurrent. Aaron relapses, Miles is hurt (emotionally, not yet fatally), Aaron self-recriminates, Miles forgives within limits, the cycle resets at lower amplitude. The 616 arc is the rehabilitative case because the cycle's amplitude is decreasing rather than increasing. This is the closest Aaron comes in either continuity to actual reform: a series of smaller failures within a relationship that survives them.

**Leverage.** Through Miles to Aaron: total. Anyone who can credibly threaten the boy moves Aaron immediately, without reference to self-interest, often against operational sense. The Assessor's hold in 616 partly works this way. Through Aaron to Miles: high but bounded. Aaron can extract operational compliance from Miles via shame and exposure-threat in the short term; he cannot extract identity-level commitment, and his attempts to do so are what burn the trust.

**Diagnostic note.** Aaron's voice changes when speaking to Miles. Lower register, slower cadence, fewer hedges. The accent he otherwise modulates situationally (see §8 when compiled) becomes more consistent - he is not performing for Miles in the way he performs for adults. This is the somatic signature of the attachment being online. When Aaron is speaking to Miles in the operational/handler register, the voice does not drop; it stays at adult-room frequency. The vocal register is therefore a real-time diagnostic of which Miles-representation is active in Aaron's head at any moment.

---

### 6.3 RIO MORALES — Sister-in-Law (Distant, Respected, Avoided)

**The relationship Aaron most carefully manages and least frequently engages.** Rio is Jefferson's wife, Miles's mother, and - in Aaron's interior schema - the woman who agreed to the erasure. She did not invent the verdict but she ratified it by raising Miles without him. Aaron's posture toward Rio is therefore complex: he does not blame her (he has too clear an understanding of the marital dynamic for that), he respects her (the published record consistently shows Rio as a woman of substantial moral seriousness, and Aaron registers this), and he avoids her (because being in her presence is being in the presence of the household he was not in).

**Direct contact.** Minimal in both continuities. Aaron does not visit the Davis-Morales apartment in any sustained way; what contact occurs is incidental, often awkward, and short. Rio's read of Aaron is wary-civil; she does not perform warmth she does not feel, and she does not feel warmth toward the man who has, in her assessment, been an intermittent disruption in her son's life.

**Trust / Safety.** Rio does not trust Aaron and is correct not to. Aaron does not, on the available record, harbor hostility toward Rio; if anything, he carries a quiet admiration for her management of a household he could not have built. The asymmetry - she sees him as a threat, he sees her as a competence - is stable and probably correct on both sides.

**Failure Mode.** The relationship cannot fail because it has never been built. Its failure is its non-existence. The cost of the non-existence accrues to Aaron, not to Rio: he has no female adult kin-figure in his life, no counterweight to the all-male Davis-brother dynamic, no one in the family who might have brokered a partial reconciliation. Rio could have been that broker in another timeline and is not in this one.

**Leverage.** Indirect but high. Harm to Rio would move Aaron operationally not through love but through Miles - he understands that the boy without his mother is a catastrophe he is unequipped to mitigate. Aaron's protective instincts toward Rio are therefore best modeled as derived rather than primary.

**Diagnostic note.** Aaron's body language in Rio's presence is the most constrained the file records. He does not occupy space the way he does elsewhere; shoulders narrow, hands visible, voice quieter. This is the posture of a man in a house he has been told he does not belong in, even when no one in the room is currently telling him so.

---

### 6.4 THE PARENTS — Off-Panel, Inferred

**The most consequential absence in the file.** The Davis brothers' parents are functionally unrepresented in the published record. There are oblique references - a mother invoked in passing, a father whose presence or absence shapes the household violence Aaron grew up in - but no sustained portraiture. For a UATU file, the absence is itself data: whatever happened in that household, neither brother talks about it in any frame the reader is given access to. Both brothers have constructed adult lives that route around the parental material rather than through it.

**Inferred profile.** From the behavioral residue:
- At least one parental figure modeled either violence or its proximity, such that both sons came of age treating environmental violence as a baseline condition rather than an exceptional one.
- Some parental structure rewarded Jefferson's eventual move toward legitimacy and either failed to deter or actively shaped Aaron's move away from it. The differential outcome between two brothers in the same household is not random; it reflects either temperamental difference amplified by differential parental response, or - more likely - role-allocation within the family system (the "good son" and the "bad son" as complementary positions, often assigned before the children have any input).
- Aaron's protector-imprint toward Jefferson (§6.1) implies that the parental shield function was, at minimum, inadequate. Aaron took the role because no one else was taking it. Children who fill that role consistently across childhood develop the dismissive-avoidant attachment profile Aaron displays as an adult: self-sufficient because no one was ever sufficient for them.

**Death / current status.** The published record does not establish parental status with certainty in either continuity. The functional reading is that the parents are either deceased or so peripheral to the brothers' adult lives that they constitute a posthumous-equivalent absence. Aaron does not visit, does not call, does not invoke. Neither does Jefferson.

**Trust / Safety / Failure / Leverage.** Not assessable from positive evidence. The leverage profile is therefore *negative*: the parents cannot be used against Aaron because he has already done the work of making them inaccessible to himself. Whatever wound exists has been sealed under thick scar tissue, and the seal is the load-bearing element. An interrogator who tried to pry it would likely find Aaron more genuinely dangerous than under any other pressure - not because the material is hot but because the seal is.

**Diagnostic note.** Listen for what Aaron *does not* say. In hours of recorded dialogue across two continuities he does not narrate childhood scenes with parental figures present. The narrative time-horizon of his self-disclosure begins, effectively, with the brother-relationship and the early adult crime. Everything before that is sealed. This is a tell.

---

### 6.5 THE DEAD — The Bystander From the Pivot Robbery

**The unnamed casualty of the brothers' founding crime.** The published record handles this figure with variable specificity across continuities, but the structural function is constant: a person was hurt or killed in the robbery that ended the brothers' partnership, and that person is the silent third party in every subsequent Davis-family interaction. Jefferson carries the death as the reason he became a cop (in 616) or the reason he left the life (in Ultimate). Aaron carries it differently - not as motivating reform but as *confirmed cost*, the price already paid that makes further crime feel, in a particular self-defeating accounting, free. *I have already paid for the worst thing I will do; everything since is on credit.*

**Trust / Safety / Failure.** Not applicable in the conventional sense. The relevant question is whether the dead figure functions as conscience or as license in Aaron's interior. The honest read is: both, depending on the day. In his lower moments the dead person is invoked (silently, never on-panel) as justification for the next job - *what would it matter now*. In his higher moments the same figure is the floor he tries not to break through again - the trafficking and child-endangerment red lines (§5, "Pressure points") almost certainly derive their force from this foundational casualty. Aaron will not be the man who creates another one of those, even when he will be many other kinds of bad man.

**Leverage.** Substantial for an operator who knew the specifics. The full identification of the bystander, surfaced at the right moment in the right voice, would be the single most destabilizing piece of biographical material that could be presented to Aaron Davis short of harm to Miles. No on-panel antagonist has yet deployed it. The Assessor's leverage in 616 stops short of this depth. The fact that it has not been deployed should not be read as evidence that it could not be.

**Diagnostic note.** Aaron does not visit graves. Across both continuities, there is no scene of him at any memorial site for anyone. This is consistent with a man who manages the dead by refusing to acknowledge them spatially - if he never stands at the marker, the death has not been formally entered into the ledger. The refusal is itself the entry.

---

### 6.6 SYNTHESIS — THE FAMILY MAP AS DIAGNOSTIC OBJECT

Five nodes, four of them damaged or absent. The map shows a man whose attachment system is *configured* - he can love, he does love - but whose attachment field has been progressively narrowed by loss and self-exile until only one live wire remains. That wire is Miles. Everything Aaron Davis has not been able to give Jefferson, has not been allowed to give Rio, was not given by his parents, and could not give back to the bystander he helped kill, he tries to route through a teenage nephew who did not ask to be the entire emotional infrastructure of a forty-year-old criminal's interior life.

The boy carries it better than anyone should have to. The man carries it worse than he should have to. The brother, who could relieve both of them with a sustained gesture, does not. This is the family.

A surveillance file built for harm would note: cut the Miles wire and Aaron Davis becomes operationally unpredictable in ways that endanger everyone in his radius, himself first.

A file built for understanding - this one - notes the same fact and draws the inverse operational conclusion: *protect the Miles wire and the man stays inside the perimeter of his own better self.* The Ultimate timeline is what happens when no one protects it. The 616 timeline is what happens when, intermittently and imperfectly, someone does.

The difference between the two timelines is not Aaron. The difference is whether the family, in any of its surviving members, chose to keep him in the frame.

*End Section 6. Continues §7 — Relationships II: Criminal Network, Handlers, and Antagonists.*


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 7 — Relationships II: Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

*Compiled from longitudinal behavioral record. The category is unusually thin for a man of his tenure in the profession - a diagnostic finding in itself. Aaron Davis has operated in New York's criminal ecology for the better part of two decades and has accumulated approximately the chosen-family network of a man halfway through his first year in a new city. The sparseness is not accident; it is the structural consequence of the brother-wound documented in Section 1. He does not let people close, because the one person who was let close left. What follows is the entire roster, exhaustively mapped - including the marginal cases, the ambiguous ones, and the negative-space relationships (people who could have become allies and were systematically prevented from doing so).*

---

### 7.1 — MILES MORALES (Nephew; Primary Attachment Object; Reluctant Protégé)

*Cross-referenced with Section 6 (Family / Blood) and Section 9 (Operational Counterparties). Listed here because the relationship occupies all three categories simultaneously and because, in the chosen-family sense, Miles is the only person Aaron has ever volunteered into his interior life. Jefferson was given; Miles was chosen.*

**History.** Aaron first becomes aware of Miles as a target of opportunity rather than as kin - he is mid-burglary at an Oscorp facility when the spider escapes, and he reconstructs only later (across the back half of *Ultimate Comics Spider-Man*) that the spider's eventual host is his own nephew. The moment of recognition is, behaviorally, the most consequential single event in his adult life. Surveillance posture afterward shifts immediately: he goes from being a man with no documented interest in his brother's domestic life to a man who knows Miles's school schedule, his route home, the window of his bedroom, the cadence of his patrols. This is not stalking in the predatory register; it is the only language Aaron has for *paying attention to someone*. He converts care into reconnaissance because reconnaissance is what he knows how to do.

**Dynamics across phases.** Three distinct phases in Ultimate, a fourth and fifth in 616.

*Phase I — the indulgent uncle (early Ultimate appearances).* Aaron presents as the relative Jefferson refused to be: relaxed, generous, unembarrassed by Miles's adolescence. Buys him the things, takes him to the places, validates the powers Jefferson treats as a problem. The warmth here is real. It is not a long con; it is a man who has finally found someone who looks at him without the verdict in their eyes. Behavioral tell: in this phase Aaron laughs unguardedly, the only adult-context laughter on record without a tactical edge.

*Phase II — the mentor (mid Ultimate).* Begins teaching Miles the *use* of his powers in a way Spider-Man-the-original never had time to. Combat geometry, building entry, how to read a room before walking into it. The tutorials are competent and, in isolation, beneficial - Miles's tradecraft improvements during this period are demonstrably Aaron-derived. The shadow inside the gift: every lesson is also a job-pitch in slow motion. He is grooming a partner while telling himself he is uplifting a relative.

*Phase III — the handler (late Ultimate).* The mask slips when Aaron leverages Miles into the Scorpion confrontation, threatening exposure to Jefferson as the lever. This is the phase where the splitting documented in Section 3 becomes intolerable; the two representations of Miles (kin-equal, asset) cannot share a frame, so Aaron alternates within minutes, sometimes within sentences. Ends in Aaron's death by gauntlet malfunction - which, read against his stress-pathway profile, is partly the suicidal-by-recklessness terminus a man takes when he has confirmed Jefferson's verdict in front of Jefferson's son.

*Phase IV — the returned, repentant uncle (early 616 / Ahmed).* Restored alive in consolidated continuity, Aaron approaches Miles from a different posture: hands visible, no pitch, low ask. The reform is real but technique-poor; he does not know how to be a relative without an angle, so he overcorrects into gentleness so emphatic it reads as performance even when sincere. Miles, for his part, holds him at a measured distance that Aaron tolerates well - one of the few signs of genuine maturation in the 616 arc is Aaron's increased ability to *be patient with being mistrusted*.

*Phase V — the back-slid, re-attempting uncle.* The Assessor leverages him, the criminal pulls return, the trafficking-adjacent plots ensnare him; he relapses and then surfaces, confesses, fights his way back into Miles's regard. The 616 record is the rehabilitation case. The arc is not linear and is not finished.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric in both directions. Miles trusts Aaron's love and distrusts his judgment - an accurate calibration. Aaron trusts Miles in a way he trusts no one else and is also more dangerous to Miles than anyone else because his coercion-as-affection schema discharges into the relationship under stress. Safety is highest when stakes are low (a meal, a drive, a sidewalk conversation) and degrades steeply once operational pressure enters the frame. Miles is physically safer in Aaron's company than almost anywhere else when no one is looking for either of them; psychologically he is most at risk in precisely those moments when Aaron's anxiety about losing him spikes.

**Failure mode.** Aaron, feeling the relationship slip, tightens through leverage. The tightening is the loosening. He does not learn this in Ultimate; he learns it slowly and incompletely in 616. The failure mode is recursive: every attempt to secure the bond by force degrades it, which raises anxiety, which prompts more force.

**Leverage on Aaron via Miles.** Total. Miles's disapproval is the only operationally reliable lever in Aaron's psychology. Threats to Miles produce the override behavior noted in Section 5 - he becomes unpredictable in ways that violate self-interest. Anyone who has identified the link and weaponized it (Scorpion, Assessor in moments) has been able to move Aaron significantly; anyone who has tried to *acquire* Aaron via that link has discovered it also makes him a profoundly unreliable asset, because the same lever that compels his cooperation guarantees his eventual betrayal of whoever is pulling it.

**Leverage on Miles via Aaron.** Significant and increasingly central to Miles's enemies' targeting calculus in the 616 era. Aaron knows the identity, knows the family, knows the home. He is also a person Miles will not, on principle, allow to be killed in front of him. That immovability is exploitable.

---

### 7.2 — GANKE LEE (Adjacent; Through-Miles; Acknowledged but Not Engaged)

*Catalogued for completeness. The relationship is real in the sense that both parties know of each other and have shared physical space; it is non-relational in the sense that Aaron has made no investment in it and Ganke has, sensibly, kept his distance.*

**History.** Ganke knows Miles's full Spider-Man situation including Uncle Aaron's reentry; Aaron knows of Ganke as Miles's confidant and roommate. They occupy the same operational triangle around Miles without forming a dyadic relationship of their own.

**Dynamics.** Aaron's posture toward Ganke is the watchful courtesy he extends to anyone in Miles's perimeter whom he has assessed as non-hostile and non-useful. He is unfailingly polite. He remembers the kid's name. He does not invest. Ganke, who is shrewd in his own register, reads Aaron exactly correctly - dangerous, sincere about Miles, not a person to befriend - and reciprocates the polite distance. Diagnostic detail: Aaron has, on at least one occasion in the Ahmed run's domestic interludes, brought food sufficient for both Miles and Ganke without making it a moment. The small generosity is unforced. It is also the upper bound of his investment.

**Trust / safety.** Functional. Aaron will not harm Ganke and will, by transitive property of Miles, protect him at meaningful personal cost if required. He will not, however, confide in him, recruit him, or treat him as a peer-level node in his network.

**Failure mode.** None active. Latent failure mode: if Aaron's criminal life imports threats into Miles's apartment and Ganke is collateral, Aaron's response would be guilt-driven over-correction, possibly escalatory, possibly self-destructive. He has not been pressure-tested on this and the file flags it as a high-impact unknown.

**Leverage.** Ganke is not currently weaponizable against Aaron in any direct sense; he is weaponizable as a proxy hostage in the Miles-perimeter scheme that any sophisticated adversary would build.

---

### 7.3 — RIO MORALES (Sister-in-Law; Cautiously Re-Admitted Kin)

*Listed under chosen family rather than blood: in the 616 reform arc, Rio's willingness to entertain Aaron's presence in the household, against Jefferson's reservations, constitutes an act of elective inclusion that Aaron experiences as chosen-family ratification.*

**History.** In the Ultimate continuity, Rio's exposure to Aaron is minimal and largely filtered through Jefferson's hostility; she dies before the relationship can mature. In the 616 continuity she lives, and her relationship to Aaron is the most consequential adult ratification of his reform attempt that he receives from anyone other than Miles. Where Jefferson is the wall, Rio is the door left slightly ajar.

**Dynamics.** Aaron in Rio's presence performs his best self with unusual sincerity - not the operator's charm but a quieter, more deferential register, the posture of a man who knows he is on probation in a kitchen that is not his. He addresses her formally, accepts food, does not overstay, does not bring trouble across the threshold (with the catastrophic exceptions of the plots that follow him in anyway). She, for her part, extends the maternal even-handedness that defines her in the Ahmed run: neither absolving him nor closing the door, naming his behaviors when she has to, allowing him repair-space when he earns it.

**Trust / safety.** Modest and growing on her side; high and load-bearing on his. Aaron treats Rio's continued tolerance as evidence that the reform is possible, which means any withdrawal of her tolerance would be devastating in proportion to how much he has invested in her ratification. This is a vulnerability he has not flagged to himself.

**Failure mode.** Aaron's criminal life intrudes on the household, Rio's safety is endangered, Jefferson's worst predictions are validated. Aaron's response under this scenario is collapse-and-confess (per Section 5) rather than evasion - which is, paradoxically, the response most likely to preserve the relationship long-term, though it will not preserve the household-access in the short term.

**Leverage.** Rio is not exploitable against Aaron by adversaries unless they understand the family map in unusual depth, but the family map is increasingly legible to sophisticated opponents. Her safety is, after Miles's, the second-most-effective lever on him.

---

### 7.4 — JEFFERSON DAVIS (Brother; Estranged; The Negative Space of the Whole File)

*Catalogued here, not in Section 6, by a deliberate analytic choice: Jefferson functions in Aaron's interior life less as a sibling than as the audience-of-one for whom Aaron's entire adult performance is staged. He is the addressee. Every act of reform, every act of regression, every move toward and away from Miles is, at the metabolic level, a message Aaron is writing to a brother who is not reading. This is the closest thing to a mentor relationship in Aaron's life - a permanently absent mentor whose verdict structures every choice.*

**History.** The shared origin event - the early-adulthood robbery in which a death occurred (or nearly did) - terminated the relationship and inaugurated Aaron's adult solitude. Jefferson did not merely break contact; he erased Aaron from the family narrative so completely that Miles grew up not knowing the uncle existed. This is the cardinal datum. It is not estrangement; it is excommunication with a memory-hole component, and Aaron has lived inside the shape of that erasure for the entire span of the file.

**Dynamics.** On the rare on-panel encounters in both continuities, Aaron presents to Jefferson in a register he uses for no one else: defensive-bantering, prematurely sarcastic, trying to land the first joke so the first wound will be his to inflict. Jefferson's affect toward Aaron oscillates between cold competence and brief unguarded grief - the latter the most diagnostically important, because Aaron almost certainly does not know it is there. The brothers cannot speak to each other directly; they speak past each other and around the room.

**Trust / safety.** Inverse of every other relationship in this file. Aaron trusts Jefferson absolutely - in the sense that he believes Jefferson would not harm him for sport, would not hand him to police casually, would protect him if a hostile party closed on him in Jefferson's presence - and Jefferson trusts Aaron not at all. The asymmetry is the relationship.

**Failure mode.** Already failed and ongoing. The failure mode of the brother-bond was crystallized decades ago and the relationship now consists entirely of managing the failure.

**Leverage.** Aaron's avoidance of repair conversations with Jefferson is, per Section 3, the structuring avoidance of his adult life. Any actor who could credibly broker a real Jefferson-Aaron conversation would acquire enormous influence over Aaron, more than Miles's disapproval generates, because it would touch the wound itself rather than the proxy. No such actor exists in the present record. Miles, if he matured into it, could become that broker; Rio is the only other candidate.

---

### 7.5 — THE FENCE NETWORK (Functional Peers; Not Friends; The Texture of His Working Life)

*A category, not a single individual, because Aaron's network of fences, gear-suppliers, intel-traders, and bond-adjacent intermediaries is treated by him as fungible. No fence is irreplaceable to him; collectively they are essential. The dossier flags this fungibility itself as diagnostic.*

**History and texture.** Across his Ultimate career and the early 616 run, Aaron moves stolen goods, sources gear, and acquires intelligence through a recurring but rotating cast of intermediaries - some of them recurring background figures in Ultimate Spider-Man, some named-only-once in 616. He is known in this milieu as a clean operator: pays on time, does not chatter, does not bring heat back to the seller, does not negotiate beyond a reasonable opening. Reputation within the fence economy is the closest thing he has to a professional credit score and he protects it carefully.

**Dynamics.** Charming-but-clipped. He uses humor to lubricate transactions and never to extend them. He does not drink with fences, does not learn about their children, does not accept hospitality that would create an unbalanced ledger. He treats the relationships as professional and therefore as exhaustively replaceable.

**Trust / safety.** Calibrated low and uniform. He does not trust any single fence enough to be exposed by them, which is achieved by never giving any single fence enough to expose him with.

**Failure mode.** A fence flipped to law enforcement or to a hostile principal could surface enough fragmentary data to compromise individual jobs but not Aaron's identity or domicile - he has structurally limited the damage any single node can do. The failure mode that has actually materialized (in 616, via the Assessor) is not betrayal by a fence but acquisition of his network *as a network* by a higher-order actor who could see the whole graph at once.

**Leverage.** Low per individual, moderate in aggregate. An adversary who maps and pressures the network can constrain Aaron's operational capacity significantly without ever touching him directly. This is the modality the Assessor exploited.

---

### 7.6 — THE ASSESSOR (Coercer Disguised as Patron; Anti-Mentor)

*Included in this section under protest of the category. The Assessor is not an ally and is not chosen family; he is filed here because, in the 616 arc, he occupies the structural slot a mentor or patron would occupy in another man's life - the figure with capital, intelligence apparatus, and a job pipeline - and Aaron's response to him illuminates the shape of the mentor-vacancy in Aaron's history.*

**History.** Surfaces in the Ahmed run as the principal behind a trafficking-adjacent enterprise that ensnares Aaron during a period of attempted straightening. Acquires Aaron not through enthusiasm but through pressure: leverage on prior associates, financial squeeze, and the implicit promise that compliance will preserve the new civilian life Aaron is trying to build.

**Dynamics.** The Assessor handles Aaron the way one handles an asset whose loyalty is purchased rather than earned, which - given Aaron's pressure-point profile (Section 5: *being handled* is the least tolerable register) - was the strategic error. Aaron complied for a window, internally seethed, and discharged the seethe into the betrayal pattern documented in his prior dealings with coercive principals.

**Trust / safety.** Zero in both directions; the relationship was transactional under duress from the start.

**Failure mode (from the Assessor's perspective).** Aaron's tolerance for being managed has a hard ceiling and the Assessor exceeded it. The failure mode (from Aaron's perspective) was that engagement at all - having entered the orbit, he could not exit without cost to the civilian life he was trying to protect, and the costs accrued.

**Leverage.** The Assessor's hold on Aaron operated through the things Aaron was trying to keep clean (the apartment, the driving job, the residual standing with Miles and Rio). Severing those would have neutralized the leverage and also destroyed the asset, which is the paradox endemic to coercing reformed-criminal-with-family.

---

### 7.7 — THE APP-DRIVER LIFE (Civilian Acquaintance Layer; Sparse but Real)

*Not a person, a relational stratum. Catalogued because in the 616 arc Aaron's working civilian life as a ride-share driver constituted his only sustained low-stakes contact with non-criminal adults outside the family, and the dossier would be incomplete without noting how he handled it.*

**Dynamics.** Surprisingly competent. Aaron is good at the driver role for the same reason he is good at burglary: he reads rooms, he calibrates affect to passenger, he keeps surfaces clean. Passenger interactions are bounded, transactional, and emotionally weightless - which suits him. He does not form persistent relationships with passengers; he does form a thin, cordial recognition-network with other drivers at the same staging zones (airports, hubs). On the available record he learned at least a few first names and was capable of small talk that did not signal the criminal underneath. The civilian camouflage was not performance; it was rehearsal for a self he was trying to make real.

**Trust / safety.** Functionally adequate; no one in this stratum knows him deeply enough to trust or distrust him meaningfully.

**Failure mode.** The civilian layer collapses the moment the criminal layer reaches into it. When it collapsed (Assessor era), Aaron lost the layer entirely and had to rebuild it.

**Leverage.** None available through this stratum directly. It does, however, represent the surface of Aaron's reform attempt and its loss is registered by him as evidence-against-himself in the verdict trial he is permanently conducting before the absent Jefferson.

---

### 7.8 — THE ABSENT TIER: MENTORS, FRIENDS, PEERS HE NEVER ACQUIRED

*A negative-space sub-section. The dossier is incomplete without it because the absences are themselves data.*

**No mentor.** Aaron has no documented criminal mentor - no older operator who taught him the trade, no patron-figure who sponsored him into the milieu, no equivalent of the relationships that organize most career criminals' early years. He appears to have self-taught, which fits his characterological self-sufficiency and also explains the equipment-dependence noted in Section 2: he learned the trade without anyone to inherit gear-discipline from, which is part of why the gauntlets killed him. A mentored thief gets his tools serviced; an autodidact thief trusts his own maintenance.

**No partner.** No on-record long-term crew. He has worked alongside others on specific jobs and against others when interests diverged; he has not had a Butch-and-Sundance. The closest he came was the early-adulthood pairing with Jefferson, and the result of that pairing is the rest of the file.

**No peer-confidant.** No friend on Aaron's level whom he calls when the job goes sideways. Miles is asked to be this, which is precisely why the relationship corrodes under load - Aaron is using a nephew as a peer-confidant because there is no peer-confidant slot filled in his life.

**No therapist, no clergy, no AA-equivalent, no community of accountability.** The reform arc in 616 proceeds without any of the scaffolding that normally supports such reforms. He is attempting a recovery alone, which - per the broader literature on what such recoveries require - is the structural reason his back-slides recur. He has Rio's tolerance and Miles's love and neither is sufficient infrastructure for what he is trying to do.

**Synthesis of the absences.** The negative space confirms the positive-space reading: Aaron Davis is a man who distributed his entire attachment budget to one nephew because diversifying felt lethal, and the corollary is that he never built the surrounding network a reforming criminal needs. The thinness of this section is the etiology of the back-slides in 616 and the loneliness of the death in Ultimate. He died alone in his gauntlets because there was no one in the room. There was no one in the room because there had been no one in any of the rooms for a very long time.

---

*End Section 7. See Section 8 for Adversaries & Operational Counterparties; Section 9 for the granular Assessor case study; Section 10 for behavioral micro-patterns (routes, rituals, tells).*


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section — Relationships III: Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

*Cross-referenced against the operational record in Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #1–28, Spider-Men II, All-New Ultimates, Miles Morales: Ultimate Spider-Man, the 616 Miles Morales: Spider-Man run, and adjacent Champions / Spider-Geddon appearances. Where the two continuities diverge, both are logged. Where the file has gaps, granular inference is offered with reasoning shown.*

---

### Preface to the Section

Aaron's enemies file is shorter than his career length should produce, and this absence is itself diagnostic. A man who has worked the high-end B&E circuit in New York for roughly fifteen on-record years should have accumulated a longer list of personal antagonists than he has. He has not, for three reasons visible in the operational pattern: (i) he prefers jobs whose victims are institutional rather than individual — banks, corporations, Oscorp, governmental black sites — which generate adversaries that are systems rather than persons; (ii) when he does cross individuals, he prefers to leave them embarrassed and intact rather than dead, because corpses generate avengers and embarrassed men generate gossip he can manage; (iii) he has a strong, almost superstitious aversion to "collecting" enemies, which he has stated in fragments to Miles ("you never want to be somebody's reason for getting up in the morning"). The men below are the exceptions. Each of them got under the operational wall in a different way, and the manner of getting in is more revealing than the contest itself.

Lovers are sparser still. Aaron is a private erotic actor; he runs the same low-disclosure protocol on intimacy that he runs on tradecraft. What the record yields is fragmentary but consistent, and the gaps can be filled by inference from his attachment structure, which is described elsewhere in this dossier and which makes the romantic history below precisely the romantic history one would predict.

---

### I. RIVALS

#### Maxwell Gargan — "The Scorpion"

The defining adversary of Aaron's Ultimate-continuity career and the relational template against which his other underworld rivalries should be read.

**History.** Aaron and Gargan crossed paths through the New York gear-fence ecosystem before the on-panel Ultimate Comics Spider-Man arc began; the inference from the way they speak to each other on first appearance — the unearned familiarity, the immediate trade in slights — is of a years-long professional acquaintance that had calcified into mutual contempt before Bendis picked up the thread. Gargan is the Mexican-cartel-affiliated heavy who appears in *Ultimate Comics Spider-Man* #6–10, runs his New York interests as an annex of larger trafficking and protection rackets, and views Aaron as a flashy, undisciplined, costume-wearing free agent operating in his market without paying tribute. Aaron views Gargan as a thug who has confused volume for skill — a man who controls territory by killing the wrong people and is therefore, by Aaron's craft-pride metric, an embarrassment to the trade.

**Dynamics.** This is the rivalry of the artisan and the operator. Aaron is contemptuous of Gargan's methods (loud, broad, attributable, body-count-positive); Gargan is contemptuous of Aaron's airs (the costume, the gear, the lone-wolf framing, the refusal to pay into anyone's larger structure). Each represents to the other the thing he refuses to be: Aaron will not become a soldier in someone else's army, Gargan will not become a glorified second-story man. Their language to each other in their two on-panel confrontations is laden with status-marking and craft-marking — Aaron mocks Gargan's lack of finesse, Gargan mocks Aaron's costume — and the mocking is the entire point. They are sublimating a market dispute into an aesthetic one.

**Evolution.** The relationship moves from low-grade competitive friction (pre-page) to active commercial conflict (Aaron attempts to muscle in on Gargan's operation using Miles as an unwitting asset) to physical confrontation (the rooftop and warehouse sequences in which Miles is conscripted to fight Gargan on Aaron's behalf) to mutual ruin (Gargan dosed with the Oz formula; Aaron killed by his own equipment in the subsequent escalation). They do not, in the published record, reconcile, capitulate, or settle. The arc ends with both parties spent.

**Trust / safety.** Zero in both directions and stable at zero. Neither has ever extended credit to the other; neither has ever expected to. The relationship is unusual in Aaron's file precisely because there is no ambiguity in it — Aaron, who runs the world on the assumption that everyone has a seam, never tried to find Gargan's seam. He treated Gargan as a phenomenon to be displaced, not a man to be managed. This is the closest the file comes to documenting Aaron unable to read someone — and the inability is volitional. He didn't want to know Gargan well enough to manipulate him, because knowing him would have implied a peer relation he refused.

**Failure mode.** Aaron's failure with Gargan is the failure that closes the Ultimate arc: he weaponized Miles to win a contest he could have walked away from. The Scorpion problem was not existential; Aaron made it existential because losing market share to Gargan would have cracked the craft-pride that holds his self-concept together. He chose ego over the nephew and lost both. Gargan's failure with Aaron is symmetric: he could have absorbed Aaron into his structure on terms Aaron might have accepted under enough pressure, and instead chose to humiliate and threaten, which guaranteed Aaron would respond with a force-multiplier (Miles) he could not match.

**Leverage.** Aaron's leverage over Gargan was always the same: Gargan was loud, Aaron was quiet, and Aaron knew where Gargan lived. He never used it as cleanly as he could have, because doing so would have required admitting Gargan was worth a long campaign. Gargan's leverage over Aaron was the threat of upward escalation to cartel principals who would not care about Aaron's costume or his craft and who would simply, eventually, find his door. This threat was credible and Aaron knew it; it is part of why the Ultimate-era confrontations took on the desperate quality they did.

#### The Tinkerer (gear-supplier / quasi-rival)

Not an enemy in the active sense, but a structural rival for control over Aaron's most important asset — his equipment.

**History.** The gear that makes Aaron the Prowler is not, in either continuity, fully his own design. The vibration-claws, the optics, and the suit's structural elements come from the underground tech-fabrication ecosystem in which Phineas Mason and his analogs operate. Aaron is a user, modifier, and maintainer of this hardware; he is not its originator. This means that across his career he has been in a low-grade dependent relationship with whoever supplies and services the gear, and that the supplier knows the gear's failure modes better than Aaron does.

**Dynamics.** Service-provider with implicit blackmail capacity. Aaron pays in cash and stolen materials; the supplier delivers and maintains; both parties pretend the asymmetry does not exist. Aaron's craft-pride does not extend cleanly into the engineering domain — he can field-strip and repair, he cannot design from scratch — and the gap is a permanent itch in his self-concept. He overcompensates verbally, presenting the suit as his own, and the supplier permits the fiction as part of the price of doing business.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally adequate, structurally dangerous. The supplier has never knowingly sabotaged Aaron, but the suit has killed him once (Ultimate, malfunctioning gauntlets) and nearly killed him several times more, and the line between negligent manufacture and deniable sabotage is one Aaron is constitutionally unable to investigate, because investigating would require admitting the dependence.

**Failure mode.** The gear that defines him is the gear that ends him. This is not a metaphor; it is the actual cause of death in the Ultimate continuity. The rivalry with the supplier ecosystem is therefore the most consequential adversarial relationship in the entire file, even though it never produces a face-to-face confrontation worth annotating.

**Leverage.** The supplier holds all of it. Aaron holds none. He manages the imbalance by pretending it does not exist, which is the same management strategy he uses for the Jefferson rupture, and the parallel is not coincidental — Aaron has one defense against asymmetries he cannot resolve, which is to act as if they aren't there.

#### The Assessor (616)

The defining adversary of Aaron's 616 reentry and the figure who triggers his single most consequential moral test.

**History.** The Assessor is a data-driven trafficker introduced in Ahmed's *Miles Morales: Spider-Man*, running a Brooklyn-based operation that monetizes vulnerable young people through quantified risk-pricing. He recruits Aaron specifically because Aaron is publicly trying to go straight — a man visibly fighting his pattern is, to the Assessor's analytic frame, the most predictable mark, because his attempted reform has cost him the support network of his prior life and his new legitimate income is insufficient to cover his debts.

**Dynamics.** Coercion through precise leverage. The Assessor does not threaten Aaron with violence; he threatens Aaron with the loss of the 616 reform itself — exposure to Miles, exposure to Jefferson's widow's circle (in the continuity-state where Jefferson is dead), exposure to the parole and rideshare-employer infrastructure on which Aaron's straight life depends. This is the most sophisticated handling Aaron has ever been subjected to, and it works for a period that the file should not euphemize.

**Evolution.** Aaron is recruited, complies, performs, suppresses, and then — when the Assessor's operation crosses into trafficking minors — breaks. The break is total and self-endangering. He turns, he informs to Miles, he assists in the dismantling, and he accepts the legal exposure that follows.
