**Trust / safety.** None ever extended in either direction. Both parties knew from contact one that the relationship was a leash. The diagnostic interest is in *how long Aaron tolerated the leash*, which was longer than his Ultimate-era profile would have predicted, and the explanation is that the cost of refusal was Miles, and Aaron had decided in advance that he would pay almost anything to keep Miles.

**Failure mode.** The Assessor's failure is the failure of all coercers in Aaron's file: he confused leverage with ownership. The pressure-points file notes this elsewhere — "Aaron tolerates being beaten more easily than being managed. Coercers who think they own him are the figures he most reliably betrays." The Assessor read Aaron as a quantified risk; what he failed to price was the hard line on children, which is not a calculated value in Aaron but a categorical one.

**Leverage.** The Assessor's leverage was the reform itself, which is the cruelest form of leverage available against a man like Aaron — using his attempt to become better as the lever to make him worse. Aaron's leverage against the Assessor was operational intimacy: he was inside the structure long enough to map it for Miles. The exchange, by the time the file closes on it, runs in Aaron's favor.

#### Hammerhead / mid-tier organized-crime principals (background)

A composite category. Aaron has had peripheral, transactional friction with several New York organized-crime figures across both continuities — Hammerhead's circle, Maggia-adjacent operators, the post-Kingpin succession churn. None rise to the level of a defined personal rivalry. The diagnostic point is the *non-engagement*: Aaron has spent fifteen on-record years working in territory these men consider theirs, and he has avoided becoming a principal-on-principal target by being small enough to not be worth the campaign and good enough to not be worth the cleanup. This is conscious. He has selected his job ceiling partly to stay beneath the threshold at which the larger structures notice him. It is one of his most professionally disciplined behaviors and it is invisible in any single appearance — only the longitudinal record reveals it.

---

### II. ENEMIES

The distinction this file draws between rivals and enemies: a rival contests the same territory and wants Aaron to lose; an enemy wants Aaron to no longer exist. By this metric, the enemies list is short, and most of the entries are figures Aaron made into enemies by the way he handled them, rather than figures who came to him hostile.

#### Jefferson Davis (as functional enemy across both continuities)

The most consequential enemy in Aaron's life is his brother, and the file would be malpracticing to place him only in the family section. Jefferson functions, in Aaron's interior operational map, as the primary adversary against whose verdict every adult action is staged. The relational details — the shared formative robbery, the excommunication, the erasure from Miles's childhood, the failure to reconcile before Jefferson's 616 death — are covered in Relationships I (Family). What belongs here is the *adversarial* reading: Jefferson is the man who definitionally declared Aaron irredeemable, and Aaron has spent his adult life either confirming or contesting that verdict, with no available third option.

**Trust / safety.** None extended in either direction in adulthood. Aaron would not turn his back on Jefferson in an operational context, not because Jefferson would harm him but because Jefferson would expose him, which is the same thing in Aaron's threat model. Jefferson would not accept anything Aaron offered, including help, including warning, including, eventually, apology.

**Failure mode.** Aaron's failure with Jefferson is to have addressed every word of his adult life to a man he refused to speak to directly. Jefferson's failure with Aaron is the symmetric one — to have addressed his refusal to a brother he had already, in the only way that mattered, killed off. The mutual non-address is the relationship.

**Leverage.** Jefferson holds it all. Even in death (in 616), Jefferson holds it all. Aaron's compliance with the reform arc is partly motivated by the absent brother's standing judgment, which Aaron cannot now appeal. This is the single most painful structural fact in the file.

#### Maxwell Gargan (as enemy, post-rivalry)

Logged above as a rival. Crosses into enemy status in the late Ultimate arc when the dispute exceeds market terms and becomes mutually annihilatory. After Gargan is Oz-formula transformed, the contest no longer admits a settlement — Aaron is dealing with something that wants him dead in a way the prior Gargan did not. The escalation is mutual and the resolution is mutual destruction. Aaron's reading of Gargan in this phase shifts: the contemptuous-craftsman posture drops, replaced by an operational seriousness that is, by Aaron's standards, an admission of respect. He never voices it.

#### The Ringer, second-tier costumed competition (background)

Composite. There exists in both continuities a small population of mid-tier costumed B&E operators who occupy adjacent niches to Aaron's. He treats them with the same mixture of professional courtesy and territorial firmness one would see in any skilled-trade local. They are not enemies; they are colleagues he occasionally has to discourage. The diagnostic point is that he discourages without killing, almost without injuring — a behavioral signature that holds across both continuities and that distinguishes him from the figures (Gargan, the Assessor) he treats as genuine adversaries. Aaron's violence is calibrated: he hurts people in proportion to the threat they represent to the long-term plan, not in proportion to how much they have annoyed him in the moment. This is unusually disciplined and worth flagging because it is the behavioral evidence against the more severe characterological readings the file could otherwise support.

#### Oscorp / Norman Osborn's residual security apparatus

The break-in at Oscorp that produced the Miles-biting spider is Aaron's defining job — it is the act that, unbeknownst to him at the time, manufactured the nephew-as-Spider-Man problem that will reshape his life. Oscorp's security infrastructure, the residual Osborn-corporate apparatus, and the various federal and corporate investigative threads attached to the spider's escape constitute a low-grade, permanent adversary in Aaron's background. He has never been caught for the Oscorp job. The file infers, from his pattern of avoiding Oscorp-adjacent contracts after the original break-in, that he knows the heat on it is permanent and that he is being patient — content to have gotten clean once and unwilling to push the luck. This is, again, professional discipline of a kind his self-presentation does not advertise.

The deeper enemy here is informational: the Oscorp job is the one secret Aaron carries that has the most operational consequence (Miles's powers), and he cannot disclose it without forfeiting the only relationship that matters. Norman Osborn's institutional ghost is, in this sense, the holder of leverage Aaron does not know is being held.

#### Federal and municipal law enforcement (NYPD, FBI)

Aaron has a file with both, deeper than his arrest record suggests. The inference, from his consistent avoidance behaviors — preferring nighttime ingress, varying routes, refusing to keep a fixed address for long stretches in the Ultimate era, in 616 maintaining a documented straight-job paper trail that is unusually meticulous for a man of his profile — is that he assumes continuous low-grade surveillance and prices it into his planning. Specific officers he has crossed are not on-panel named with any frequency, which is itself the data: he has not made it personal with any specific law-enforcement actor, because making it personal converts a manageable structural adversary into an enemy of the dangerous kind. The 616 parole infrastructure is the closest the file comes to a named institutional adversary, and his management of it is, again, more disciplined than his self-presentation would suggest.

#### Self (operational adversary)

The file would be incomplete without naming the most consistent adversary in Aaron's life, which is Aaron. The pattern is documented elsewhere in this dossier — the gauntlets that kill him, the relapses in 616, the inability to refuse a job at the moment he most needs to refuse one. In adversarial terms: Aaron is the figure in his own life most likely to undo whatever Aaron has built, and the only adversary against whom he has no successful countermeasure. The Ultimate-era death is the literal expression of this. The 616 reform is the slow, ongoing, mixed-success campaign against it. There is no peace treaty available.

---

### III. LOVERS & INTIMATE PARTNERS

The file here is thin by design — Aaron's. What follows is the documented record, the inferred record, and the structural reading.

#### Documented and Named

The published record names no long-term romantic partner for Aaron Davis in either continuity. This is itself a finding. A man of Aaron's social skill, physical presentation, and operational mobility is not celibate by accident; the absence of a named partner in fifteen on-record years means he has actively curated against documentation. The behavioral pattern this implies — short-duration relationships, deliberate non-overlap with operational life, geographic and informational compartmentalization — is the pattern one would expect from a professional thief with an attachment-dismissing baseline and a single fiercely guarded family-attachment focus.

#### Inferred Pattern (Ultimate Era)

The behavioral signatures across the Ultimate run — the apartments visibly arranged for a single occupant, the absence of partner-presence in the spaces Miles visits, the casual references to women that do not recur as named figures, the absence of any mourner in his Ultimate-era death except Miles — describe a man whose erotic life is conducted in cycles of a few weeks to a few months, with partners selected for their disinterest in the parts of his life he will not disclose. He is, by inference, a competent and considerate short-term partner whose partners learn, eventually, that there is a door past which they are not invited, and who leave when they realize the door is the entire interior.

The selection criteria, inferred from the few on-panel social interactions and from his interpersonal style: women who are themselves operating with some privacy of their own — colleagues in adjacent professions, people with their own reasons for not asking questions, people for whom the relationship's compartmentalization is a feature. He does not, by this reading, date civilians who expect to meet his family. He cannot deliver the family.

**Trust / safety in this register.** He is physically safe to be with — his calibration of violence applies in intimate contexts as it does in operational ones, which is to say he is exceptionally controlled. He is emotionally unsafe in the specific sense that he does not disclose enough for a partner to make informed decisions about the relationship's trajectory, and he does not commit to disclosures that would require him to surrender operational privacy. He is not cruel; he is closed.

**Failure mode in this register.** The relationships end when the partner asks the question Aaron will not answer, which is some version of "who are you really." Aaron's response is consistent: he tells a partial truth, registers the partner's awareness that it is partial, and exits with as much grace as the situation permits. He does not, on-record, leave women angry. He leaves them puzzled, which is a deliberate choice — a puzzled ex is less dangerous than an angry one, and Aaron has been managing his exposure profile since adolescence.

**Leverage in this register.** None ever accumulates, by design. The lovers are selected and the relationships structured precisely so that none of them ever holds enough of Aaron to extort, expose, or even surprise him. This is professional risk management applied to intimacy. It is also a profound personal foreclosure, and the file should not pretend the operational logic of it is the same as the personal cost of it.

#### Inferred Pattern (616 Era)

The reform arc reframes the erotic life as well as the criminal one. The 616 Aaron, working app-driving hours, maintaining a documented address, sustaining a reconstructed relationship with Miles, appears to be slowly building the kind of stable interpersonal infrastructure that could, in principle, accommodate a long-term partner. The file does not document one within the published window. The inference is that he is moving toward the possibility and that he is not yet there, because the work of becoming a man who can be partnered is downstream of the work of becoming a man who can be in the family frame Miles is keeping open for him, and that primary work is not finished.

The 616 partner, when she appears (the file projects forward on the trajectory the record establishes), will be someone connected to the rideshare or recovery or community-reentry ecosystems Aaron is now embedded in — someone whose own history requires no apology from his, and whose presence in Miles's life is acceptable to Miles. The 616 Aaron will not date in secret. The Ultimate Aaron could not date in any other way. The shift is the reform in miniature.

#### Structural Reading

Aaron's erotic life is the most legible expression of his attachment structure, precisely because it is the domain where he has the most freedom and uses it for the least intimacy. The dossier's main psychological formulation — dismissing-avoidant baseline with a single preoccupied exception focused on Miles — predicts exactly the lover-history the record shows: many short, competent, undisclosed relationships and no documented enduring partner. The single attachment budget is allocated to the nephew. There is none left for a wife.

This is not a deficiency to be regretted; it is a choice, made under conditions Aaron did not entirely choose, that has structured the surface of his romantic life and the depth of his loneliness. The Ultimate-continuity death scene contains no romantic mourner. The 616


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

*Capabilities mapping, derived from operational record across Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #1-onward, Spider-Men II, All-New Ultimates, Miles Morales: The Ultimate Spider-Man, and the 616 reintroduction in Miles Morales: Spider-Man (Ahmed). Cross-referenced with observed tactical decisions, equipment failures, and longitudinal change in technique.*

---

### 6.1 Baseline Physiology

Aaron Davis is, in the strict biological accounting, **a normal-baseline adult human male of late thirties to early forties** with no augmentation, no exposure-derived enhancement, no surgical implant, no symbiote, no mutation. Every measurable instance of "superhuman" output on his record traces to gear, training, or terrain advantage. This is the single most important fact in the capability file: the man whose nephew can stick to walls and dodge bullets enters the same fight wearing batteries.

Physical conditioning is, by visible parameter, **high-end operator grade** - somewhere between special-forces baseline and elite parkour athlete, without quite reaching the silhouette of a metahuman-tier acrobat. He is lean, long-limbed, with the developed forearm and shoulder mass consistent with a career of climbing, hanging, swinging, and gauntlet-bracing. Resting heart rate inferable as low; pre-job he reads as physiologically calm where a civilian would be tachycardic. Recovery from blunt trauma is normal-human - he stays beaten when he is beaten, requires hours-to-days to walk off impact injuries, and shows no regenerative signature.

**Hand-eye coordination and proprioception** are the standout native attributes. He places gauntlet-claws into specific anchor points - mortar joints between bricks, the lip of a window frame, the seam of a rivet on an industrial duct - at speed and in low light without missing. This is trained more than gifted; what is gifted is the **spatial memory**, the apparent ability to reconstruct a building's interior topology from minutes of reconnaissance and operate inside it semi-blind.

### 6.2 The Suit: System Architecture

The Prowler rig in the Ultimate continuity reads as a **modular, primarily Oscorp- and Roxxon-derived stack** - corporate-grade hardware assembled and modified by a man who understands its function operationally without necessarily holding the engineering education to have built it from first principles. He is a **user-modifier**, not a designer. He maintains it, swaps parts, tunes it, but the foundational engineering is borrowed - which is precisely why it eventually kills him.

The core elements, as observed across both continuities:

- **Powered gauntlets with extendable claws.** Three-to-four-claw configuration per hand, retractable, evidently driven by a sprung-and-actuated mechanism with electromagnetic latching. The claws function across three discrete use-modes: (a) climbing anchor, biting into masonry, brick, soft stone, wood, and most metal sheeting under 1/8 inch; (b) edged weapon for close combat; (c) launch-projectile, with at least one or more claws detachable on a tether or as a free projectile.
- **Wrist-mounted ranged systems.** Cable launcher used for traversal and disarmament; in some appearances a directed-energy or kinetic projectile system mounted to the forearm. The energy output of these systems is what fails terminally in the Ultimate confrontation - the gauntlet either overloads or detonates against the body of the user.
- **Boot armatures.** Provide grip on vertical surfaces (likely a combination of micro-spike and tacky polymer), shock absorption for drops in the two-to-four-story range, and silent footstrike. He can land from heights that would cripple a civilian and continue at sprint.
- **Mantle/cowl with optics.** Low-light and likely thermal overlay, peripheral HUD elements, audio dampening. The cowl conceals the lower face; the eye-lenses are reflective. He uses the optics as much for **target-discrimination** in dim interiors as for navigation.
- **Body armor.** Light-to-medium ballistic weave under the costume's outer layer; rated against handgun rounds and edged weapons at standard distances, not against rifle calibers, not against superhuman strike force. He has been put down by Scorpion's strikes and by his nephew's pulled punches.

The 616 iteration of the suit is functionally similar with cosmetic and capability adjustments per Ahmed's run, but the diagnostic architecture is the same: **a meat operator inside borrowed corporate hardware.**

### 6.3 Tradecraft — The Real Skill Set

Strip the suit and what remains is the more dangerous half of Aaron Davis. The hardware is the amplifier; the operator is the instrument.

**Breaking and entering, professional grade.** He reads buildings the way most people read faces. Pre-job behavior, inferable from his on-panel arrival sequences: he walks a perimeter, identifies primary and secondary ingress, locates HVAC and utility routes, marks camera coverage and the angles they do not cover, clocks the security-rotation cadence. He prefers **roof entry** when the rig is on (vertical approach maximizes the gauntlet/boot advantage and minimizes ground-floor witness exposure) and **service entry** when working clean. He defeats commercial locks rapidly; he defeats electronic systems via either signal-spoof tools built into the gauntlets or, more often, by simply going around them through structural vulnerabilities other thieves do not see.

**Close-quarters combat.** Fights in a **gauntlet-forward, low-stance idiom** - claws angled outward, weight back, exploiting the reach and intimidation of the edged hardware to dictate distance. His unarmed striking is competent but not his preferred mode; he does not bare-knuckle when he can claw, and he does not claw when he can disengage. The combat philosophy is **disengagement-positive**: he wins fights by ending them, not by dominating them. Against superior opponents (Scorpion, Spider-Man-tier) he survives by terrain manipulation - drawing them into spaces where his climb/swing advantage matters and their power advantage decays.

**Marksmanship and projectile use.** Competent with the wrist systems at intermediate range; demonstrates lead, holdover, and snap-shot capacity. He is not a trained rifle shooter on-panel; the projectile work is gauntlet-integrated and within twenty meters.

**Driving and route knowledge.** New York topology is in him at the bone level. He moves through the boroughs the way locals move through their own apartments - knows which alleys connect, which fire escapes have collapsing bottoms, which rooftops are jumpable, which subway service tunnels parallel which streets. The 616 driver-for-app-platform period is not merely an income source - it is **reconnaissance disguised as employment**, a constant low-grade refresh of the city map he carries in his head. Whether he consciously codes it that way is another question; the behavior is consistent with a man who cannot stop running route updates even when not actively planning a job.

**Social engineering.** First-tier. He is the most engaging man in any room he chooses to engage, can establish rapport in under a minute, can extract information through conversational drift without the target registering they were interviewed. He is excellent at **performing harmlessness** - the cool uncle, the affable driver, the guy at the bar - which is the most useful skill a working thief possesses. He runs it on Miles. He runs it on Jefferson when forced into proximity. He has run it on his entire adult life.

**Tactical patience.** Will wait. Will surveille for days when the job calls for it. Does not have the chronic urgency signature of an impulsive criminal; the work is planned, sequenced, and only abandoned mid-execution under specific failure conditions. This is the single feature most discordant with an antisocial-impulsive read and most consistent with the **craftsman self-concept** that organizes his professional identity.

### 6.4 What He Cannot Do

The negative space is as diagnostic as the positive.

- **He cannot take a superhuman hit.** Any sustained engagement with a meta-tier opponent ends with him on the ground. He is functional against street-level criminals, mid-tier powered antagonists at brief engagement distances, and overmatched against anyone in the Spider-Man weight class who does not pull strikes.
- **He cannot build his hardware.** He maintains and modifies; he does not originate. This makes him **supply-chain dependent** - on the original Oscorp/Roxxon stock, on the gray-market techs who service it, on whoever he can leverage or pay. The dependency is a permanent vulnerability and a permanent reason to take jobs he should refuse.
- **He cannot operate at scale.** He is a solo or two-man operator. The few times he runs crew (the Ultimate gang configurations, the All-New Ultimates appearances) he is visibly worse at it than at solo work - the management overhead degrades his tactical performance.
- **He cannot fight a war of attrition.** Normal-human stamina, normal-human pain envelope. Engagements are designed to be brief because long engagements are losing engagements.
- **He cannot, in any verified instance, defeat his own equipment in failure mode.** The gauntlets that killed him in Ultimate continuity were diagnosable; he did not diagnose them. He trusts the rig past the point the rig has earned trust. This is the operational expression of the broader psychological pattern - he commits to instruments that have already begun to betray him.

### 6.5 Growth and Decay Over Career Time

**Early-career (pre-Miles-discovery, inferable from incidental backstory).** Pure operator phase. Job-focused, gear-confident, low affective involvement in work. Technical proficiency rising; the relational deficits not yet operationally relevant because there are no relational stakes in the work.

**Mid-career (Ultimate, Miles-discovery through Ultimate death).** Performance becomes **uneven and identity-distorted.** The tradecraft remains sharp on technical axes but degrades on judgment axes: he takes jobs he should refuse because they create proximity to Miles, escalates coercion when escalation is operationally counter-indicated, runs leverage plays against a partner whose powers exceed his own equipment by an order of magnitude. The terminal gauntlet failure is not bad luck - it is the somatic expression of a man whose attention has migrated off his own gear and onto a relational chess game he is losing. **He died because he stopped being a craftsman first.**

**Late-career (616, Ahmed run).** The technical capability is preserved or slightly degraded by the attempted-straight period (the body softens, the routes go stale a little, the gauntlets are maintained but less obsessively). What grows is **discrimination** - he can now refuse jobs, can disengage from leverage, can use the tradecraft for protective rather than acquisitive ends. The skill set is the same; the deployment ethic has changed. He becomes, intermittently and partially, **a competent operator in the service of his nephew rather than against him.** The arc the Ultimate version was denied.

### 6.6 Signature Applications

Several specific operational patterns recur often enough to constitute a **behavioral signature** - the kind of MO an investigative agency would file as a fingerprint.

- **The vertical entry.** When the rig is on, he enters from above. Roof access, ductwork, light-well descent. He does not breach a ground-floor door if a window two stories up is available.
- **The single circuit.** He does not loiter on a target site. One traversal in, one traversal out, no double-back. If a thing is not where the intel said it would be, he leaves; he does not search.
- **The claw-tether disarm.** Preferred opening move against armed opposition - claw-tether launched to snatch or redirect a weapon rather than to strike the wielder. Buys time, demonstrates control, signals capability without committing to lethal escalation.
- **The conversational extraction.** Pre-job intel often gathered by talking to a peripheral figure - a doorman, a delivery driver, a bartender - in a register so casual the target never notices the interview.
- **The disappearance.** Post-job exfiltration that exploits the city's vertical and subterranean infrastructure. He does not run; he goes up or down, and then sideways across a plane the pursuers are not using.
- **The gift as instrument.** With Miles specifically, material generosity is operationally deployed - the gift establishes obligation, opens the rapport channel, pre-empts the harder conversation. He is aware he does this. He does it anyway.

### 6.7 The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

The capability profile is, end to end, **a portrait of his psychology in hardware and motion.**

He is a man whose entire operational identity is **borrowed gear worn over a normal body** - which is exactly his relational structure. The Prowler suit is the professional-craftsman surface; the body inside is the disinherited brother. Strip the rig and he is a human being who can be hit. Strip the cool-uncle affect and he is a man whose only sibling pretended he was dead. The hardware and the persona perform the same load-bearing function: they keep the soft middle from being seen, and they fail under the same conditions - when proximity to family forces the surface off.

He **enters from above and leaves through routes pursuers cannot use** - which is also how he handles intimacy. He arrives in Miles's life from an angle Jefferson did not cover, and when the relationship becomes confrontational he disengages through channels (humor, exit, leverage-pivot) the other party cannot follow into. The vertical-entry, single-circuit, no-loitering job pattern is the operational form of his attachment defense: be present, be effective, do not stay long enough to be cornered.

He **disarms before he strikes** - the claw-tether disarm is his preferred opener, not the lethal stab. This is the man, not just the technique: he prefers to neutralize threat without committing to destruction, prefers to control the engagement geometry rather than win the fight outright. He coerces Miles via threat-of-exposure rather than via violence for the same reason - leverage over kinetic, control over destruction, every time, until the leverage fails and the rig overheats.

He **trusts equipment past the point it has earned trust**, and the equipment kills him. This is the precise structural rhyme with how he handles the relationship with Miles in the Ultimate arc - he commits to a coercive frame that is already failing, escalates inside it, refuses to diagnose the failure mode, and the frame detonates in his hands. The gauntlets are the relationship. The malfunction was legible in both, and he read neither.

He **cannot build the hardware, only modify it** - which is the cognitive shape of a man who inherited the criminal frame from his environment rather than originating it, who has lived inside a structure he did not design and cannot replace. The 616 reform arc is, in capability terms, the attempt to **operate without the rig** - to be a man who can drive a car, hold a conversation, be an uncle, without the suit doing the load-bearing. He is partially successful. The suit comes back. It always comes back, because he has not yet built a self that can carry the weight the hardware was carrying.

And he **runs route updates even when he is not on a job.** The driver-app period in 616 is the cleanest single index of who he is at the operational unconscious: a man who cannot stop mapping the city, cannot stop reading rooms for seams, cannot stop scanning his nephew for leverage even when he has decided not to use it. The capability is the symptom. The craft is the wound, professionalized. The Prowler is what Aaron Davis built to survive being unseen, and the price of the build is that the man inside the suit is still, at the structural level, the boy his brother walked away from.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## SECTION 6 — OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

*Derived from on-panel operational footage across Ultimate Comics Spider-Man #1–28, the Scorpion arc, the Roxxon/Oscorp adjacent jobs, All-New Ultimates appearances, the 616 Assessor/Iron Spider/Barbara arc in Miles Morales: Spider-Man, and the rideshare-cover period of Ahmed's run. Inferences extend the documented behavior into the granular detail a total-surveillance file would contain.*

---

### 6.1 Operational Identity and Cover Architecture

Subject maintains a **three-layer identity stack** at all times, each load-bearing for a different threat model.

**Layer one — civilian Aaron.** The public name, the Brooklyn address(es), the documented vehicle, the tax-visible income. In the Ultimate continuity this layer is thinly maintained; in 616 it is reconstructed deliberately as part of the going-straight project, with the rideshare driver shell as its core. The rideshare cover is exceptionally well-chosen and deserves note: it manufactures legitimate cash flow, justifies presence in any neighborhood at any hour, provides a moving, GPS-trackable alibi that he can manipulate by toggling app status, and permits visual reconnaissance of target environments at the pace and angle of an unremarkable driver. He is one of perhaps a dozen working criminals in either continuity who has selected a cover job whose surveillance value exceeds its income value.

**Layer two — the Prowler.** The costumed operator. Used only when a job requires either the kit's specific capabilities (vertical access, gauntlet weaponry, optics) or when the kit itself functions as identity-obscuring kit. Crucially, Aaron treats the Prowler not as an alter ego but as **a tool he wears** — there is no Prowler-personality, only Aaron operating in Prowler-mode. This is operationally healthy (no dissociative drift) and tactically efficient (no ego-investment in being seen as the Prowler — he will discard the gear cold if the kit becomes liability).

**Layer three — the negotiating broker.** Out of costume, in plainclothes, in a meeting with a fence, client, or rival. This is the most dangerous version of him because it is the one in which his read-rate is highest and his disclosure is lowest. He uses first names readily, drinks slow, sits with his back to a wall, and lets the other party speak roughly sixty percent of the time. He closes meetings before he has been pressured to commit, citing a phone call or a stop he has to make, almost always returning later with a counter-frame that is closer to his own original price.

---

### 6.2 Decision-Making Process

Aaron's decision architecture is **pattern-recognition driven, with a deliberate slow-gate before commitment.** The pattern is consistent across both continuities:

1. **Passive intake.** He absorbs information without visibly working — names dropped at a bar, signage on a door, a tradesman's van outside a building, the way a guard does or does not check his radio. He retains this without notes. The retention is the long-cultivated habit of a man who learned young that writing things down creates evidence.

2. **Lateral scan for seam.** Given a target, he does not ask "how do I get in" — he asks "where is the system designed to ignore me." He looks for the redundant guard whose attention has lapsed, the camera with a sun-glare window, the maintenance schedule, the contractor badge that gets waved through without scrutiny. He prefers exploiting **procedural complacency** over defeating technical security.

3. **Tempo selection.** Aaron makes a deliberate, often slow, decision about pace. He will sit on a target for days when the score warrants and burn through it in ninety seconds when surprise is the asset. The on-panel record shows both extremes: the patient stalking of opportunities and the fast smash-and-evac on Oscorp-adjacent jobs.

4. **Slow-gate before commit.** This is the diagnostic. Aaron rarely accepts a job in the room where it is offered. He will leave, walk, drive, sleep on it, and return. The slow-gate exists because his impulsivity is real and he knows it — the gate is the self-imposed counter to his own pattern. The Assessor coercion in 616 succeeds precisely because it bypasses the slow-gate by placing leverage on Miles, which collapses the deliberation window to zero.

5. **Exit-first planning.** He plans the exit before the entry, and the contingency exit before the primary. He has been observed (Ultimate Spider-Man, Scorpion arc) to abort midway through a job because the exit had degraded, with the loot in hand. This is mature tradecraft and uncommon — most thieves are entry-biased; Aaron is exit-biased.

6. **The single intolerable variable.** Across the record there is one factor that consistently overrides his judgment: Miles. When Miles enters the equation, the slow-gate collapses, the exit-first principle yields to the protective-first principle, and Aaron makes operationally inferior decisions he would never make for money. This is the file's clearest predictor.

---

### 6.3 Tradecraft — The Kit

**The Prowler suit (Ultimate spec, reconstructed and refined in 616).** A purpose-built infiltration platform rather than a combat suit, though it is combat-capable. Documented or inferred components:

- **Gauntlets.** Spring-loaded retractable claws (steel-alloy, edged for cutting and puncturing); integrated projectile launcher (darts, occasional explosive payloads); electrical discharge capability at close range. Aaron favors the claws over the projectiles — projectiles announce; claws disappear. The gauntlets are the component with the documented failure history, including the malfunction that killed him in the Ultimate continuity. He has been observed to manually reseat or strike them when behavior degrades, suggesting an awareness of the fault that he has never adequately addressed — a telling piece of negligence in an otherwise meticulous operator and almost certainly a function of his ambivalent relationship to his own equipment.
- **Boots / climbing rig.** Microspike or adhesive sole tech permitting wall-traversal short of true vertical. Observed scaling surfaces no human without enhancement should manage; not equivalent to spider-adhesion but sufficient for most urban architecture.
- **Optics.** Goggles with at minimum low-light enhancement and probable IR. He routinely operates in darkness with no visible degradation in performance.
- **Soft armor.** Distributes blunt impact without restricting motion. Insufficient against superhuman strength (he gets thrown around by enhanced opponents) but adequate against firearms at distance and edged weapons.
- **Mask and voice modulation.** Identity-concealing; he is careful to never speak in his civilian register while suited, and conversely never lapses into Prowler-cadence while in civvies.

**Tooling outside the suit.** Lock picks (mechanical and electronic), small thermal cutting tools, RFID cloners, signal jammers, burner phones rotated on a strict schedule (he discards rather than archives), pre-paid debit instruments, multiple sets of clean ID. He carries a folding knife at all times in civilian dress — close to body, drawn-side, never the same pocket twice in succession, a tic that suggests both training and superstition.

**Weapons philosophy.** Aaron is a **tool-economy minimalist**. He carries the smallest viable kit. He does not stack contingencies in his pockets; he stacks them in his head. When he needs something he did not bring, his first move is to source it on-site (a kitchen knife, a length of cable, a fire extinguisher used as a stun device). This is the mark of an operator who has been searched and stopped enough times to internalize that carried gear is evidence and improvised gear is not.

---

### 6.4 Movement, Surveillance, and Counter-Surveillance

**Route discipline.** Aaron almost never takes the same route twice within a short window. In the rideshare cover this is camouflaged by the app routing; without that cover, he relies on a memorized internal map of the boroughs that includes pedestrian-only shortcuts, restaurant kitchen pass-throughs, and at least a dozen rooftop transitions. He prefers **third-route logic**: from A to B he plans the obvious route, the police-evasion route, and a third route used for nothing else and never told to anyone, reserved for when the first two are compromised.

**Vehicle use.** In civilian work he drives unremarkable late-model sedans with current registration. He does not personally own a tactical vehicle; he sources transport per job through chop-shop and short-term theft networks. Observed preference for hybrids on extraction (quiet idle), though this may be incidental to availability.

**Counter-surveillance behaviors.** Constant low-grade scanning of reflective surfaces (windows, car panels, phone screens). Tendency to stop short of a destination and walk the last block. Frequent backtracking through buildings with two entrances. He memorizes the cars on his block by the second week of any residency and notes additions. He has been observed checking the underside of his own vehicle without ceremony, the gesture folded into bending to tie a shoe — a habit that pre-dates any specific threat and reads as baseline rather than reactive.

**Cell discipline.** Multiple devices, each scoped narrowly: one for family, one for work, one for fences and clients, occasionally a fourth for a single ongoing operation, discarded at close. He does not save contacts under real names. He uses the family device differently from the others — leaves it on, takes Miles's calls live — and this asymmetry is itself a vulnerability he has accepted because severing the Miles channel for opsec reasons is exactly the thing he refuses to do.

---

### 6.5 Financial Architecture

Aaron operates on a **layered-liquidity model** rather than an accumulation model.

- **Working cash.** Mid-four-figures kept on person or stashed in vehicle, replenished from jobs. He pays for everyday expenses in cash even when card use would be easier; the habit suppresses transactional records.
- **Operating reserve.** A larger sum, probably mid- to high-five-figures at any time, distributed across at least three physical caches — minimum one outside New York City, almost certainly one in a location associated with a fence or a former partner rather than with himself.
- **Convertibles.** Watches, jewelry, small high-value items held as portable wealth, liquidated through known fence networks at predictable discount.
- **Income legitimation (616).** The rideshare income is real, declared in part, and laundered against to justify modest deposits. He pays taxes in 616 — a counterintuitive but observable behavior, executed precisely because going-straight requires a paper trail that does not invite scrutiny.
- **No banking sophistication.** Aaron does not run shell entities, offshore accounts, or crypto wallets of any meaningful scale. His financial security is physical, distributed, and small enough to be invisible. This is by design: complex financial structures create persistent records and require accountants, and accountants are people who can flip.

He is **not motivated by accumulation.** He does not live large. His apartments across the record are utilitarian, his vehicles unremarkable, his clothing functional. Money is the medium of operational continuity, not the goal. This is one of the cleaner indicators that his criminality is dynamically rather than acquisitively motivated.

---

### 6.6 Infrastructure and Network

**Safehouses.** Minimum two operating safehouses at any time, neither leased in his legal name. Preferred profile: ground-floor or top-floor walk-ups (top floor for roof egress, ground floor for street egress), in mixed-use blocks where transient traffic is normal. He pays cash rent through intermediaries or short-term sublet arrangements. He does not decorate. He does not bring women, friends, or Miles to safehouses — the kin-isolation of these spaces is absolute.

**Fences and brokers.** A small, durable network — three to five established fences across the metro, several of whom predate his Prowler career. He maintains them by being reliable rather than by being friendly. He does not haggle aggressively; he takes the offered cut and leaves, on the theory that fences punish hagglers with bad prices on later jobs. This is sophisticated counter-party management.

**Tech support.** Aaron is a competent end-user of his own gear but is not the engineer of it. The Prowler suit is sourced — its original provenance in Ultimate is murky and the 616 reconstitution implies either reverse-engineering, gray-market acquisition, or a tech contact whose identity he protects scrupulously. The fact that he has never been observed troubleshooting the gauntlet malfunction with a technician suggests either that the contact is unavailable, unaffordable, or that Aaron is avoiding the diagnosis — possibly all three.

**Crew composition.** He prefers **solo work**. When he takes a crew it is small (two to four), single-job, never repeated in identical composition. He pays out before extraction is complete — small advance, balance on success — and does not extend credit. He is known among working criminals as professional, fair on payouts, and **not a friend** — exactly the reputation he wants.

**Authority interfaces.** Aaron has, across the record, demonstrated familiarity with at least several corrupt or coercible figures in the law-enforcement and corporate-security spaces. He does not have a regular police contact (his brother's profession in 616 makes this particularly unviable), but he knows who in a given precinct can be bought for what and who cannot. This intelligence is sourced rather than personally cultivated, suggesting an info-broker contact in the network.

---

### 6.7 Combat Posture

Aaron is a **competent fighter, not a great one**, and he knows it. His combat doctrine reflects this self-assessment:

- **Avoidance first.** He does not engage if exit is available. He has walked away from confrontations a more ego-invested operator would have escalated. The avoidance is not cowardice; it is bookkeeping — combat creates witnesses, evidence, and injuries.
- **Surprise second.** When engagement is unavoidable, he prefers to strike first, from an unexpected vector, with maximum disabling force. He does not posture, does not announce, does not banter pre-strike (the in-fight quips are real but post-engagement, a regulation behavior rather than a taunt).
- **Tools over technique.** The gauntlets do the heavy work. His unarmed combat is functional — street-tempered, with what appears to be some formal grounding (boxing rhythm in the footwork, observable across both continuities) — but he would lose an unarmed fight against a trained martial artist of equal size, and he avoids those fights.
- **Mobility over stand.** He uses the suit's climbing capability to break engagement vertically and reset. He does not hold ground.
- **Lethal force restraint.** Aaron has killed and can kill, but he does not casually. The body count is operational, not recreational, and within the network this is part of his professional brand. Bystander harm is a particular line; the 616 trafficking arc demonstrates that crossing that line in front of him terminates his cooperation regardless of leverage.

Against superhuman opposition (Scorpion, the various enhanced operators in All-New Ultimates, the situations that put him near Miles in costume), Aaron's pattern is to **substitute terrain and surprise for the strength gap he cannot close**. He fights enhanced opponents in environments he has pre-mapped, with traps, in low light, from elevation. He loses these fights more often than he wins them but survives more of them than the matchup predicts.

---

### 6.8 Information Practices

Aaron is an **excellent passive collector and a poor archivist** — a tradecraft-consistent combination. He absorbs everything and writes down almost nothing. The few records he keeps are physical (a card, a slip of paper, a photo), single-purpose, and destroyed at job-close. He does not maintain a contact book; the contacts live in his head. This makes him hard to roll up forensically — there is little to seize from him — and makes him correspondingly fragile to his own memory, illness, or distraction.

He compartments information per counterparty by default. A fence learns what the fence needs; a client learns what the client paid for; a crew member learns only the segment of the job they execute. He does not assemble whole-picture briefings. This is unfussy and professional and reflects training that he likely acquired by watching elders fail at it.

The single exception, and the diagnostic one, is Miles, to whom Aaron over-discloses in both continuities — operationally inadvisable revelations about his work, his past, his relationships. The Miles-channel runs unencrypted because Aaron cannot bear to compartment his way out of intimacy with the only person he has it with.

---

### 6.9 Signature Operational Tells

A short list of behaviors that a watcher would learn to recognize:

- **The shoulder roll.** Before any engagement or job-entry, an unconscious single roll of the right shoulder, as if seating a jacket. Pre-action regulation. Present in both continuities and in both civilian and suited contexts.
- **The half-smile pre-violence.** A small, closed-mouth upward pull at the left side of the mouth in the moment before he commits to a strike. Not a taunt — a tell, almost certainly involuntary.
- **The two-beat doorway pause.** On entering any new space he stops for roughly two seconds inside the threshold, eyes moving once across the room. He does this in restaurants as readily as in target buildings; the habit has overgeneralized.
- **The hand-on-pocket check.** Touches the location of his folding knife, phone, and cash in fixed sequence when transitioning between environments. A grounding ritual but also an inventory.
- **The first-name lock.** In rapport-building, will use a counterparty's first name within the first thirty seconds and then sparingly thereafter. The pattern is consistent enough to be diagnostic of him specifically.
- **Walks past the target once before approaching.** Almost never approaches a target building on first pass; walks past at distance, registers it, comes back. The pre-pass is non-negotiable; he has aborted jobs over what he saw on it.
- **Refuses to sit facing away from a door.** Will reseat himself in a restaurant, request a different table, or stand. Civilians read this as restlessness.
- **Drives the speed limit.** Without exception. The discipline of a man who has been pulled over once too often.
- **Slow-blink response to lies.** When being lied to in negotiation, his blink rate slows perceptibly and his verbal tempo decreases. He has not learned to suppress this and probably does not know he does it.
- **Says Miles's name differently.** Voice drops a quarter-step and softens on the name in a way that no other proper noun receives. The single most reliable verbal tell in the file, and the one that any competent adversary would learn to bait him with.

---

### 6.10 Operational Failure Modes

The profile is internally consistent and effective; it fails predictably in four scenarios:

1. **Leverage on Miles.** Collapses the slow-gate, overrides exit-first planning, and produces decisions of inferior quality made at speed. Documented exploit (the Assessor in 616).
2. **Gauntlet malfunction.** The unaddressed equipment fault. Documented terminal in the Ultimate continuity. Not yet corrected on the 616 record.
3. **Handler dynamics.** Anyone who attempts to **own** rather than **contract** him triggers betrayal behaviors. He will sabotage operations he has been coerced into, often subtly enough that the handler does not see it until the loss is realized.
4. **Jefferson contact.** Direct interaction with his brother degrades his operational composure for hours afterward. He has been observed to make uncharacteristic errors in the immediate wake of brother-encounters — a window an informed adversary could exploit by simply timing operations after surveilled family contact.

---

### 6.11 Synthesis

Aaron Davis operates as a **disciplined, low-signature, mid-tier urban professional** whose tradecraft would place him in the top decile of working thieves but whose psychology installs three reliable failure modes that a sophisticated adversary can exploit. His tools are competent, his network small and durable, his money distributed and modest, his decision-making slow-gated and exit-biased — the profile of someone who intends to keep operating for a long time and has structured his life accordingly. The dissonance between this disciplined operational surface and the single channel of unmanaged disclosure (Miles) is the file's central operational fact: everything else about how Aaron works is designed to keep him alive and untraceable, and the one thing he refuses to discipline is the thing through which he will, eventually, be found.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — Worldview & Operational Code

*Derived from longitudinal behavioral record; cross-checked Ultimate and 616 continuities. All articulations below are reconstructions of operating beliefs evidenced in conduct, not self-statements unless cited. Aaron Davis is not a man who would, sober, narrate any of this aloud. The code is legible because it is consistent across two timelines, three creative regimes, and roughly fifteen years of published behavior.*

---

### 6.1 First Principles — The Shape of the World

Aaron's cosmology, reconstructed from how he moves through rooms and arranges his choices, has the following load-bearing axioms:

**(a) The world is a built thing, and built things have seams.** Every system Aaron encounters — a corporate vault, a police perimeter, a family argument, an Oscorp clean-room, a rival crew's hierarchy — he reads first for joinery. Where two pieces meet, the work was done by a person, and the person was tired, distracted, underpaid, or vain. This is not nihilism about institutions; it is the opposite. He has profound functional respect for systems precisely because he sees them as made by hands like his. He defeats them at the seam, never the face. Frontal confrontation is for amateurs, drunks, and Scorpion.

**(b) Most security is theater.** Real security is rare, expensive, and recognizable by its absence of signage. The visible apparatus — cameras pointing at the obvious places, guards on standard patrol arcs, alarm decals — is the cost of insurance, not the cost of defense. Aaron's working assumption on entry to any high-value site is that the real countermeasure is the one nobody is advertising and that he will discover only by tripping it. This produces his characteristic pre-job behavior: long, patient, low-cost reconnaissance focused on what is *missing* from the apparent defenses, because the missing thing is where the actual defense lives.

**(c) People are systems with seams too.** He reads humans the same way he reads vaults. He scans for what they want and cannot ask for, what they fear and pretend not to, what they would do to keep one specific thing from being said about them. He is rarely wrong. He is also incapable of switching the scan off, which is the central deformation of his interior life — he cannot stop reading his nephew the way he reads a mark, and he knows it, and the knowing is what the 616 arc is fighting.

**(d) The universe is morally inert and operationally fair.** Aaron does not believe in cosmic justice, providence, or karmic accounting. He believes the world distributes outcomes by competence, leverage, and luck, in that order, and that complaining about the distribution is a tell of an amateur. This is why he does not present as bitter despite a life that would license bitterness. Bitterness is a posture for people who expected the world to be a different shape.

**(e) The past is a country with no roads back.** He treats history as terrain that exists but cannot be traversed. Decisions calcify on the day they are made. This is why his attempts at repair with Jefferson are so stunted; he does not believe, at a structural level, that the road exists. The 616 arc is partly the slow, embarrassed discovery that the road may exist after all — at least with Miles, possibly not with Jefferson.

---

### 6.2 Conflict — The Doctrine of Avoidance and the Geometry of Force

Aaron's conflict doctrine is **avoidance-first, leverage-second, force-third, lethality almost never**. The ordering is not moral; it is professional. Each escalation step costs more than the last, attracts more attention, generates more downstream containment work, and burns more relational capital.

- **Avoidance.** The preferred resolution to any confrontation is to not have been there. He has spent more career-hours studying egress than ingress. He thinks in routes — he will know his way out of a building before he commits to the way in, and he will know the second and third ways out before he commits to the first. He carries this into civilian space: he sits where he can see the door; he parks facing out; he picks restaurants with kitchen exits. This is not paranoia, it is hygiene.

- **Leverage.** When confrontation is unavoidable, his first instrument is information. He prefers to win an encounter by making it expensive for the other party to continue rather than by overpowering them. With Scorpion he negotiates through implied knowledge of the man's operation; with Miles, catastrophically, he weaponizes identity exposure. The leverage doctrine has one signature failure mode: it generalizes from strangers to kin, and that is the move that destroyed the Ultimate-arc relationship.

- **Force.** Applied with technical economy. Aaron's combat style on-panel is sequential, low-flourish, and aimed at incapacitation through the shortest available chain of strikes. He uses the Prowler suit's claws and projectiles as ranged stand-off tools, not as displays. He does not posture mid-fight. He does not monologue. When he does talk during violence it is to keep an opponent's cognition busy while he relocates.

- **Lethality.** Avoided as a matter of practice. Bodies generate investigations, and investigations are heat, and heat is bad for business. There is also a residue of conscience here that he will not name. He will threaten, maim, and intimidate; he is conspicuously slow to kill. The deaths in his vicinity tend to be either accidental, his own equipment turning on him, or attributable to associates he failed to control.

The deeper rule under all four tiers: **never let a fight be a fight you chose for its own sake**. Conflict in Aaron's code is always instrumental. A confrontation entered for ego, for revenge, for a point — that is the kind of decision that gets a man arrested or buried. He has watched it happen to others and he watches himself for the temptation.

---

### 6.3 Control — What He Will and Will Not Try to Govern

Aaron has a strict and idiosyncratic taxonomy of what is controllable.

- **Controllable, therefore his responsibility:** preparation, tooling, route, timing, the version of himself he chooses to present, who knows what about him, what he says in front of Miles.
- **Influenceable, therefore worth shaping but not relying on:** the behavior of partners, the dispositions of marks, the temperature of a room, his brother's willingness to be in the same space as him.
- **Uncontrollable, therefore not his department:** weather of consequence, the moral verdict of others, the past, the question of whether he is loved.

The last item is the one that does the most damage. Aaron has filed *being loved* under uncontrollable, which means he has stopped trying to earn it through any of the methods that might work — disclosure, sustained presence, accountability — and instead supplies its proxies (gifts, mentorship, access to the cool uncle). The proxies are what he can control. The thing itself he has surrendered to fate. This is why he is generous in style and bankrupt in intimacy.

A corollary belief: **control by visible force is weak; control by invisible architecture is strong**. He admires figures who arrange situations such that the desired outcome appears to be the other party's free choice. He is, in his own corrupt way, an architect of consent. This is what makes his coercion of Miles especially ugly — he understands the difference between making someone do something and making someone want to do something, and he chose the cruder option because he was in too much of a hurry, which is to say, in too much fear of losing the relationship.

---

### 6.4 Trust — The Rationing of a Scarce Resource

Aaron's trust economy is small, slow, and zero-inflation. He does not extend trust based on declarations, contracts, or affinity. He extends it based on **demonstrated behavior under cost** — what a person did when telling the truth was expensive, what they did with information they could have sold, whether they showed up when showing up was inconvenient.

Trust tiers, reconstructed:

1. **Kin-tier (one slot, occupied by Miles; vacant slot historically held by Jefferson, never reissued).** Unconditional in commitment, conditional in expression. He will lie to a kin-tier person to protect them; he will not lie to them about anything that matters to their safety. He will steal for them, bleed for them, die for them — the Ultimate arc literally tests and confirms this — and he will also, contradictorily, exploit them, because the same machinery that loves does not know how to operate without leverage.

2. **Professional-tier (small, fluid, contractual).** Fences, drivers, occasional partners. He trusts them to the limit of their visible incentives and not one inch further. He pays on time, takes calls, keeps his word on jobs — his professional reputation is meticulously maintained, because in his world reputation is the only durable asset — and assumes that any of them would sell him for the right price if the price ever materialized. The assumption is not insulting; it is the floor of the business.

3. **Civilian-tier (almost everyone else).** Treated with surface charm and zero operational disclosure. They are not enemies; they are weather. He is unfailingly polite to bartenders, doormen, app-driver dispatchers, the building super. Politeness is cheap and reduces the number of people who will remember him with specificity.

4. **Adversary-tier (handlers, coercers, anyone who thinks they own him).** Trusted to be exactly what they are. He gives them nothing, takes from them what he must, and waits for the opening to defect. The Assessor in 616 belongs here, as do the worse iterations of his Ultimate-era patrons. His reliable instinct to betray people who try to handle him is, in his code, not treachery but hygiene — the handler violated the protocol first by attempting ownership of a free operator.

The cardinal trust rule: **trust earned by demonstration can be revoked by demonstration; trust extended by category cannot be revoked at all**. Miles is in the second category. There is nothing Miles can do that will remove him from the kin-tier slot, including refusing Aaron, exposing Aaron, hating Aaron. This is the single most important fact about Aaron's interior life and the one he will go to his grave (and in Ultimate continuity does go to his grave) without articulating.

---

### 6.5 Risk — The Calculus of a Professional

Aaron's risk philosophy is more conservative than his reputation suggests. The Prowler brand reads as a high-risk identity; the man inside it is a careful actuary.

- **He distinguishes sharply between risk and recklessness.** Risk is a known cost paid for a known potential gain; recklessness is paying an unknown cost for a feeling. He has contempt for reckless operators and does not work with them twice.

- **He prices his own life lower than his own pride.** He will accept survival risks to protect his professional standing — being seen as a man who walks away, who pays out, who keeps his word — because he understands that the standing is what keeps him alive across many jobs, while the life is only worth what the standing can buy.

- **He prices Miles's life and identity above his own pride, eventually.** This is the moral arc. Early Aaron will trade Miles's security for an operational edge. Later Aaron, in both continuities, will absorb significant personal cost to keep Miles out of consequences. The shift is not from selfish to selfless; it is from short-tenor to long-tenor calculation. He realizes Miles is the only asset he holds whose value is not finite.

- **He treats his equipment as a permanent failure-risk surface.** This is forced on him by experience — the gauntlets that kill him in Ultimate are not the first time his suit has malfunctioned. He maintains and modifies obsessively, but he does not trust the gear, which is partly why he is so deadly in it: he assumes any given component will fail in the worst possible moment and plans accordingly.

- **He does not believe in luck as a resource, only as a noise floor.** He will not lean on luck. He will plan for the unlucky version of every job and execute the lucky one if it shows up.

The doctrine is roughly: **be willing to die for nothing important, because the alternative is to live for nothing at all**. Stated more cleanly: he accepts that his profession is a slow form of suicide and considers it the honest deal he made with himself in exchange for not being his brother's brother anymore.

---

### 6.6 Authority, Law, Institutions — A Practical Anarchism

Aaron is not an ideologue. He has no anti-state theory. His relationship with institutional authority is purely operational and faintly tired.

- **Police** are an environmental hazard. Not enemies, not legitimate, just present — to be evaded, mapped, and respected for what they are capable of when properly motivated. His brother's police career in 616 puts a permanent crackle on this attitude that he will not name.

- **Corporations** (Oscorp paradigmatically) are richer marks than people, structurally less innocent than people, and therefore easier to steal from with a clean conscience. He does not romanticize this; it is simply true that taking something from Norman Osborn requires less psychological maintenance than taking something from a person.

- **Organized crime** is a labor environment with worse benefits and better margins than legitimate work. He treats crime bosses the way a freelancer treats clients — be on time, do the work, don't get attached, get paid, leave. He resists being absorbed into any organization because absorption means losing the freelancer's exit.

- **Government, in the abstract** — he has no opinion. He votes (or doesn't) on no recorded axis. Politics in Aaron's worldview is something other people do to fill the hours he spends working.

- **Vigilantes / costumed actors.** Treated as a weather system of unusual intensity. He neither idolizes nor despises them. Spider-Man specifically, before Miles, was a logistical problem; Miles-as-Spider-Man is a category collapse that he has spent both continuities trying to metabolize.

The underlying belief: **legitimacy is a story institutions tell about themselves to lower their enforcement costs**. He does not contest the story. He just does not pay the discount.

---

### 6.7 Money — The Instrument He Will Not Worship

Aaron steals for money and does not love money. This is a meaningful distinction.

Money in his code is **fuel and proof**. Fuel because it pays for the next job's prep, the apartment, the gifts for Miles, the maintenance on the suit. Proof because the size of a take is the only public scoreboard his profession offers, and he keeps score. But he does not accumulate. He has no recorded interest in wealth as security, in property, in passive income, in legacy assets. The lifestyle on-panel is consistently middle-tier: decent apartment, reliable car, no conspicuous consumption. The 616 turn to app-driving is not a humiliation he hides; it is, for him, just another way of paying for the apartment.

He treats people who love money for its own sake as he treats people who fight for fun: with the dismissive professional pity of a man who knows that confusing the medium for the message ends careers.

---

### 6.8 Family — The Only Theology He Has

He does not have a religion. He has Miles. He had, and structurally still has, Jefferson. Everything that other men route through faith — meaning, judgment, salvation, the wish to be known — Aaron routes through the family axis.

Operating beliefs:

- **Blood is not magic, but the people you grew up frightened with are the only ones whose verdict on you is real.** Jefferson's verdict on Aaron — that he is the brother who could not be saved — is the sentence Aaron has been serving and contesting his entire adult life.

- **You owe the next generation an unforced version of yourself.** This is the principle he violates most often and returns to most reliably. The Ultimate arc is the violation; the 616 arc is the return. He believes, accurately, that Miles deserves an uncle who is not running a play on him, and he is sometimes capable of being that uncle for stretches of time before the old machinery resumes.

- **A family member's contempt is not a thing to be defended against; it is a thing to be earned out of.** He does not argue with Miles when Miles is disgusted with him. He absorbs it. He thinks the absorption is the price. This is one of his best qualities and one of the few places his pride is genuinely silent.

- **You do not bring the work home.** Repeatedly violated, repeatedly repented. The deep wish behind the principle is the wish for a domestic space that does not have to be scanned on entry — a wish he has not had fulfilled since boyhood and may have stopped believing is available to him.

---

### 6.9 The Self — How He Locates Himself in the World

Aaron's self-location is precise and stripped-down.

- **He is a craftsman first.** If asked what he is — and he would not answer honestly — the truthful answer is *a working professional in a specialized trade*. The trade happens to be illegal. The pride is in the work, not in the illegality.

- **He is a younger brother who became an older man without ever being made the older brother.** Jefferson took the senior role by moral default when Aaron disqualified himself. Aaron has never been anyone's elder in the way Jefferson is Miles's father. With Miles he is trying, awkwardly, to occupy a kind of avuncular eldership without the standing to claim it. He knows the standing is borrowed.

- **He is the cautionary tale.** He knows this is the function he serves in Jefferson's household — the story you tell the boy about what not to become. The 616 arc is partly the project of becoming a cautionary tale who lived long enough to revise his own moral. He does not expect to be remembered well. He has decided he can live with being remembered accurately, and that this would be more than he was previously going to get.

- **He is not, in his own estimation, a bad man — but he is not arguing the point.** The internal verdict is more complicated than the external posture. He thinks of himself as a man who made a series of survivable decisions in a bad environment and accumulated, by survival, a debt he cannot fully repay. He does not request mercy from himself, and he does not extend it to himself either. He simply continues.

---

### 6.10 The Operational Code, Distilled

If reduced to the short list of rules he actually executes against, the code reads approximately:

1. Know the exits before you commit to the entrance.
2. The advertised security is not the real security; find the quiet one.
3. Read the room for what nobody is admitting they want.
4. Win by leverage; spend force as a last resort; spend lethality almost never.
5. Reputation is the only durable asset. Pay on time. Keep your word on jobs. Do not be the man who flinches.
6. Trust by demonstrated cost, not by category — except for kin, which is a slot you do not revoke.
7. Treat handlers as obstacles. The first opening to defect from a handler is the correct one.
8. The gear will eventually try to kill you. Plan for that.
9. The past is closed terrain. Stop trying to walk back into it; build forward from where you are.
10. Do not bring the work home. When you bring it home, that is the day you become the warning.
11. Miles does not get the version of you that other people get. Miles gets the unforced one or none at all. (Aspirational; intermittently honored; the through-line of the reform arc.)
12. The world does not owe a verdict. Earn the verdict you can live with from the small number of people whose verdict you cannot dismiss.

---

### 6.11 Internal Contradictions in the Code

A complete worldview file must flag where the code breaks against itself. Aaron's principal internal contradictions:

- **Rule 4 (leverage over force) vs. Rule 11 (Miles gets the unforced version).** Aaron's instinct to leverage everyone collides directly with his commitment to not leverage his nephew. He loses this collision repeatedly and catastrophically in Ultimate. He wins it more often than he loses in 616. The struggle is the man.

- **Rule 6 (trust by cost) vs. Rule 11 (kin is uncategorical).** He has installed a permanent override on his own trust accounting for a single person. This makes him predictable to anyone who knows where the override is, which is the vulnerability the Assessor and others have repeatedly exploited.

- **Rule 9 (the past is closed) vs. the entire Jefferson axis.** He cannot reach his brother because of Rule 9; he cannot stop trying to reach his brother because Jefferson is the original addressee. The unresolvable tension between the rule and the wish is what gives his interior life its particular weight.

- **The craftsman-pride frame vs. the cautionary-tale acceptance.** He believes both that his work is good and that his life is a warning. He has not synthesized these and probably will not.

These are not weaknesses in the code. They are the places where the code, accurately, refuses to lie about a man who is genuinely two things at once.

---

*End Section 6. See Section 7 (Interpersonal Pattern: Dyadic Operational Profiles) for application of the code against named relations — Jefferson Davis, Miles Morales, Rio Morales, the Assessor, Scorpion, and incidental professional contacts.*


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — Moral & Ethical Framework

*The code as enacted across the published behavioral record, not as Aaron would describe it if asked. Aaron does not articulate ethics. He performs them, and the performance is consistent enough to be reverse-engineered.*

---

### 6.1 The Operative Code (Enacted Rules, in Descending Order of Stability)

What follows is the ordering observable in practice — the priority queue the record actually demonstrates when two rules collide. The order matters; Aaron is not a man of principles but a man of priorities, and the priorities are stable even when the principles aren't.

**Rule 1 — Blood is non-negotiable. Specifically: the boy.**
The most durable line in the entire file. Across both continuities, Aaron will burn jobs, betray partners, eat losses, and ultimately die rather than allow direct lethal harm to come to Miles by his hand or with his consent. Note the qualifier "direct" and "lethal" — the rule does not prohibit using Miles, lying to Miles, extorting Miles, or putting Miles in danger Aaron believes he can control. It prohibits Miles being killed or maimed on Aaron's account. This is a much narrower rule than "I love my nephew," and the gap between the rule he keeps and the rule a healthy uncle would keep is most of his pathology.

**Rule 2 — Non-combatants are off the board.**
He will rob a vault, beat a guard, threaten a fence, and gut-punch a rival operator without hesitation. He will not, on the record, kill a civilian for convenience or torture a non-participant for information. The 616 arc clarifies and hardens this: when he stumbles into trafficking-adjacent operations, the moral floor activates with surprising force and overrides self-interest. This is consistent enough across decades of published material to be treated as a real internal line, not a writerly softening — Bendis's Ultimate Aaron already declines several available cruelties Ahmed's 616 Aaron later refuses more loudly.

**Rule 3 — Children are sacred.**
A subspecies of Rule 2, but operating with stricter enforcement and broader scope. Any minor, not just Miles. The trafficking subplot in 616 demonstrates that this rule will override Rule 4 (self-preservation) and Rule 5 (loyalty to working partners). The rule predates and is independent of his attachment to Miles; he does not become a child-protector because of Miles, he is one because of something older — almost certainly the unspoken content of his and Jefferson's shared childhood, which the canon does not fully render but which Aaron's reflexes describe.

**Rule 4 — Self-preservation.**
Surprisingly low. Aaron is not reckless in the borderline-suicidal sense, but he ranks his own survival below the three rules above and roughly equal with the rule below. He will accept significant personal risk for craft pride, for Miles, for a non-combatant he has decided to shield. The Ultimate-era death is, in part, a Rule 4 failure — he gambles past survivable margins because Rules 1 and 7 are collapsing simultaneously.

**Rule 5 — Loyalty to working partners while the contract is active, and only then.**
Aaron honors deals in progress. He will not sell out a crew mid-job. After a job concludes, all loyalty obligations expire; he is a free agent and treats former colleagues as future obstacles or future marks. This is professional ethics in the older underworld sense — trustworthy in the room, no obligations at the door. The Scorpion episodes in Ultimate map this perfectly: he works clean while working, and the moment the relationship turns coercive (i.e., the partner attempts to make Aaron a permanent asset rather than a contracted one), the loyalty terminates immediately and is replaced with active hostility.

**Rule 6 — Craft over greed.**
He would rather do a clean small job than a sloppy large one. He looks down on operators who take stupid risks, who hurt people unnecessarily, who use ten units of force when three would suffice. This is partly aesthetic, partly tactical, but it functions ethically: it removes a category of harm from his behavior that pure profit-maximization would have included. His contempt for the Scorpion's operation is not just professional snobbery; it is a moral judgment dressed as a craft judgment, and the moral content is "he hurts people when he doesn't have to."

**Rule 7 — Be seen as competent.**
Not technically an ethical rule, but it functions as one because it constrains his behavior. He will not take jobs that humiliate him, will not be visibly handled by another principal, will not occupy the subordinate position in a hierarchy he respects. This rule's instability is what the Assessor exploits in 616 — coercion that threatens exposure threatens not just Aaron's freedom but his self-image, and the self-image is more load-bearing than the freedom.

**Rule 8 — Honesty to Miles, conditional.**
The youngest rule, almost entirely a 616 development, and the most fragile. Aaron in the Ultimate arc lies to Miles constantly and with technique. Aaron in the 616 arc tries — visibly, effortfully, imperfectly — not to. When he lies to 616-Miles, he lies smaller and confesses faster. This is the rule that signals the reform is real: a new entry in the priority queue, still being load-tested, still occasionally failing under stress.

---

### 6.2 What He Will Do (Enacted, Not Hypothetical)

- **Steal at any scale** — petty to corporate-grade. No internal hierarchy of property worth protecting. Oscorp, banks, private collectors, fences, rival criminals: all licit targets.
- **Use violence instrumentally** against armed opponents, security, rival operators, and anyone who has accepted combatant status by entering an operational space armed.
- **Threaten, intimidate, and coerce** — including by leveraging information he has no moral right to (Miles's identity being the master example).
- **Manipulate kin** — the most damning category and the one he most resists naming. He instrumentalizes Miles's affection, Miles's powers, and Miles's fear of Jefferson's discovery. He does this while sincerely loving the boy. The simultaneity is the file's central moral fact.
- **Lie comprehensively** to law enforcement, to partners, to marks, to Jefferson (in any flashback or implied reconstruction), and — in Ultimate — to Miles.
