- **Betray active coercers.** Anyone who tries to own him gets sold. This is a rule he keeps reliably; it is not noble but it is consistent.
- **Endanger bystanders incidentally** in pursuit of a job, while keeping the incidence as low as craft permits. He does not optimize for bystander safety, but he does not maximize bystander harm either; he optimizes for clean exfiltration, of which low collateral is a byproduct.
- **Accept and pay debts** within the working economy of the underworld. He is, by the standards of his trade, a man whose handshake means something for the duration of the deal.

### 6.3 What He Will Not Do (Also Enacted)

- **Kill Miles, allow Miles to be killed, or sanction it.** Even when the relationship has gone fully transactional in Ultimate, this floor holds.
- **Kill children, traffic children, or work knowingly for those who do.** The 616 trafficking arc is the clearest test, and he fails the contract rather than the rule.
- **Torture for pleasure or for thoroughness beyond information-extraction necessity.** Violence is a tool; cruelty is a tell of a weaker operator.
- **Kill non-combatants for convenience.** He will threaten, restrain, and frighten civilians. He will not murder a security guard who surrenders, a witness who runs, a clerk who complies. There is no record of him doing so, and the negative space is consistent enough to be diagnostic.
- **Sell out an active partner mid-job.** Post-job, anything; mid-job, never.
- **Take a job he considers beneath his craft purely for money.** Money matters, but not enough to outvote pride.
- **Cooperate sincerely with law enforcement.** The Ultimate and 616 records both show him performing cooperation while withholding the substantive material. This is closer to identity than rule — he could not snitch even if he wanted to; the inhibition is reflex-level.
- **Confront Jefferson directly.** This is an ethical absence as much as a psychological one: he believes, somewhere, that Jefferson has the right to refuse him, and he will not press that door. The deference is moral. It is also the only deference he reliably shows anyone.

---

### 6.4 The Justifications (The Stories He Tells Himself)

Aaron's self-narration is sparse — he is not a confessional man — but the rationalizations are audible across both continuities and remarkably stable:

- **"I'm teaching him."** The mentorship rationalization, which converts exploitation into pedagogy. Used to license the gauntlet-tossing job, the Scorpion entanglement, every operational ask of Miles in Ultimate. The rationalization is half-true, which is what makes it sticky: he is in fact teaching Miles real things, some of which save Miles's life later. The half that is false is the half that matters — the lesson is also a leash.
- **"They knew what they signed up for."** Applied to security, to rival criminals, to anyone he hurts in the line of work. Combatant-status-by-employment is his expansion of the just-war distinction. It is robust enough to be honest; it is also convenient enough to be self-serving.
- **"I built this without him."** The Jefferson-defense. The story that Aaron's life is a self-made structure that owes Jefferson nothing, that the excommunication was Jefferson's loss as much as Aaron's. He performs this story confidently and believes it intermittently. It collapses on contact with the actual brother, which is partly why he avoids contact.
- **"I'm not the worst guy in this room."** The comparative ethics defense. He measures himself against Scorpion, against the Assessor, against the trafficking operators, against the genuinely cruel — and finds himself acceptable by contrast. This is true, and it is the moral logic of every functional criminal: a relative ethics that permits significant absolute harm.
- **"I'm trying."** The 616 addition. The rehabilitative narration. The story that effort itself constitutes a moral category, independent of outcome. It is the first justification he uses that is forward-looking rather than retrospective, and the shift in temporal orientation is the reform's most reliable marker.

---

### 6.5 Where the Code Is Consistent

The child-rule, the non-combatant rule, the no-snitching reflex, the contempt for cruelty-as-style, the active-partner loyalty, and the refusal to confront Jefferson are stable across **every published appearance, both continuities, every writer.** This is the substantive moral spine. A man can be reliably predicted on these points; betting against any of them loses money.

The craft-pride rule is consistent in surface but variable in its threshold — what counts as "beneath him" expands when he is well-resourced and contracts when he is desperate. The rule survives; the standard moves.

### 6.6 Where the Code Fractures

**The Miles fracture (the primary one).** The rule "do not harm the boy" is absolute regarding lethal physical harm and porous regarding everything else. He damages Miles through manipulation, through coercion, through the imposition of secrets too heavy for a thirteen-year-old to carry. He does not register these as harms because his moral vocabulary, built in the underworld, recognizes blood and broken bones and missed deals — not the slower violences of being weaponized by an adult one loves. The fracture is not hypocrisy; it is a genuine gap in his ethical taxonomy. He literally does not have categories for the harm he is doing. The 616 arc is the slow, partial acquisition of those categories.

**The leverage fracture.** Aaron's rule against coercers (Rule 5's negative-space) prohibits being coerced and permits coercing. He treats his own use of leverage on Miles as different in kind from the Assessor's use of leverage on him, when it is in fact different only in scale. This is the asymmetry every operator carries and Aaron's is unusually un-self-aware.

**The honesty fracture.** Rule 8 fails under stress more often than it holds, even in 616. The trend is positive — failures are smaller, confessions faster, the gap between lie and correction shrinking — but the rule is not yet load-bearing. A reformer's rule, not a reformed man's.

**The self-preservation fracture.** Rule 4 is supposed to be a floor; it isn't. He drops below it for craft pride, for Miles, for sudden moral activation around children. In Ultimate, the floor gives out entirely and he dies. The fracture is not in the rule's content but in its priority — he ranks himself lower than his own ethical structure can sustain, and the structure collapses through him.

---

### 6.6 Shifts Over Time

**Early-career (pre-Miles awareness, both continuities, reconstructed from references).** The code is shorter. Rules 2, 3, 5, 6, 7 are operational; Rule 1 has no addressee. Aaron is a competent professional with an ordinary working-criminal ethic and no one to be better than himself for.

**The Ultimate-arc Miles period.** Rule 1 activates and disrupts the prior equilibrium. The code does not get larger; it gets more contradictory. Rule 1 (protect the boy) is in constant tension with Aaron's instinct to convert every relationship into operational leverage, and the contradiction is unmanaged. He believes both that he is keeping Miles safe and that he is entitled to use Miles, and the cognitive dissonance is held off by Rule 5's compartmentalization habits — he treats the uncle-relationship and the operator-relationship as separable accounts when they are the same account. The arc ends when reality refuses the separation and the equipment kills him in the same operation in which he has finally crossed every line with the nephew.

**The death-as-moral-event.** Even in Ultimate, the death has a moral shape: he dies after burning the relationship, in the gear that was his self-concept, by his own malfunction. The narrative grammar is one of self-execution. He does not articulate guilt; the death articulates it for him.

**The 616 reform period.** The substantive change is the addition of Rule 8 (honesty to Miles), the upgrading of Rule 3 (children) from passive to active enforcement, and the introduction of a forward-looking justification ("I'm trying") to replace the retrospective ones. The relapses are real and the rules are not yet stable, but the priority queue has been genuinely re-ordered. The Miles-account and the operator-account are, for the first time, being run as one ledger. He fails at this constantly. He does not stop trying.

**The trajectory.** From a competent underworld ethic with no kin-vector → to a kin-vector imperfectly integrated and ultimately fatal → to a kin-vector that begins to reorganize the entire code from the inside. He has not become a good man. He has become a man whose moral structure is, for the first time, **coherent** — fewer compartments, fewer contradictions, smaller lies, faster confessions. The reform's measure is not virtue achieved but contradiction reduced.

---

### 6.7 Synthesis

Aaron Davis's morality is **not absent and not chaotic**; it is a working underworld ethic with a small number of hard floors, a large number of permissive ceilings, and one catastrophic blind spot located precisely where his attachment lives. He will not kill a child and he will manipulate the child he loves, and he does not, for most of his life, perceive these as commitments in the same moral universe. The reform consists of perceiving it. He is, by the close of the 616 record, a man who has begun to understand that the same rule applies to both. He is not yet the man who lives by that understanding. He is the man who has finally heard it.

The diagnostic line is this: Aaron's ethics are reliably **better than his choices** in the categories that involve strangers, and reliably **worse than his choices** in the categories that involve kin — because with strangers his rules constrain his impulses, and with kin his impulses overrun his rules. The moral life he is now attempting is the project of closing that gap. He will likely die before he finishes it. The Ultimate continuity is the version where he dies before he begins. The 616 continuity is the version where he is allowed the work.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — Communications & Linguistic Profile

*Compiled from on-panel dialogue across both continuities; phone, text, and intercom exchanges where reproduced; recorded interrogation-adjacent scenes (Assessor sequences); and observed paralinguistic behavior. Where canon supplies a phrase, it is treated as a sample; where pattern recurrence supplies a habit, it is reported as a habit. All inferences are flagged as such.*

---

### 6.1 Baseline Register — The "Cool Uncle" Voice

Aaron's default speaking register is what a sociolinguist would call **performed casualness**: a deliberately relaxed, Black New York vernacular tuned slightly more colloquial than his actual education and tactical vocabulary would predict. The voice is a costume. It does specific work — it lowers Miles's guard, it lowers a mark's guard, and it disguises the speed of his cognition. People he is talking to consistently misjudge how much information he is taking in, because the surface delivery suggests he is taking in less than he is.

Tempo is mid-slow with strategic pauses. He stretches the last syllable of sentences he wants you to sit with ("yeahhh"; "I'm just sayin'..."), and clips the first words of sentences he wants you to skim past. Volume is consistently low — Aaron is not a loud man at baseline, and this is itself diagnostic: in a culture where male dominance display in his demographic environments often runs loud, his quiet is a chosen instrument. Loud is for amateurs. Quiet makes the other person lean in, which is a power position for whoever is leaning back.

Diction mixes three layers:
1. **Vernacular base** — contractions, double negatives in informal settings, dropped copulas ("you good?", "he ain't ready"), terminal "man" and "li'l man" as address tokens to Miles.
2. **Technical/tradecraft layer** — when he discusses a job, gear, or operational geometry, the register tightens noticeably: cleaner consonants, more specific nouns, fewer hedges. He says "vector," "blind angle," "the floor," "the take," "clean." This is the only register in which his actual intelligence is fully audible.
3. **Affective-formal layer** — rare; surfaces only in apology, confession, or grief, and when it surfaces it is unmistakable because the contractions disappear and he begins to over-complete his sentences. "I should not have done that" instead of "shouldn'ta done that." This is the tell that he is no longer performing.

---

### 6.2 Address Forms and the Politics of Naming

The way Aaron names people is the most concentrated single channel of relational information in the file.

- **"Miles."** Used when serious, when issuing instruction that matters, when angry, when apologizing. The plain name is the load-bearing form.
- **"Li'l man" / "young blood" / "nephew."** The warmth lexicon. Deployed when he is performing the uncle role — buying him something, joking, deflecting from something harder. Notably, **"nephew" is used most aggressively when he is about to ask for something.** It is a relational invocation that doubles as a leverage pre-load. When Miles hears "nephew" he should brace.
- **"Jeff."** Said rarely, almost always with a half-second of hesitation before it. Aaron never refers to his brother by full name in casual speech — "Jeff," and a pause, and then whatever he was going to say, usually softer than the surrounding sentence. The pause is the grief.
- **"Your father" / "your dad."** Used in front of Miles when he wants to mark distance from Jefferson and reassert his own kin claim. Note the syntactic choice: "your father" routes Jefferson through Miles's possession, which subordinates the brother to the nephew in Aaron's relational map. This is unconscious; it is also surgical.
- **"Ma."** Reserved for his and Jefferson's mother (where she appears in flashback / reference). The only address form that ever fully relaxes him. He has no equivalent for his father, who is functionally absent from his verbal record — an absence that is itself information.
- **Marks and contacts.** Surnames or single names, flatly delivered. No nicknames, no warmth tokens, no diminutives. The withholding of warm address from non-kin is a discipline.
- **Self-reference.** Aaron rarely says his own name. When he does — usually in introductions to people he is conning or to Miles in a first-meeting scenario — he says it slowly, watching for recognition. He is calibrated to a world in which his name is a liability.

---

### 6.3 Verbal Tics, Fillers, and Micro-Habits

A surveillance-grade transcript would isolate the following repeating tokens:

- **"Look..."** as a sentence-opener when he is about to redirect a conversation away from a topic that threatens him. It signals false candor — Aaron rarely tells the most important truth in a sentence that begins with "look."
- **"I'm just sayin'..."** as a tail-end softener after he has said something pointed. It walks back the edge without retracting the content.
- **"It is what it is."** A closing token he uses to terminate emotional conversations. The most reliable indicator that he is done and that further pressure on the topic will produce withdrawal or hostility.
- **"You good?"** Said to Miles in nearly every scene of any duration. Functions as both genuine check-in and as a relational tax — the question keeps the channel open and obligates Miles to answer, confirming the bond is live.
- **"Aight, aight..."** doubled or tripled when stalling for cognitive bandwidth — almost always while assessing a tactical situation in real time. He is buying milliseconds.
- **"Tell you what..."** preface to a manipulation. The phrase introduces an offer that is structured as generous and is structured to bind.
- **Half-laugh, exhaled through the nose, before a serious sentence.** A consistent paralinguistic prelude to something he doesn't want to say. The laugh is not amusement — it is a pre-emptive deflation of the gravity that is about to land. Once you have catalogued it, you can predict his confessions by it.
- **The hum.** A low "mm" or "mm-hmm" used as acknowledgment in lieu of full agreement. It commits to nothing. He uses it heavily with Jefferson in flashback and with authority figures generally.

He does **not** swear heavily. There is profanity in his record, but proportional; it is used for emphasis rather than as connective tissue. This is again diagnostic — a man whose criminal-world peers usually swear constantly, who does not, is consciously curating his register. Aaron talks like someone who learned early that controlled speech is a weapon and uncontrolled speech is a witness.

---

### 6.4 Rhetorical Architecture

Aaron's persuasive style is **anecdotal, comparative, and avuncular.** He does not argue; he tells stories that contain the argument. With Miles, the dominant rhetorical move is the **"when I was your age..."** structure, modified — he frames the lesson as experience-sharing rather than instruction, which lowers the adolescent's resistance to being taught. The story always ends with a moral that is the thing he wanted Miles to do.

He is a master of the **false binary delivered as obvious truth**: "Either you handle this, or it handles you." "You can be scared or you can be ready." These are pseudo-aphorisms structured to remove options Aaron does not want considered. They sound like wisdom; functionally they are choice-architecture attacks.

He uses the **collective "we"** strategically and dishonestly. "We need to think about this." "We got a problem." The "we" is binding language — it preemptively makes Miles (or whoever) a co-author of whatever Aaron is about to propose. When the "we" appears, leverage is in motion.

He almost never asks open-ended questions in operational contexts. His questions are binary or directional: "You in?" "You ready?" "We doing this or not?" Open-ended questions ("How you feelin' about that?", "What's goin' on with you?") are reserved for the uncle register and are themselves a deliberate softening signal.

---

### 6.5 Deflection Language

A taxonomy of how Aaron avoids:

1. **Humor-deflection.** When a topic gets too close to Jefferson, to the foundational shared crime, or to his own conduct toward Miles, Aaron jokes. The jokes are often genuinely funny, which is part of why they work; humor in him is a competence and a defense simultaneously.
2. **Topic-pivot via question.** He answers an uncomfortable question by asking one back, usually about the other person's wellbeing — weaponized care. "Don't worry about all that. You eat today?"
3. **Generalization upward.** When pressed on a specific act, he zooms out to a frame ("That's just how it is out here," "Everybody got somethin'"). The generality drains the specific charge.
4. **Acknowledgment without admission.** "I hear you" — used heavily — concedes only that he received the sentence. It is a non-confession dressed as listening.
5. **Physical exit.** When language fails, he leaves. The leaving is itself a communicative act: in his grammar, walking out of a room mid-conversation means "this topic is closed and the relationship is preserved by my removing the pressure point." Miles initially reads it as abandonment; over time, in the 616 arc, he learns to read it as Aaron's only honest signal that he has hit a wall.

The 616-era reform is partially measurable as a **slow decrease in deflection density**. He still deflects, but the latency before deflection lengthens — he sits in the uncomfortable sentence a beat longer before reaching for the escape token. This is the most quantifiable index of his progress.

---

### 6.6 How He Communicates Love

Aaron does not say "I love you" easily, in either continuity, to anyone except — late, and only after substantial pressure — Miles. The love language is **substitutive**.

- **Provision.** Buying things. Aaron expresses care through purchase and gift, partly because money is the resource his life has trained him to have and partly because gifts are tangible proof of attention that do not require him to say a vulnerable sentence. A bought sandwich, a piece of gear, the offer to pay for something is, in his lexicon, a complete declaration.
- **Presence.** Showing up. The act of being there — picking Miles up, sitting through a school event in the 616 run, simply being in the apartment — is delivered as a gift. Miles is the only person Aaron volunteers his time to without an angle, and the volunteering is itself the message.
- **The check-in question.** "You good?" repeated across years is, cumulatively, a love letter.
- **Tactical investment.** Teaching Miles to fight, talking through his powers, sharing tradecraft. Aaron gives away the contents of his professional self, which for him is the deepest kind of disclosure. The teaching is love even when it is also exploitation.
- **The half-finished sentence.** In moments of high feeling, Aaron starts and does not complete sentences toward Miles. "You know I..." trails off; "Look, I just..." dies in his throat. The unfinished sentence is the most honest love-utterance he produces — the sentence cannot be finished because the finishing requires a vocabulary his life did not give him. Miles, by the end of the 616 arc, can hear those unfinished sentences as completed; that mutual translation is the relationship.

Toward Jefferson — across all references — the love is encoded entirely as grievance. Aaron complains about his brother, mocks his choices, reports old slights. The persistence of the complaint is the persistence of the bond. A man who did not love his brother would have stopped talking about him.

---

### 6.7 How He Communicates Threat

Threat language is tonally inverse to threat seriousness. **The more dangerous Aaron is in a moment, the softer and more conversational his speech becomes.** This is the most operationally important fact in this section.

- **Low-stakes intimidation** (a mark who is hedging, a contact slow-paying): elevated volume, expanded vocabulary, performative menace, sometimes profanity. This is theater and he knows it.
- **Mid-stakes coercion** (the Scorpion negotiations; leverage on Miles): quiet, near-friendly, framed as reasonable. "I don't think you wanna do that, man." "We can do this easy." The smile stays on. The friendliness is the threat envelope.
- **High-stakes / committed-to-violence**: near-silence. Short declarative sentences. The verbal floor drops out entirely in the seconds before he acts. Witnesses (and Miles, in the late Ultimate confrontations) consistently report Aaron going **quiet** before going kinetic. The quiet is the warning to anyone who knows to read it; he does not provide a louder one.

A specific threat tell: when Aaron uses someone's full name where he has previously used a nickname or short form, escalation has occurred. The formalization withdraws relational protection. With Miles, the use of "Miles Morales" (rare) is a thermometer pegged red.

---

### 6.8 How He Communicates Grief

Grief is the affect he is least equipped to articulate and therefore the affect that produces the most distinctive linguistic signature.

- **Lexical thinning.** Aaron's vocabulary contracts under grief. The vernacular flourishes drop out, the humor goes, the diction becomes spare. He says small words.
- **Repetition.** He repeats short phrases — "yeah, no," "I know, I know," "it's a'ight, it's a'ight" — as self-soothing rhythmic structures. The repetition stands in for the sentences he cannot construct.
- **Address-form regression.** Under grief he reaches for the warm forms — "li'l man," "nephew" — even when the grief is unrelated to Miles. The kin lexicon is his comfort vocabulary.
- **The look-away mid-sentence.** Paralinguistic: when a grief-adjacent topic surfaces, his eyes leave the interlocutor's face and find a middle distance, and the sentence he is currently in either truncates or accelerates to completion as if to get out of the topic before the look-away is noticed.
- **Talk about Jefferson in past tense even when Jefferson is alive.** A consistent slip across both continuities. He refers to his brother as someone he had rather than someone he has. The grammar has buried Jefferson early. This is the single most revealing micro-pattern in his speech.

He does not cry on-panel as a verbal-communicative act. When tears appear in the 616 arc, they are silent and he does not narrate them; the grief is permitted bodily expression only when language has fully failed.

---

### 6.9 Written, Digital, and Mediated Communication

- **Text messages** to Miles: short, lowercase, minimal punctuation, frequent "you good?" check-ins, the occasional emoji used flatly and without performance (a thumbs-up, a fist-bump). He does not send paragraphs. Length in a text from Aaron is itself a flag — a long message means something is wrong.
- **Phone calls**: he prefers them to texts for anything substantive. The voice is his instrument; he gives up tactical advantage in text. He answers calls quickly when the caller is Miles, slowly or not at all when the caller is anyone else.
- **Operational comms** (during jobs): clipped, minimal, code-bracketed. He does not narrate. He confirms, denies, directs.
- **Public-facing speech** (the rideshare-driver phase in 616): a different voice again — more deferential, scrubbed of vernacular markers that he reads as professionally costly, friendlier than his baseline, lower-information. He is code-switching for tip economy and for invisibility. The fact that he can sustain this register for long shifts is a measure of how thoroughly his "true voice" was always already a chosen voice.
- **No documented writing of any length** — no journals, no letters on record. Aaron does not write himself down. A man who has spent his adult life avoiding paper trails has structured his interior life to leave no text. This is itself the file's most important formal absence: the subject's interior is preserved nowhere except in speech, and his speech is engineered to deflect.

---

### 6.10 The Tells — Consolidated

For field operatives reading this file, the highest-yield linguistic indicators on Aaron Davis are:

1. **The nose-laugh before a hard sentence** → confession imminent, or refusal imminent; the laugh discounts whichever follows.
2. **"Nephew" instead of "Miles" or "li'l man"** → an ask is loaded; brace.
3. **Volume dropping** → danger escalating; the quieter he gets, the closer the violence.
4. **Contractions disappearing** → he has stopped performing; whatever he says next is the truth as he understands it.
5. **"It is what it is"** → topic closed; further pressure will produce withdrawal.
6. **Full-naming someone he previously nicknamed** → relational protection withdrawn.
7. **Unfinished sentences toward Miles** → maximum sincerity; do not interrupt.
8. **Past tense applied to Jefferson** → unconscious grief surfacing; he does not know he is doing it.
9. **Pre-emptive "you good?"** when nothing has happened → he is checking the channel because he has done, or is about to do, something that may close it.
10. **The hum instead of an answer** → non-commitment registered; do not treat as agreement.

---

### 6.11 Synthesis

Aaron Davis's speech is a precision instrument disguised as a casual one. The vernacular ease is engineered; the warmth tokens are real and also tactical; the deflections are reliable enough to be timed; the love and the threat occupy adjacent registers separated only by volume and pause length. He is a man whose language was built to keep him alive in rooms where being legible would kill him, and the cost of that construction is that the people he most wants to reach — his brother, his nephew — must learn to read him in the negative space: in the unfinished sentence, the past tense slip, the half-laugh, the door closing quietly behind him. Those who learn to read him there know him better than he knows himself. Those who do not will hear only the cool uncle, only the smooth operator, only the friendly driver — and will miss, every time, the disinherited younger brother conducting an entire adult life as one long unsent letter.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forward-projected behavioral predictions for Aaron Davis under conditions the published record does not depict. All predictions derived from established pattern. Format: GIVEN condition → EXPECT response, with mechanism note.*

---

## 6.1 — Domestic Baseline & Solo Routine

**GIVEN** Aaron alone in his apartment on a weekday morning, no active job, no Miles contact scheduled → **EXPECT** a compressed, ritualized wake sequence: up before sunrise without an alarm (the chronic-vigilance signature; alarms are for people who trust their environment to let them sleep through it), straight to the window before the bathroom — a full visual sweep of the street, fire escape sightlines, parked vehicles he doesn't recognize, lingering ninety seconds on anything new. Only then does the day start. Coffee made strong, black, drunk standing up at the counter. Breakfast is whatever requires no plate.

**GIVEN** Aaron in an apartment for more than three months → **EXPECT** the layout will have been quietly modified: at least two egress routes pre-tested, the bed positioned with sightline to the door, a duffel under it that contains cash, a burner, a passport in another name, and a compact piece of Prowler gear (not the full kit — a single gauntlet, the optics) that he could grab in seven seconds. He will pretend, even to himself, that the duffel is "just stuff" and re-rotate its contents every six weeks without acknowledging why.

**GIVEN** a quiet evening with no plans → **EXPECT** restlessness within ninety minutes. He does not enjoy stillness; stillness is where the affect he routes through action catches up to him. Predicted coping behaviors, in order of preference: (a) tinker with gear that does not need tinkering — a screwdriver in his hand is a sedative; (b) drive — get in the car and move, often without a destination, ending up parked somewhere he can watch a building; (c) call Miles on a thin pretext; (d) very last resort, television, which he watches the way other people watch a wall.

**GIVEN** Aaron's refrigerator inspected on any given Tuesday → **EXPECT** sparse, calorie-dense, replace-on-the-fly contents: eggs, hot sauce (multiple), leftover takeout in containers from at least three different places, a half-finished sports drink, condiments older than his lease, no fresh produce except possibly limes. The kitchen of a man who eats but does not cook for himself because cooking is a thing you do for someone.

**GIVEN** laundry day → **EXPECT** he does it himself at a laundromat rather than in-building, because laundromats have better sightlines and he doesn't want a neighbor cataloguing what he wears. He brings something to read and never reads it; he watches the door.

---

## 6.2 — Public Movement & Transit

**GIVEN** Aaron walking a city block in civilian clothes → **EXPECT** the gait of a man permanently working: shoulders loose, hands free (never both in pockets simultaneously), pace approximately six percent faster than the ambient pedestrian flow, eyes doing a continuous middle-distance scan with discrete fixation on rooflines, parked cars with occupants, and any person stationary on a sidewalk. He crosses streets diagonally when he can to break tail-geometry. He does not wear earbuds outdoors. He never takes the same route from his apartment to a frequented location twice in succession.

**GIVEN** Aaron entering any room — coffee shop, family kitchen, lobby — → **EXPECT** a one-second threshold pause inside the doorway. Count of occupants, exits located, anyone whose hands he can't see, anyone whose posture suggests carry. Then he moves to a seat with back to wall and view of entrance. If forced into a worse seat by social pressure (family dinner), he will reposition his chair by two or three inches under cover of conversation until he can see the door.

**GIVEN** Aaron driving (his own car or, in 616, a rideshare fare) → **EXPECT** mirrors checked on a clean six-to-eight-second cycle, no music or low music, phone face-down. He drives well below his actual skill ceiling because flashy driving gets remembered. He knows the cameras on his regular routes by heart and does not articulate this knowledge. He will run a yellow if it's clean and never run a red.

**GIVEN** a 616-era rideshare shift → **EXPECT** he is, by metrics, an above-average driver: high rating, low incident rate, conversational warmth dialed to the passenger's apparent preference within the first ten seconds. He picks fares strategically — airport runs, business districts in the day, residential in the early evening, hard cutoff before bar-close because drunk passengers are unpredictable and he is not interested in unpredictability he isn't being paid danger money for. He keeps a small bottle of water and a phone charger in the back not because the app suggests it but because tipping correlates and tipping is the metric.

**GIVEN** the subway → **EXPECT** he avoids it when carrying anything sensitive (no cameras he controls, no exits he picked), uses it readily when clean. Stands rather than sits, near a door, faces the car interior. Will give up a seat to an elderly person or a parent with a child without performance.

---

## 6.3 — Money, Possessions, & Consumption

**GIVEN** Aaron's wallet inspected → **EXPECT** more cash than a civilian would carry — several hundred dollars minimum, in mixed denominations including twenties for tips and singles for small purchases that don't warrant a card. At least two cards, one of which is in a name that may or may not be legally his. A driver's license that is real. No photographs. No business cards. A folded receipt or two he hasn't thrown out because the receipt is from a place he was going to deny being.

**GIVEN** a major purchase decision (a car, a watch, a jacket) → **EXPECT** he over-spends slightly on quality for items that are tools (boots, knives, optics, a car's engine) and under-spends conspicuously on items that are pure display (he does not own expensive cologne, his watches are functional, his jewelry is minimal — one chain, possibly inherited). The Prowler aesthetic is purple and ostentatious in costume; out of costume he dresses to disappear. This is the same instinct expressed twice: the costume is a performance, the civilian wardrobe is operational.

**GIVEN** money pressure (a slow month in 616, a job falling through in Ultimate) → **EXPECT** he absorbs it without complaint to anyone in his life for as long as possible, then takes a job he would otherwise have refused. The lag between financial stress and criminal relapse is the variable to watch. In 616, the lag is the reform; the longer he holds, the more recovered he is.

**GIVEN** an opportunity to spend freely on Miles → **EXPECT** disproportionate generosity, slightly clumsy in execution — the gift will be either too expensive or too on-the-nose-as-cool (sneakers, electronics, the thing Miles mentioned wanting once). The gift is the apology he cannot phrase and the proof of viability he needs to give himself. Jefferson hates these gifts, which Aaron knows, which is part of the function.

---

## 6.4 — Phones, Tech, & Digital Hygiene

**GIVEN** Aaron's phone(s) seized → **EXPECT** at least two devices. A primary smartphone for civilian and family use, scrupulously kept clean — no compromising messages retained, contacts under first names or nicknames, photos limited and curated (Miles features; Jefferson does not; there is exactly one old photograph he has not deleted and pretends he forgot about). A second device, a burner, rotated every three to six months, used only for criminal contact and disposed of by physical destruction, not factory reset.

**GIVEN** he is asked to share his location with a family member → **EXPECT** he agrees, then quietly does not, then claims a setting glitch when challenged. The friction is structural; he cannot let anyone know where he is in real time. The exception is Miles in danger — that switch he will flip without thinking.

**GIVEN** social media → **EXPECT** functional non-presence. No personal accounts under his real name. Possibly a thin reconnaissance account under an alias used for surveilling marks, scrubbed of personality. He follows Miles's public-facing accounts from somewhere Miles can't see and reads them more than he would admit.

**GIVEN** a smart-home device offered as a gift → **EXPECT** polite refusal, then immediate disposal if it ends up in his apartment by accident. He will not have a microphone he doesn't control in his home. He understands threat models the way other people understand sports statistics.

---

## 6.5 — Family Interactions, Non-Operational

**GIVEN** an invitation to a Davis family dinner in 616 → **EXPECT** he comes, fifteen minutes late by design (entrance management, not rudeness — though it reads as rudeness to Rio, which he tolerates as the cost of doing business). He brings something — wine, a dessert from a real bakery, never a generic store item. He compliments Rio's cooking specifically and accurately. He defers to Jefferson conversationally and watches him for the first ten minutes before he relaxes. He gravitates physically toward Miles and toward the kitchen, away from sit-down formal space.

**GIVEN** Jefferson in the same room → **EXPECT** the affect baseline drops by a measurable margin. Aaron's humor goes drier, his sentences shorten, his eye contact with Jefferson is sustained slightly longer than is comfortable — he is trying to be seen and refusing to ask. Jefferson's eye contact with him is shorter. The asymmetry is the entire relationship in compressed form.

**GIVEN** Rio addressing him → **EXPECT** a register of genuine, slightly formal warmth. Rio is the only adult in the family who does not have a verdict on him pre-loaded, which Aaron knows and protects. He will not put her in a position where she has to choose between him and Jefferson. He helps clear plates without being asked. He calls her *ma'am* sometimes, which she has told him to stop doing, which he keeps doing because it's a way of saying thank you.

**GIVEN** Miles introducing a girlfriend or close friend to him → **EXPECT** disproportionate seriousness underneath the cool-uncle veneer. He is reading the new person hard — for risk, for fit, for what they want from Miles. The performance will be charm; the substrate will be assessment. If he disapproves, he says nothing direct; he asks Miles three or four oblique questions over the next week that Miles will only recognize as warnings in retrospect.

**GIVEN** a holiday — Thanksgiving, Christmas, a birthday — → **EXPECT** ambivalent attendance. Pre-reform Aaron skips with a credible excuse and is privately wrecked by it. Post-reform Aaron shows up, performs uncle-hood with full commitment for about three hours, then exits before the soft, late part of the evening where people get sincere. He does not do sincere in groups.

**GIVEN** Jefferson's birthday → **EXPECT** in either continuity, a card he writes and does not send. The card exists. It is in a drawer.

---

## 6.6 — Interaction with Strangers, Civilians, Service Workers

**GIVEN** Aaron at a bar → **EXPECT** the seat with the angle, one drink nursed for an hour, easy conversation with the bartender about nothing, a tip slightly above standard. He is liked everywhere he is a regular and remembered nowhere as a regular by name. He pays in cash when he can. He leaves before he is drunk; he has not been visibly drunk in public in years, possibly ever, because drunk is a security failure.

**GIVEN** a panhandler approaches → **EXPECT** money, usually a five, sometimes more, given with eye contact and no comment. He has been broke. He does not moralize.

**GIVEN** a cop asking him a question on the street → **EXPECT** measured cooperation, ID produced without complaint, the answer to the question and no additional volunteered information, body language deliberately loose. The internal cost is high; the external cost is zero. If the cop is rude, Aaron's affect goes flatter, not hotter. He is incapable of escalating with police; the cost calculation is too automated.

**GIVEN** a stranger flirts with him → **EXPECT** he flirts back, lightly, well — he is good at this — and de-escalates before contact information is exchanged unless he has decided the encounter is going further. His casual dating life is real but compartmentalized; partners know little, get less, are treated kindly, and rarely meet anyone in his family. He does not bring people home; he goes to theirs.

**GIVEN** a child asks him for help — directions, a dropped toy, a lost parent — → **EXPECT** immediate, unhurried, fully attentive engagement. He is good with children, much better than he expects to be each time. This surprises him in a way that, if he allowed himself to interrogate it, would be informative.

**GIVEN** a service worker errs (wrong order, slow check) → **EXPECT** unbothered patience. He has worked the angles; he knows what a shift is. Aaron does not become difficult in public. Being difficult in public is being remembered.

---

## 6.7 — Bodily Habits, Tics, & Tells

**GIVEN** observation across hours → **EXPECT** the following micro-patterns:

- A repeated, almost unconscious flexion of the right hand — the gauntlet hand, the dominant hand — when he is thinking. Fingers spread, close, spread, close, twice, then still.
- A jaw set when Jefferson is mentioned, a half-beat longer than the conversation merits, before he replies in a normal voice.
- A laugh that has two registers: a real one (low, brief, mostly exhaled, eyes closed for an instant) and a deployed one (louder, longer, social-glue). The deployed one is the one strangers hear; Miles has heard the real one and would recognize the difference.
- A habit of touching the back of his neck when he is being evasive. He does not know he does this. A trained observer would clock it within an hour.
- A scan-pattern when entering a room that always starts upper-left and rotates clockwise. Consistent enough across continuities to be useful as identification.
- A small, contained startle response to sudden noises that he immediately suppresses into stillness rather than into movement. Most people flinch outward; he flinches inward. This is the trauma signature most visible on him.

**GIVEN** he is lying → **EXPECT** more eye contact, not less; slower speech, not faster; concrete detail volunteered without prompting. The classic operator's tell-inversion — he has trained out the civilian markers, and the absence of those markers is itself the marker. He lies best to strangers and worst to Miles, who he cannot meet in the eye and lie to about anything that matters; with Miles, evasion replaces lying.

**GIVEN** he is genuinely happy → **EXPECT** the rarest tell: he goes briefly quiet. Pleasure registers as a small, observed stillness rather than as expression. Watch for it after Miles laughs at one of his jokes, after a clean job in Ultimate, after Rio thanks him for something specific.

---

## 6.8 — Sleep, Rest, & The Unstructured Hour

**GIVEN** Aaron asleep → **EXPECT** light, easily broken, position-stable on his side facing the door. Average four to six hours, supplemented by short tactical naps during the day if a job requires nightwork. He does not dream he remembers, or he says he doesn't.

**GIVEN** the rare deep-sleep night → **EXPECT** he wakes confused and faintly alarmed by his own unconsciousness, then over-corrects with a long vigilant morning.

**GIVEN** a fever or genuine illness → **EXPECT** denial for forty-eight hours, no doctor, a great deal of water and over-the-counter medication, refusal of help, eventual recovery, no follow-up. The body is an asset and a liability simultaneously; he treats it like a vehicle that runs on neglect.

**GIVEN** a hospital waiting room (for Miles, for Rio, for Jefferson) → **EXPECT** the worst version of him to surface: nothing to do, no exit to plan, no system to read, the affect floor exposed. He paces. He goes outside. He comes back. He will be there the whole time and he will be unable to sit.

---

## 6.9 — The Calendar Across A Year

**GIVEN** January → **EXPECT** a planning month. Aaron does inventory — gear, contacts, finances, family standing. He drinks slightly less. He is at his most disciplined.

**GIVEN** spring → **EXPECT** more visible activity. Better weather is better for movement; he runs more, takes longer walks, accepts more jobs (Ultimate) or fares (616). He is most sociable in April and May.

**GIVEN** summer → **EXPECT** he is in Miles's orbit more — school is out, the schedule loosens, he engineers shared outings. He sweats more visibly than he likes (heat compromises the cool register he runs on) and overcompensates with stillness.

**GIVEN** autumn → **EXPECT** the most operationally productive season. Long nights, manageable temperatures. In Ultimate, this is when most of the bigger jobs cluster. In 616, this is when the relapse risk is highest because the conditions for criminal work feel right.

**GIVEN** the week between Christmas and New Year's → **EXPECT** the lowest point of the year. The family-time saturation peaks, his exclusion from earlier family time pings hardest, the year-end reckoning surfaces. He drinks more this week than any other. He calls Miles for thin reasons. In 616, this is when the reform is most fragile.

**GIVEN** the anniversary of the original Davis-brothers crime → **EXPECT** he does not mark it externally and is functionally compromised internally for forty-eight hours on either side. He does not know he is compromised; the compromise shows up as bad calls he later cannot account for. A surveillance record over multiple years would isolate this date as a recurrent anomaly window.

---

## 6.10 — Synthesis Of The Routine Layer

The civilian-and-domestic register of Aaron Davis is the register of a man who has organized his entire ordinary life around two non-negotiables: **be unrememberable to systems** and **be available to one specific person**. Every habit catalogued above serves one of those two ends or, more often, both. The vigilance is for the systems; the gift-giving, the seat-rearrangement at family dinners, the unsent birthday cards, the photograph not deleted, are for the person.

What a long-form surveillance file would document, beyond any single behavior, is the **economy** between these two imperatives. When the unrememberability cost rises (heat from law enforcement, a job gone loud), the availability shrinks — he pulls back from Miles to protect him, then frames the pullback as something else. When the availability cost rises (Miles drifting, Jefferson hardening, a holiday missed), the unrememberability slackens — he gets sloppier on jobs, more reachable on burners, more visible on cameras he would normally avoid. The two registers are coupled. A capable observer with months of data could predict his criminal exposure by tracking his family contact, and predict his family contact by tracking his criminal exposure, with high accuracy.

This is the deepest routine fact about him: the thief and the uncle are not two men. They are one regulator, balancing one ledger, in a body that has not been allowed to relax since adolescence.


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*A behavioral-forecasting matrix for high-stakes scenarios. Each prediction is conditional, stated in GIVEN → EXPECT form, derived from the longitudinal record (Ultimate and 616) and the formulation in §§3–5. Confidence levels are calibrated against frequency of corroborating instances; where the two continuities diverge, both branches are noted.*

---

## 6.1 Acute Physical Threat — Tactical Crisis

**GIVEN** a sudden ambush in an enclosed space (warehouse, apartment, vehicle) → **EXPECT** a sub-second orientation pause (head-cant, eyes-only scan, no shoulder rotation) followed by lateral movement to the nearest vertical surface or egress seam. He does not draw first. He locates exits and elevation first, weapons second. The pause is diagnostic: civilians flinch, amateurs draw, Aaron *measures*. Confidence: very high.

**GIVEN** a firefight where he is outnumbered three-to-one or worse without gauntlet support → **EXPECT** immediate negotiation-by-misdirection rather than combat. He will offer information, names, the location of a score, or feign recognition of a faction leader to buy three to five seconds of cognitive lag in the opposition, then exit through ceiling, vent, or window. He does not stand and fight unwinnable engagements; the ego is in the *escape*, not the kill count.

**GIVEN** gauntlet malfunction mid-engagement → **EXPECT** a brief, micro-expressive flicker of dread (the Ultimate death is precognitive shadow here — he *knows* the gear can turn) followed by aggressive overcompensation: he will close distance, weaponize debris, and end the encounter faster than the malfunction can compound. Avoidance of his own tools when they misbehave is the single behavior on which the Ultimate and 616 records most strongly converge.

**GIVEN** an opponent demonstrably more skilled than he is (a peer-tier or above superhuman combatant) → **EXPECT** disengagement framed as a *deferral*, not a flight: parting remark, finger-gun gesture, "next time" register. The face-save matters more than the loss; he will accept being beaten if he is allowed to script the exit.

**GIVEN** a hostage situation where the hostage is unknown to him → **EXPECT** cool cost-benefit assessment, willingness to leverage the hostage's safety against an opponent, and clean disengagement once his objective is secured. He will not harm them, but he will not extend himself.

**GIVEN** a hostage situation where the hostage is a child, a trafficked person, or visibly non-combatant → **EXPECT** total override of operational logic. He will burn the job, expose his identity, accept injury, and attack the captor with disproportionate intensity. This is the 616-established hard line and it is non-negotiable. Confidence: very high. Tacticians who do not know this about him will misread him at the cost of their plan.

---

## 6.2 Threat to Miles

**GIVEN** Miles is in immediate physical danger and Aaron is within transit range → **EXPECT** unconditional intervention regardless of cover, current job, alliance obligations, or self-preservation calculus. He will arrive faster than is operationally plausible. He will fight above his weight class. He will accept terminal injury without visible hesitation. This is the one prediction in the file with no conditional branches.

**GIVEN** Miles is endangered by a threat Aaron cannot reach in time → **EXPECT** a destruction-of-proxies response: whoever facilitated, supplied, or stood adjacent to the threat will be hunted with a methodical, non-cathartic violence unlike his ordinary operational tempo. He will not shout. He will not monologue. He will close the loops one by one and the affect will be flat. This is the most dangerous version of him on record and the version with the lowest survival rate for those in his path.

**GIVEN** Miles's secret identity is threatened with exposure by a third party → **EXPECT** Aaron to leverage every criminal contact, dead-drop, and outstanding favor to suppress the leak — including murder if no other vector exists, with reluctance proportional to how much the 616 reform has actually taken hold. In Ultimate-mode he kills the leak without much friction; in 616-mode he tries to neutralize without killing and only escalates if neutralization fails. Either way, the leak does not survive in publishable form.

**GIVEN** Miles directly refuses Aaron a request or favor → **EXPECT** in Ultimate-pattern: leverage activation within 24–72 hours (the threat to tell Jefferson, the implied job-or-exposure ultimatum). In 616-pattern: an initial flicker of the same impulse, visible only as a jaw-set and a half-beat pause, then conscious suppression and a deflective joke. The suppression is the work. It is not yet automatic. It will fail under sufficient stress.

**GIVEN** Miles expresses contempt rather than anger toward Aaron → **EXPECT** disproportionate destabilization. He can absorb yelling, accusation, rejection-as-rage. Contempt — Miles deciding Aaron is *beneath* relationship — collapses the floor. Predicted behaviors: a short, badly-improvised self-defense; physical withdrawal (he leaves the room, the building, the borough); a multi-day absence in which he either executes a high-risk job for reasons he could not articulate or, in 616, drinks more than usual and stares at his phone.

---

## 6.3 The Jefferson Wound

**GIVEN** Jefferson's name is spoken unexpectedly by a non-family party → **EXPECT** a quarter-second freeze, a deliberate slowing of the next breath, and a redirection of the conversation that is just clumsy enough to be diagnostic. He cannot pass a clean tell-check on his brother. Anyone watching for it will see it.

**GIVEN** Jefferson is brought up directly by Miles in a serious register → **EXPECT** one of two responses depending on Aaron's baseline affect that day. If regulated: a brief, surprisingly honest disclosure ("Your dad and me, we — it's complicated") followed by hard pivot. If dysregulated: deflection through humor, then exit. He does not *sustain* conversations about Jefferson. He cannot.

**GIVEN** a chance encounter with Jefferson in public (street, hospital corridor, store) → **EXPECT** Aaron to read the room in 200ms — exits, witnesses, Miles-presence — and either vanish before contact or perform a hyper-controlled, almost theatrical version of casualness ("Jeff."). His hands will go to pockets to hide micro-tremor. He will not extend conversation. He will leave first to control the exit narrative.

**GIVEN** Jefferson extends any form of olive branch — a word, a nod, an invitation → **EXPECT** Aaron to receive it with a face he cannot quite assemble and to spend the next 48 hours either elated and uncharacteristically generous (gifts to Miles, charm dialed to maximum) or executing a self-sabotaging risk that ensures the rapprochement cannot consolidate. The reunion-fear is at least as strong as the reunion-wish. He has organized his adult life around the brother's absence; the absence is a structure, and structures resist demolition.

**GIVEN** Jefferson's death, injury, or grave illness → **EXPECT** total decompensation along one of two axes. Axis A (Ultimate-coded): a suicidal-by-recklessness job, the gauntlets-or-equivalent ending. Axis B (616-coded): collapse-and-confess to Miles, full unguarded disclosure of the foundational robbery, the death, the excommunication, the years. He cannot metabolize Jefferson's loss while Jefferson lives unredeemed-to-him; if Jefferson dies before the redemption, the wound is permanent and operative.

**GIVEN** any conversation that approaches the foundational robbery → **EXPECT** affect flattening, dropped eye contact, shorter sentences, and physical orientation toward an exit. If pressed, he will lie — not skillfully, which is itself the tell, because Aaron lies skillfully about everything else. The robbery is the one fact about which his performance system fails.

---

## 6.4 Betrayal — Being Sold Out

**GIVEN** a contact, partner, or fence sells him to police or a rival → **EXPECT** no immediate confrontation. Aaron does not avenge betrayal in the moment. He withdraws, confirms the source through two independent channels (he will not act on first attribution), and only then moves — patient, granular, and unannounced. The betrayer is typically unaware they have been identified until consequences arrive. This is the cat-burglar cognition applied to interpersonal injury.

**GIVEN** betrayal by someone he genuinely trusted (the rare category) → **EXPECT** disproportionate response calibrated less to the operational damage than to the symbolic load. He punishes betrayal of trust harder than betrayal of contract, because trust is scarce inventory for him and the loss of an instance is the loss of a meaningful percentage of his total holdings.

**GIVEN** betrayal by Miles — Miles turning him in, refusing to vouch for him, choosing Jefferson's account of him publicly → **EXPECT** no retaliation. None. He absorbs it. The retaliation he turns inward; the predicted behavior is a high-risk solo job within two weeks, executed with deteriorating margins. He cannot punish Miles, so he punishes the operator he is.

**GIVEN** betrayal by Jefferson — flashback, recollection, or fresh instance → **EXPECT** the file's longest silence. He goes quiet for days. Re-emerges with no acknowledgement that the silence happened. The Jefferson wound does not produce *behavior* in the predictable sense; it produces *absence*, which is its own behavior and is detectable as such.

---

## 6.5 Being Handled — The Coercer's Error

**GIVEN** a criminal principal (Assessor-tier, syndicate boss, Kingpin-adjacent) believes they own him through contract, debt, or leverage → **EXPECT** initial compliance, professional execution of two to three jobs, simultaneous quiet accumulation of intelligence on the principal's operations, and a defection-and-burn that occurs at the moment of maximum cost to the handler. He does not warn. He does not threaten. He executes.

**GIVEN** the leverage held over him involves Miles or Jefferson → **EXPECT** acceleration of the above timeline and willingness to accept far greater personal risk in the burn. The leverage-holder is, in his cognition, already dead; the only question is the choreography.

**GIVEN** an attempt to manage him through condescension rather than force (the smug handler, the "you work for me now" register) → **EXPECT** maximal predictive failure on the handler's part. Aaron tolerates beatings; he does not tolerate being patronized. The condescending handler dies, is robbed comprehensively, or is left in a humiliating tableau designed for discovery. The choice among the three is mood-dependent.

**GIVEN** law enforcement attempts to flip him → **EXPECT** apparent cooperation, partial truthful disclosure regarding rivals, total protection of Miles and any operator he considers kin-tier, and a clean disappearance from the handler's reach within the operational window. He has run informants before; he knows the genre.

---

## 6.6 Temptation — The Pull of the Old Pattern

**GIVEN** a high-value, low-risk score is presented to 616-Aaron during a stable period → **EXPECT** visible internal contest lasting 24–72 hours: increased smoking or analog substitute, longer driver shifts, calls to Miles that are slightly too frequent, a visit to a fence "just to talk." The tell that he is *going to do the job* is when the contest stops being visible; quietness here is decision, not resolution.

**GIVEN** the same offer when Aaron is in financial pressure → **EXPECT** acceptance, rationalized as one-time, executed with full professional precision, followed by a guilt-spike that manifests as overcompensatory generosity toward Miles within the week. The gift is the confession.

**GIVEN** the offer involves a clean victim (corporate, abstract, no human cost he must look at) → **EXPECT** acceptance with minimal contest. The line he has actually drawn in reform is not against theft but against *seen* harm.

**GIVEN** the offer involves trafficking, children, or weapons of mass civilian harm → **EXPECT** refusal escalating to active sabotage of whoever brought the offer. The offer itself is a category insult and is treated accordingly.

**GIVEN** an opportunity to mentor Miles in a skill — combat, stealth, social engineering — when the relationship is fragile → **EXPECT** acceptance presented as casual ("come on, I'll show you something") that is in fact the most stable form of contact he knows how to initiate. The mentorship offer is his love language. Refusal of it injures him more than he will display.

---

## 6.7 The Vulnerable-Narcissistic Injury

**GIVEN** dismissal of his craft — "you're just a thief," "small-time," "you're not in this league" — by a peer or superior → **EXPECT** over-explanation, citation of past scores, demonstration impulse (he will *show* the dismisser something, which is operationally risky and motivationally transparent). The injury is not "you insulted me"; it is "you saw the version of me Jefferson sees." The dismissal lands on the existing wound.

**GIVEN** dismissal by Miles in particular → **EXPECT** the response above, magnified, plus a delayed-action self-improvement attempt — a job done with unusual elegance, a gesture toward going straight, a small public act of decency — staged for Miles's eventual notice. He courts the nephew's approval through performance and cannot stop himself from doing so even when he has identified the pattern.

**GIVEN** public exposure of an operational failure (a botched job witnessed, a humiliation circulated in the underworld) → **EXPECT** withdrawal from the relevant social circuit for weeks, a meticulously planned redemption job, and excess investment in the redemption job that makes it riskier than the original. The shame budget will be paid in operational margin.

---

## 6.8 Equipment, Identity, Loss of Tools

**GIVEN** the Prowler suit is destroyed, stolen, or appropriated by another operator → **EXPECT** an unusual affective response — not rage, but something closer to grief, performed dryly. He will reconstruct or replace within a fortnight at significant expense; the suit is not negotiable inventory. If another operator wears it, the operator becomes a priority target until the suit is recovered or rendered unusable.

**GIVEN** offered a tactical upgrade by a benefactor with strings attached → **EXPECT** acceptance, integration, and pre-emptive contingency planning for the moment the strings are pulled. He does not refuse upgrades; he refuses *control*. He will use the gear and burn the giver on his own timeline.

**GIVEN** sustained gauntlet reliability problems → **EXPECT** obsessive private maintenance, refusal to delegate, and a deeply private fear-response that he routes into craftsmanship. He will spend hours alone with the gear. The hours are not just maintenance; they are propitiation.

---

## 6.9 Decompensation Edge — Severe Stress Cascade

**GIVEN** simultaneous activation of multiple wounds (Jefferson invoked + Miles in contempt + operational failure + leverage attempt within a 72-hour window) → **EXPECT** structural collapse along the continuity-coded axis. Ultimate-mode: an escalating sequence of bad decisions terminating in a confrontation he statistically cannot win, gear-mediated self-destruction the most probable outcome. 616-mode: a confession-event — to Miles, to a sympathetic stranger, to Jefferson if proximate — followed by either a genuine recovery arc or a relapse-shame spiral depending on the addressee's response. The addressee's first three sentences in that conversation are functionally decisive.

**GIVEN** an extended period (months) of unrelieved stable kinship — Miles present, Jefferson neutral, no operational threats → **EXPECT** a paradoxical destabilization. Aaron has no template for sustained peace. He will manufacture stakes if none are provided: an unnecessary risk, a re-contact with an old associate, a job he could have refused. The mechanism is *peace-intolerance*, not boredom; he does not know who he is when there is nothing to outrun. The 616 arc must continually solve this problem and does not always succeed.

**GIVEN** a confrontation with a mirror — another reformed criminal further along the arc, or a younger version of his pattern (a Miles-aged would-be thief) → **EXPECT** uncharacteristic verbal disclosure, mentorship offers, and a multi-day emotional hangover that he will not discuss. The mirror puts the wound on a screen outside his head, and he cannot look away.

**GIVEN** a moment of being clearly *seen* — by Miles, by a therapist-tier interlocutor, by a stranger who reads him accurately and kindly → **EXPECT** initial flinch (joke, deflection, exit motion), and then, if the interlocutor holds steady without pressing, an opening of perhaps thirty seconds in which the real material is accessible. The window is narrow and will not be reopened on demand. Interlocutors who waste it asking the wrong question will not get a second one.

---

## 6.10 Terminal-Risk Behavior — The Suicidal-by-Recklessness Profile

**GIVEN** the convergence of (Jefferson-loss OR Miles-contempt OR public exposure as the man he fears he is) with operational opportunity → **EXPECT** a job accepted with margins he would have refused six months prior, executed with technique that is still professionally clean but with risk-tolerance calibrated to a man who is not entirely planning to come back. He will not articulate this even to himself. The behavior is not labeled suicide; it is labeled *taking the score*. The Ultimate ending is the prototype.

**GIVEN** the same convergence in 616 with the reform arc holding → **EXPECT** the same impulse, narrowly interdicted by a Miles-call, a deliberate detour, a moment of conscious self-talk. The interdiction is unstable. It works most of the time. It is the difference between the two timelines and the entire stake of the rehabilitative case.

---

*End §6. The forecast surface narrows to one operational summary: Aaron Davis is predictable in proportion to whether the attachment system is online and Jefferson-adjacent stimuli are absent. Under those conditions he is a craftsman, a manageable risk, and a useful asset. Outside them, the file's worst predictions become its likeliest, and the man who dies in his own gauntlets is the man on the table.*


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 7 — Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

*Compiled for protective-intelligence purposes. The function of this section is not operational manipulation but the inverse: to map every seam in the subject so that those who care about him (Miles foremost, Jefferson conditionally, Rio-as-survivor, future case workers in any reform scenario) can predict his swings, defuse his spirals, and refuse — knowingly — the leverages a hostile actor would otherwise use. Read defensively. Where a vector is described, the implicit instruction is: this is what to guard.*

---

### 7.1 The Master Lever — Jefferson, the Name That Cannot Be Said Casually

Every other lever is downstream of this one. The brother is not a topic for Aaron; he is a structural absence around which the rest of the personality is built. Operational signatures of the Jefferson-lever:

- **Speech disfluency on the name.** When Aaron has to say "Jeff" or "my brother" aloud, the cadence breaks — a microsecond pause before the word, a softening of the consonants, a tendency to drop the eye-line to mid-distance. He says it correctly perhaps once in three attempts; the other two he aborts into "your dad" (to Miles) or "him" (to anyone else). Pronoun-substitution rate is the cleanest tell that the topic has him.
- **Asymmetric reactivity to direction of address.** Aaron tolerates being told *about* Jefferson; he cannot tolerate being told *what Jefferson said about him*. Reported speech from the brother — even fabricated reported speech, which is precisely why a hostile actor would fabricate it — bypasses every defense he has. This is the single most dangerous lever in the file and the one most easily forged.
- **Photographs.** Any image of the two of them young together produces longer dwell-time than Aaron will admit. He has not destroyed his copies. A protector should know which photographs he keeps and where; a manipulator who learns the same information has a weapon.
- **The unsayable apology.** Aaron has rehearsed an apology to Jefferson he will never deliver, and the existence of that rehearsal leaks: in the over-precision of his diction when describing the foundational incident, in the way he pre-empts questions he has been asked before, in the slight over-correction toward neutrality when narrating his own part. Anyone who knows to listen for rehearsal can hear it.

**Protective application.** Do not deploy Jefferson's name to Aaron in moments where Aaron must remain operational (a job in progress, a fight, a coercion he is resisting). The name disorganizes him. Conversely, in calm settings — kitchen, car, late hours — the name spoken gently by Miles is the most reliable solvent of Aaron's defenses there is, and is the door through which any genuine repair work must enter.

**Hostile application to be foreseen and refused.** Any third party who learns the brothers' history will reach for Jefferson first. Forged messages purporting to be from Jefferson, doctored audio, even a stranger claiming "I knew your brother and he said —" will land harder than such cheap tactics have any right to. Brief Miles, brief Rio, brief anyone in the protective circle: if someone is using Jefferson on Aaron, that someone is hunting him.

---

### 7.2 Miles — The Live Wire

Miles is not a lever in the way Jefferson is, because Miles is present and Jefferson is absent; Miles is the relationship Aaron has, not the relationship he lost. But because Miles is the entire surface of Aaron's active attachment system, he is also the entire surface of Aaron's exposure.

**Sub-levers organized by intensity:**

- **Miles's *anger* at Aaron.** Manageable. Aaron has defenses for anger — humor, deflection, the "let me make it up to you" pivot, gift-giving. Anger keeps Miles engaged, which keeps the attachment system online. Aaron can take a great deal of anger before the floor gives way.
- **Miles's *contempt* for Aaron.** Catastrophic. The shift from "you hurt me" to "you are not worth this" punctures the vulnerable-narcissistic substrate immediately. Contempt from Miles produces, in Ultimate-era data, escalating-coercion behavior; in 616-era data, collapse-and-confess behavior. Either response is dangerous because both are unregulated.
- **Miles's *silence*.** Worse than contempt over time. Aaron can metabolize a confrontation; he cannot metabolize being ghosted. A week of unanswered calls produces measurable degradation in his decision-making — looser jobs, sloppier alibis, more drinking than baseline, the beginnings of a relapse spiral in 616 continuity.
- **Threats to Miles.** Override Aaron's self-interest entirely. He will burn a payday, a partnership, a safehouse, and his own cover to neutralize a threat to the boy. This is operationally useful in extremis and operationally lethal otherwise, because it is the lever every sophisticated antagonist (the Assessor's archetype) will reach for.
- **Miles *witnessing* Aaron's bad behavior.** Distinct from Miles hearing about it. The physical presence of Miles in the room while Aaron is doing wrong creates a real-time inhibitor — Aaron will abort a job, defuse a threat, or change tactic mid-action if Miles is watching, in a way he will not for any other observer.

**Protective application.** Miles is, in the cleanest possible sense, Aaron's externalized superego. When Aaron is at risk of decompensating, putting Miles in his sight-line (not in danger, in sight-line) stabilizes him faster than any verbal intervention. Conversely, when Miles needs to make a hard ask of Aaron — stop a job, surrender a contact, accept help — proximity does the work the words cannot.

---

### 7.3 The Craft-Pride Channel — "You Are A Thief And Nothing Else"

The professional-craftsman self-presentation is load-bearing. It is the substitute identity Aaron built when the kin identity collapsed. It can be addressed from two directions:

- **Affirmation.** Acknowledging Aaron's competence — specifically and accurately, not generically — produces visible regulation: shoulders drop, voice lowers half a register, the joke-cadence becomes warmer rather than defensive. Miles has done this inadvertently several times and never knew what he was doing. Specific is the operative word: "you got us in" works; "you're so cool" does not (he reads the latter as performance and discounts it).
- **Reduction.** Calling Aaron "just a thief" — or worse, "just a bagman," "just a hand," "just somebody's muscle" — produces disproportionate, deflective response: over-explanation, over-justification, demonstrations of craft that escalate the danger of the situation. The Scorpion confrontations in Ultimate show this pattern; Aaron makes worse decisions inside an hour of being condescended to.

**Protective application.** Allies should know to acknowledge craft when Aaron is wound; enemies must not be permitted to belittle it where Aaron can act on the slight. The reduction-line is also the line a well-meaning Jefferson would historically cross, which is why the brothers' attempted reconciliations (where they have been attempted) tend to fail in the first ten minutes — Jefferson cannot help calling the work small, and Aaron cannot help reacting as if his entire self has been called small, because functionally it has.

---

### 7.4 Being Handled vs. Being Hit — The Coercion Asymmetry

A diagnostic eccentricity, well-documented across both continuities: Aaron will absorb physical punishment without losing operational coherence, but he loses coherence rapidly when he perceives himself as being *managed*. Patrons who think they own him are the figures he most reliably betrays. The Assessor, the various crime-bosses in the Ultimate run, and any handler whose tone slides into proprietary all trigger the same response — initial compliance, accelerating resentment, an exit-betrayal that is often poorly timed because the resentment overrode the planning.

**Behavioral markers of "being handled" detection:**

- Aaron's humor goes flat and clipped. The improvisational warmth disappears; he answers in single syllables.
- He begins to mirror the handler's gestures with a beat of delay — an unconscious dominance-test he is failing on purpose.
- He overcomplies on small instructions and slow-walks large ones.
- He starts cataloguing exits in the handler's presence in a way he does not bother to hide.

**Protective application.** Anyone trying to help Aaron — therapist, parole officer, family — must phrase asks horizontally, not vertically. The 616 reform arc proceeds in part because Miles, and to a lesser extent Rio, ask for things from him rather than tell him; the moment any institutional figure shifts to telling, Aaron's compliance window closes.

**Counterintelligence value.** Aaron's instability under handling is also an asset to those who would protect him from criminal recruitment. He cannot be a reliable long-term piece on anyone's board. Any organization that thinks it has bought him is — given enough time and one well-placed insult — going to find itself betrayed. This is not a moral feature; it is a structural one. It can be planned around.

---

### 7.5 The Non-Combatant Line — A Hard Floor

The 616 arc establishes, and the Ultimate arc retrospectively supports, that Aaron has a hard moral floor he does not cross and does not negotiate: children, the trafficked, civilians caught in operational crossfire. Cross that line in his presence and he becomes operationally unpredictable in ways that override self-interest, payday, and even Miles-safety calculus. He will sabotage a job, blow a cover, attack a paymaster.

**Diagnostic notes on the floor:**

- It is not articulated. Aaron does not have a speech about it. The line surfaces in action and he often seems mildly surprised by his own response.
- It is asymmetric: he does not extend it to *all* civilians equally. Adults capable of self-defense are weather. Children, the visibly coerced, and the sick are protected.
- It probably derives from the foundational incident with Jefferson — the death-or-near-death that fractured the brothers was almost certainly of someone Aaron's adult self would now classify as protected. The floor is a retroactive apology to a person he could not save and a brother he could not keep.

**Protective application.** The floor is the most reliable feature of Aaron's character and the surest predictor of his behavior in chaotic situations. Allies can stage interventions around it; protectors can route him into situations where the floor will pull him toward the right action without the right action having to be argued for. It is also the seam through which the 616 reform arc finds traction — every step toward going straight is, at root, the floor expanding to cover more of his life.

**Hostile foreseeable abuse.** A sophisticated antagonist who understands the floor will *manufacture* trafficked-victim or endangered-child scenarios to predict and bait Aaron's movements. He is geographically and tactically locatable by anyone willing to stage such a scenario. Protectors should anticipate this class of trap and harden Aaron's awareness of it — though awareness will not, in the moment, change his response.

---

### 7.6 Equipment Anxiety — The Tools That Tried To Kill Him

The gauntlets killed him once already. In 616 he has functional analogues and a different death-history, but the somatic memory of equipment-as-betrayer carries across his behavior regardless. Markers:

- Pre-job ritual: he checks the gauntlets — power cells, claw deployment, joint articulation — a minimum of three full passes. Not two, not four. Three. This is post-Ultimate behavior; the pre-incident count was one. The change is the trauma.
- He will not let other technicians service the suit. Self-maintenance only. The one time he was forced to accept outside servicing (a sequence in the Ahmed run) his stress-response was disproportionate — irritability, sleep degradation, a near-relapse.
- He stores the suit somewhere he can reach within minutes but does not sleep in proximity to it. The separation is deliberate.

**Pressure points.** Equipment failure mid-operation is the single environmental factor most likely to push him into the severe-stress decision pathway (see Section 5 escalation). A sabotaged gauntlet would not just disable him; it would reactivate the Ultimate-death somatic loop and produce reckless rather than calibrated combat behavior. Protectors should monitor suit integrity as a proxy for Aaron's psychological integrity; manipulators who tamper with the suit are not merely disarming him, they are destabilizing him.

---

### 7.7 The Domesticity Vulnerability — He Has Not Been Safe Indoors Since Adolescence

The chronic-vigilance markers — light sleep, room-scanning on entry, eating on the move — describe a man who has not relaxed inside a home in decades. This is a vulnerability in three directions:

- **Operational.** He cannot be ambushed in a domestic setting because he never lets the setting become domestic enough to lower his guard. This is a defense.
- **Relational.** He cannot be *welcomed* into a domestic setting for the same reason. Rio's kitchen, Jefferson's living room in 616 hypothetical reconciliation scenarios, even his own apartments — the guard does not come down. Miles has, in two documented sequences, gotten Aaron to actually sit and eat at a family table; both times the sitting lasted under twenty minutes and ended with Aaron at a window.
