- **Therapeutic.** Any intervention that requires Aaron to be in a held, stable, low-stimulation environment for long stretches will fail on the body before it fails on the mind. He cannot tolerate it.

**Protective application.** Reform work with Aaron has to happen in motion — in the car, on a walk, mid-task. The 616 Uber-driving arc is structurally important not because the job is virtuous but because the cab is a moving room and Aaron can be sat with inside it. Miles has, without theorizing it, learned that hard conversations with his uncle happen in vehicles. They cannot happen on couches.

---

### 7.8 Affect Leak Indices — How To Read Him

For protective monitoring, the following micro-tells indicate Aaron's internal state at granularities he himself does not register:

- **Hand position when seated.** Relaxed Aaron rests hands open on thighs or table. Mildly stressed Aaron tents his fingers. Moderately stressed Aaron pockets one hand and uses the other for gesture. Severely stressed Aaron pockets both — and this is the read-off for "exit imminent or coercion imminent."
- **Joke latency.** Aaron's humor cadence is fast when he is well and slow when he is not. A two- or three-beat delay before a quip that would normally land instantly is the earliest warning of decompensation.
- **Use of Miles's name.** Aaron says "Miles" warm-and-low when grounded, "kid" when affectionate-and-deflective, "nephew" when leveraging or distancing. The pronoun choice is a thermometer. A shift from "Miles" to "nephew" inside a single conversation is the operational equivalent of an alarm bell.
- **Eye-line during disclosure.** Aaron tells the truth looking mid-distance and lies looking at his interlocutor. This is opposite to civilian baseline and worth knowing.
- **Breathing during physical contact.** Hugs from Miles produce, on first contact, a sharp inhale Aaron does not realize he is taking. The inhale is the involuntary registration that this is real. Its presence is a wellness sign; its absence (he has been seen to brace through hugs in dark periods) is a warning.
- **Walking tempo.** Aaron strolls in safety, walks briskly when alert, paces when destabilized. A pacing Aaron has lost regulation; intervene.

---

### 7.9 Persuasion Vectors — What Works, What Does Not

**What works:**

- *Specific witnessing.* Acknowledging a specific thing he did, accurately, without flattery. This regulates him faster than any other verbal intervention.
- *Asks framed as favors between equals.* He responds to "I need you to —" from Miles or Rio in a way he does not respond to "you should —" from anyone.
- *Time and motion.* See 7.7. Walk with him, drive with him, work alongside him. Verbal work nested inside physical task succeeds where direct sit-down work fails.
- *Naming the pattern, not the person.* He will accept "this is what you do when you feel cornered" much more readily than "you are doing this." The slight grammatical distance from his identity-surface is the difference between defense-up and defense-down.
- *Letting him save face.* Aaron will comply with almost anything if the route to compliance does not require him to admit defeat aloud. Provide the route.

**What does not work:**

- Direct moral argument. He has heard every version of it and out-rehearsed the responses.
- Promises of consequence. He has a foreshortened sense of future and discounts threats accordingly.
- Therapeutic vocabulary used at him by non-intimates. He hears it as handling (see 7.4).
- Public confrontation. The vulnerable-narcissistic substrate cannot tolerate witnessed shaming; it converts to coercion or exit within minutes.
- Sentiment without specificity. Generalized "we love you" registers as performance; he discounts it.

---

### 7.10 Provocation Vectors — What Will Set Him Off

Documented for awareness, not deployment:

- The reductive label ("just a thief," "small-time," "errand boy"). See 7.3.
- The implication that he is replaceable to Miles. Specifically, a third party suggesting Miles has "real" father figures and Aaron is decorative. The vulnerable-narcissistic wound + the kin-instability combine here and produce the fastest visible affect-spike of any provocation on record.
- Reported speech, real or fabricated, from Jefferson. See 7.1.
- Any suggestion that he is being indulged by Miles out of pity. He would rather Miles hate him than pity him.
- Equipment tampering, witnessed. See 7.6.
- Being touched without permission by men he does not know. A street-level register of his hypervigilance; he reads it as control and responds with controlled violence faster than the situation usually warrants.
- The non-combatant floor (see 7.5) crossed in his presence.

---

### 7.11 De-Escalation Protocols — Bringing Him Back

Indexed by stress level.

**Mild (tented fingers, slowed jokes):** Acknowledgment of craft (7.3, affirmation register). Shift of physical setting toward motion. Offer of small task that uses his competence. He regulates inside ten minutes.

**Moderate (single hand pocketed, name-shift to "nephew," pacing onset):** Miles in the sight-line, not asking anything, just present. If Miles is unavailable, motion plus task plus the slight grammatical distance of pattern-naming (7.9). Avoid eye-contact-heavy intervention; sit beside, not across. Twenty to forty minutes.

**Severe (both hands pocketed, braced through contact, the floor going out from under affect):** This is the dangerous zone — the Ultimate-final-confrontation zone. He is in the suicidal-by-recklessness or collapse-and-confess pathway. The intervention is physical proximity from Miles, sustained, and no demands. He will either drop into confession (the 616 pattern, which is the rescuable one) or attempt exit-into-action (the Ultimate pattern, which is the lethal one). In the latter case, the only counter-lever is interrupting the action with the non-combatant floor — putting a person he is bound to protect into the operational space and trusting the floor to redirect him. This is a last resort and carries its own ethical weight.

---

### 7.12 The Inverse Reading — What He Cannot Be Leveraged Into

For completeness, a defensive cartography requires noting where Aaron is *not* exploitable:

- He cannot be leveraged into harming Miles. No payment, no threat, no coercion has held against this. The Ultimate arc shows him coercing Miles into work but never into self-harm and never into harm-of-Miles; the line holds even in his worst version.
- He cannot be leveraged through deprivation. He has been broke, homeless, hunted, and beaten; none of these states have moved him on the questions that matter. Material pressure is a weak vector against him.
- He cannot be leveraged through legal threat alone. He has metabolized the possibility of prison; it does not regulate his behavior.
- He cannot be reliably leveraged through sentiment alone (see 7.9). Hollow appeals slide off.
- He cannot be leveraged into harming the protected categories under the non-combatant floor (7.5). He has refused payment, walked away from setups, and burned partners over this. The floor holds.

The shape of what cannot be moved is also the shape of who he is when the rest of the noise is subtracted: a man who will not hurt his nephew, will not hurt a child, will not be owned, and will not pretend the work he can do is small. Everything else in him is negotiable. These four are not.

---

### 7.13 Synthesis — The Leverage Map Read Defensively

Read the compendium as a single instrument and the protective posture becomes clear. Aaron Davis is a man whose attachment system has been narrowed by injury to one nephew and whose criminality is symptomatic rather than constitutional. Every lever in this file routes, eventually, back to the brother he lost and the nephew he is trying not to lose. A protector who keeps Miles in the sight-line, keeps Jefferson out of the conversation except in controlled domestic settings, keeps strangers from belittling the craft, keeps the equipment serviced by his own hand, and keeps motion available in hard moments will keep Aaron Davis stable enough to continue the 616 trajectory rather than the Ultimate one.

A hostile actor who reverses every one of those — isolates him from Miles, weaponizes Jefferson against him, belittles the craft publicly, tampers with the suit, traps him in static enclosed settings, and *handles* him — will produce, predictably, the man who dies in his own gauntlets.

The leverage map is, in other words, the same map twice: once as the route to his preservation, once as the route to his destruction. The choice of which map is being read is the choice of who is reading it. This file, by its mandate, is a preservation document. The destruction-uses are catalogued only so that those who love him will recognize them when they arrive, and refuse them on his behalf in the moments when he is, by the architecture of his own wounds, unable to refuse them himself.


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — Strengths, Assets & Resilience

*The asset ledger. What this man has, what he can do, what has kept him alive, and what — under the right conditions — could keep him good. Compiled with the same granularity the deficits file received; the positive column is not shorter than the negative one, only less often itemized.*

---

### 6.1 Physical & Somatic Assets

**Baseline conditioning.** Aaron carries the body of a man who has trained continuously for two decades without ever joining a gym he had to sign for under his real name. Lean musculature concentrated in the posterior chain, shoulders, and grip — the build of a climber rather than a striker. Resting heart rate observably low; he does not visibly elevate under tactical stress until well past the threshold where most operators would be panting. Recovery is rapid: he is shown taking serious blunt-force impacts in Scorpion confrontations and walking the next scene without limp adjustment.

**Hand-eye and proprioception.** Exceptional. The Prowler kit demands sub-second placement of clawed gauntlets on irregular surfaces at speed; he does this without visible miscalculation across years of panels. His weapon presentation — drawing, switching modalities mid-motion, recovering when one tool fails — reads as deeply trained rather than improvised. He has a thief's hands: long-attention fine motor work (lock-defeat, device interface, sleight) and short-burst gross motor work (gauntlet strikes, vault-and-clear) coexist in the same nervous system.

**Pain tolerance and injury management.** He metabolizes pain as information rather than alarm. Where a civilian would freeze, he continues to plan. He self-triages — pressure, immobilization, exit — without medical access, indicating either learned trade-craft from a no-hospital career or a personality-floor stoicism that predates the work.

**Sensorium.** Sustained hypervigilance has, as a byproduct, trained his ambient perception to a level most legitimate professionals never achieve. Room-scans on entry are automatic; he registers exit count, sightlines, weapon presence, and demeanor cluster within the first three seconds of any space. His peripheral attention budget is enormous. This is a cortisol cost in the long run but a tactical asset in the moment.

**Sleep architecture.** Light, fragmentable, restorative on demand. He can take twenty minutes in a car seat and recover function. This is the metabolism of someone who has not slept long-form safely in years; it is also a deployable capability that allows him to operate on schedules that would degrade most opponents.

---

### 6.2 Tradecraft & Cognitive Assets

**Craft pride as discipline.** The most underrated asset in his file. Aaron's self-concept as a *clean* professional — the operator who does not leave bodies he did not need to leave, who does not break what he does not need to break, who walks out the way he walked in — is a self-imposed code that functions as a brake on the worst version of him. A criminal without craft pride is a vector for unconstrained damage. Aaron's craft pride continually narrows the blast radius of his decisions. It is not ethics, but it does ethics' work in many situations.

**Planning depth.** He thinks in layers: primary plan, contingency, fallback, abort. He plans backward from extraction, not forward from entry — the signature of a mature operator. He pre-stages exits. He pre-positions resources. He runs jobs that have already been mentally rehearsed enough times that under live conditions he is executing a recording, which is why his affect stays low during the work.

**Pattern recognition on humans.** He reads people the way he reads buildings — for seams, alarms, asleep zones, and pressure plates. Within minutes of meeting someone he has a working model of what they want, what they fear, and which of those is more operative. This is the cognitive substrate of his charm and also of his coercion; weaponized one way it manipulates, weaponized another way it makes him an unusually perceptive mentor to a young person trying to figure out who in a room is dangerous and who is bluffing.

**Improvisational floor.** When a plan collapses, his floor is high. He does not freeze, does not flood, does not escalate into rage; he downshifts into present-tense problem-solving. He has been shown losing equipment, losing position, losing partners, and continuing to function. The improvisational range is wider than his prepared-plan range, which is itself wide.

**Multi-domain literacy.** He is conversant with high-end security systems, Oscorp-grade biotech security at least at the perimeter (he successfully extracted the spider), street-level fence networks, vehicular work, and — by the 616 arc — gig-economy logistics and basic legitimate-sector navigation. He is not a specialist; he is a generalist with no shallow spots that matter.

**Verbal facility.** Quick, dry, register-flexible. He code-switches between street, professional-criminal, family-warm, and customer-service-flat (616, the driving) without seams. This is a survival skill from a life requiring different faces in different rooms; it is also an asset in any negotiation, interrogation, or de-escalation scenario.

---

### 6.3 Equipment & Material Assets

**The Prowler kit itself.** Even with the documented hazard of the malfunctioning gauntlets that killed the Ultimate iteration, the suit represents a substantial standing material asset: climbing capability approaching low-tier superhuman, edged and projectile gauntlet weaponry, optical enhancement, signature recognition (the reputational weight of *the Prowler* as a name in the underworld is itself an asset that opens doors and closes negotiations).

**Distributed caches.** Inferable from operational pattern: a man who plans extractions pre-positions resources. Aaron almost certainly maintains multiple low-profile equipment, cash, and identity caches across the city, none individually critical, redundancy built in. He has been shown moving between locations without a logistical bottleneck.

**Network of fences, drivers, and information brokers.** Two decades of clean professional work in New York generates a Rolodex. He has people who will move goods without asking, people who will drive without asking, people who will not have seen him. The network is loose-tie rather than gang-tight, which is itself a security feature: no one holds enough on him to flip him.

**Reputational capital in the underworld.** *Aaron Davis* is a name with weight. He is known to be competent, known to be selective, known to have killed when forced and known not to have killed when not forced — a profile that buys him latitude in negotiations with figures who would steamroll lesser operators.

**Legitimate-sector toehold (616).** The app-driver work is a small thing financially and an enormous thing structurally. It is a verifiable income, a verifiable schedule, a verifiable face-to-the-state. It is the seed crystal of a legal life and he has shown he can hold it.

---

### 6.4 Relational & Social Assets

**The Miles relationship.** The single most valuable item in the entire ledger, and the one that makes every other entry safer to deploy. Miles is not just a person Aaron loves; Miles is the **regulator** that keeps the rest of Aaron's system from going into runaway. The attachment is asymmetric in intensity (Aaron needs it more) and asymmetric in disclosure (Miles knows less of Aaron than Aaron knows of Miles), but it is real on both sides, and across the 616 arc it has demonstrated the capacity to absorb betrayal and reconstitute. A relationship that survives what theirs has survived is a load-bearing asset.

**Capacity to mentor.** Distinct from the Miles bond as such: Aaron has the structural ability to teach a young person tactical competence, social reading, and self-possession in dangerous environments. Even in the coercive Ultimate frame, the tradecraft and confidence he transmits to Miles is real and useful and stays with the boy. Under benevolent direction, this is an unusually high-value pedagogical asset for any young operator in his orbit.

**Charm as social asset.** He can be the most engaging person in a room when he wants to be. He builds rapport with strangers quickly, holds it lightly, and exits cleanly. This is a transactional skill in criminal contexts and a community-building skill in legitimate ones, and the underlying capacity is the same.

**Selective loyalty.** What loyalty he gives, he gives without hedging. The list of people he will spend himself for is short, but membership on it is non-revocable on his side — Jefferson never falls off the list despite a quarter-century of mutual silence. This is a rare and bankable quality; it means anyone Aaron has committed to is committed to in full.

**Capacity for non-combatant discrimination.** The hard line around children and the trafficked, established and held in 616, is not performance — it overrides his self-interest. This is a moral asset, narrow but absolute, and the kind that does not erode under pressure.

---

### 6.5 Psychological & Characterological Resilience

**Refusal of self-pity.** Aaron does not, in any continuity, narrate his life as a victim story. He owns his choices, including the catastrophic ones. This refusal is partly defense (it spares him the collapse self-pity would invite) and partly genuine character, and it is the precondition for any rehabilitation he undertakes. A man who blames the world cannot reform; a man who blames himself can.

**Functional shame.** He carries enormous shame and it does not incapacitate him. In the 616 arc the shame becomes generative — it powers the reform — rather than purely corrosive. The capacity to feel shame *and continue functioning* is a specific developmental achievement; many of the genuinely dangerous men in his trade have lost it.

**Remorse capacity.** Demonstrated. He can recognize that he has wronged Miles, articulate it, and act differently. This is the single feature that disqualifies the psychopathy reading and the single feature that makes him a candidate for handling as an asset rather than a target.

**Action-based affect regulation.** A double-edged trait, but on the asset side: he does not flood, does not dissociate, does not freeze under stress. He can be deployed in conditions that would non-functionalize most subjects.

**Stoic floor under physical threat.** He absorbs intimidation poorly directed at his ego and absorbs physical threat with composure. Coercers who attempt to break him through pain alone fail; this is why he survives the underworld.

**Identity stability.** Unlike borderline-organized personalities, Aaron's sense of who he is does not oscillate. He may dislike who he is, but he knows. This stability is what makes deliberate change possible for him — he has a self to change, not a self to assemble.

**Humor under pressure.** Not nervous humor; tactical humor. He uses it to lower the temperature of rooms, to reframe his own panic to himself, to maintain the persona that maintains him. It is a regulator, a social lubricant, and a small daily mercy he extends to himself.

---

### 6.6 Rehabilitative & Trajectory Assets

**Demonstrated reform capacity (616).** The 616 arc is, in asset terms, an existence proof: under the right conditions — a brother no longer present to reject him, a nephew willing to hold the door open, an external structure (the driving work) that organizes his days — Aaron can hold a non-criminal life for sustained periods. Relapse occurs under leverage, not under boredom. This is the rehabilitative profile that responds to *protection from coercion* more than to *internal transformation*; both are needed, but the former is the unlock.

**Insight, accruing.** Across the 616 run he becomes increasingly able to see his own patterns in real time — the automatic scan-for-leverage on Miles, the deflection into humor when feeling exposed, the urge to tighten the relationship through control when it feels loose. Insight without action is inert; Aaron has shown action following insight, which is the rarer combination.

**Moral asymmetry of his pressure points.** The things that destabilize him most reliably are not greed, not ego in the deep sense, and not appetite — they are kin-rejection and accusations of being merely a thief. These are pressure points that *point toward* the better version of him rather than away from it. A man whose worst destabilizers are shame-based rather than appetite-based is a man whose collapse trajectory bends toward repair rather than toward depravity.

**Late-life thematic arc.** The dominant note of his mid- and late-career record is a man fighting his own pattern, not feeding it. This is the trajectory of someone whose story can plausibly end somewhere other than where it began. The Ultimate ending is one such ending; the 616 arc is the proof that it is not the only one.

---

### 6.7 What Makes These Assets Durable

The asset profile holds up under stress because it is **mutually reinforcing**, not stacked. The craft pride protects the mentorship capacity. The mentorship capacity protects the Miles bond. The Miles bond protects the reform trajectory. The reform trajectory protects the legitimate-sector toehold. The legitimate-sector toehold reduces the financial pressure that historically reactivated the criminal pattern. Each asset, when active, shores up the next.

The asset profile is **fragile in one specific way**: it is all routed through a single relationship. Sever Miles from the system and most of the rehabilitative capacity goes offline, the craft pride untethers from any moral anchor, and what remains is the competent professional with nothing slowing him down. This is the lesson of the Ultimate ending. Conversely, **preserve and protect that single relationship** and the entire asset stack stays online, and Aaron Davis becomes — in the right hands — one of the more valuable redeemable subjects in this file series: a man with elite tradecraft, real loyalty, demonstrated moral lines, and a working conscience.

The instruction this section yields is simple. The assets are real, they are deep, and they are durable *as long as the attachment system is online.* Manage to that variable and almost everything else in this dossier moves in the direction of the man he is trying, against his own history, to become.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — Failure Modes & Decompensation

*How the subject breaks. The architecture of his collapses, the order in which his defenses give way, the somatic and behavioral tells at each stage, and the environmental conditions that reliably produce each failure mode. Substantiated against the Ultimate arc terminal sequence, the late-Ultimate Scorpion confrontations, the 616 Assessor entanglement, the recurrent Jefferson-adjacent affect leaks, and the consistent micro-pattern of leverage-tightening under attachment threat.*

---

### 6.1 The Stable Baseline — and Why It Is Already Half a Failure

Before tracing the breaks, the baseline must be named, because Aaron's "well" state is itself a chronic compensated failure of the developmental project. Baseline Aaron is **functional, charming, operationally fluent, and structurally lonely**. He sleeps in short cycles in spaces he has personally swept. He eats standing or in motion. He keeps his apartments thin — the recurring visual of his living spaces across both continuities is sparse furniture, no photographs, no books on display, the kitchen of a man who does not cook for company. He has no on-panel romantic partner of any duration; the closest analogues are short, transactional, and never named in the family record. His phone contacts are short; his ties are operational or kin.

This is not contentment. It is **a successfully managed dissociation between the part of him that needs people and the part of him that has been taught people end in excommunication**. The compensation works. It works so well that the man does not know he is in failure until something forces the channels back open. Miles is what forces them open. Every collapse documented below begins, structurally, the moment Aaron lets the attachment system back online — because the attachment system has nowhere safe to terminate.

---

### 6.2 The Escalation Path — Stage Model

Aaron's decompensation runs a reliable five-stage course. The stages are not equal in duration; stages 1–2 can hold for weeks, stages 3–4 compress to hours, stage 5 to minutes. The transitions are observable.

#### Stage 1 — Hypercontrol of Tempo
**Trigger conditions:** a job presenting variables outside rehearsal; a Miles encounter going off-script (the nephew asking a question Aaron hadn't planned an answer for); the appearance of a handler-figure (Scorpion in the early Ultimate sequence; the Assessor in 616) attempting to set the pace of Aaron's operation.

**Behavioral signature:** Aaron becomes **more verbal, not less**. He narrates the plan aloud, repeats steps, walks back through contingencies he has already covered. He arrives early to meetings — not by minutes but by hours, sometimes pre-clearing the site. He cleans gear that does not need cleaning; the gauntlets in particular get inspected as a ritual, the same sequence each time (left palm, right palm, claws extended and retracted in counted sequence, optics wiped on the inner forearm of the suit). He smokes more in the Ultimate-era depiction; in 616 the equivalent is gum, mints, the oral fixation displaced.

**What this is:** the craft-as-regulator defense doing its proper job. Action absorbs anxiety. As long as he can keep moving and keep planning, the structure holds.

**Cost:** crew and family find him exhausting at this stage. He talks past them. He does not hear push-back well. This is the stage at which he will most reliably make decisions his future self will hate, because he is treating disagreement as a tempo-disruption to be routed around rather than as information.

#### Stage 2 — Leverage-Tightening
**Trigger conditions:** stage 1 fails to discharge the anxiety; or the anxiety is specifically relational rather than operational; or Miles signals withdrawal (cancels a meet, takes a call in the other room, repeats Jefferson's phrasing).

**Behavioral signature:** Aaron reaches for **contractual hardening of relationships that were not contractual**. In the Ultimate arc this is the explicit move — *do this job with me or I tell your father*. In 616, where he is trying not to do this anymore, the same impulse appears in softened forms: the unsolicited large gift, the favor extended with the receipt visible, the reminder of past help dropped into casual conversation. Both versions are the same mechanism: **convert the warm tie into a debt structure that cannot be casually exited**.

**Tells:** the humor flattens. The grin that has been his most reliable instrument across both continuities becomes more frequent and less warm — it now appears on phrasing where it does not belong, as a closer rather than as an opener. He touches people more (a hand on Miles's shoulder, a clap on the back) and the touches last a half-beat longer than they should. Eye contact lengthens to the point of pressure.

**What this is:** **coercion-as-affection**, the Section 3 diagnosis manifesting as behavior. Aaron experiences attachment uncertainty as imminent loss and tries to bolt the door from the inside. He cannot tell the difference between binding someone to him and being safe with someone, because he has never had the second without the first.

**Cost:** this is the stage at which Miles begins to pull away in earnest. The leverage move is precisely the move that produces the loss it is trying to prevent. In the Ultimate continuity Aaron cannot see this. In 616 he can, sometimes, after the fact — and the seeing produces the next stage's particular flavor.

#### Stage 3 — Operational Recklessness
**Trigger conditions:** leverage has failed or visibly backfired; the handler-figure has tightened pressure beyond Aaron's tolerance; Miles has named what Aaron is doing.

**Behavioral signature:** the planning quality degrades sharply. Jobs Aaron would have walked away from a week earlier get taken. Margins shrink — he accepts shorter recon windows, thinner exits, partners he has not personally vetted. The gauntlets get used in situations where the suit alone would have sufficed; he leans on the gear because the man is no longer trusting the man. **Speed up, footprint up, noise up.** This is the stage at which his criminal record, if it were being kept by a non-superhuman law enforcement entity, would acquire its sloppy entries.

**Somatic markers:** he stops sleeping the short cycles and starts not sleeping at all. The eating-on-the-move pattern degrades to skipped meals; coffee intake spikes. The room-scan on entry, which is automatic at baseline, becomes performative and incomplete — he goes through the motions but the data is not landing. He has begun to **dissociate from his own competence**, which is the most dangerous thing that can happen to a man whose competence is his floor.

**What this is:** the affect-regulation strategy failing. Action no longer downregulates because the action itself is now anxiety-producing. The thrill that used to be the regulator is now the noise. He keeps doing the thing because he has no other thing.

#### Stage 4 — Shame-Floor Drop
**Trigger conditions:** something he cannot route around. Categorically: (a) Miles articulates contempt — not anger, contempt, the Jefferson-tone; (b) the Jefferson name surfaces in a context where Aaron cannot deflect; (c) Aaron sees himself doing the thing he promised himself he would not do, with enough clarity that the promise's failure is undeniable; (d) the handler-figure's contempt — a coercer making it visible that Aaron is owned — combines with (a) or (b).

**Behavioral signature:** the grandiose surface fails. The face that has carried him across two continuities of professional crime **goes still**. The voice drops in register and loses its musicality. He stops performing competence and starts simply enduring the conversation. In the Ultimate arc this is the stage where, late in the run, the cocky-uncle affect is no longer recoverable on demand and Miles can see something else underneath. In 616 the equivalent is the confessional posture in the Assessor sequence and its aftermath — head down, hands loose, the body of a man who has stopped trying to look like anything in particular.

**Affect-leak tells:** the eyes go wet without tears. A long exhale that he doesn't manage. The micro-gesture of running a palm down the face from forehead to jaw, which appears across both continuities at moments of self-witnessing. He says less than he has said in days.

**What this is:** the **vulnerable-narcissistic substrate exposed**. The shame that has been load-bearing under the grandiose surface is now the surface. He does not become depressed in any clinically useful sense — too brief, too situational — but he becomes legibly the man Jefferson said he was, and he knows it, and he knows the witness knows it.

**This is the inflection stage.** What happens at stage 4 determines whether the collapse terminates in repair (the 616 trajectory) or in self-destruction (the Ultimate trajectory). The variable is not internal. The variable is **whether the attachment object stays in the room**. If Miles stays, Aaron eventually speaks and the collapse converts to a repair attempt. If Miles leaves — or, in Ultimate, was never going to stay — stage 5 begins.

#### Stage 5 — Suicidal-by-Recklessness Terminal Sequence
**Trigger conditions:** stage 4 with the attachment object absent or repudiating; equipment in hand; an opponent or scenario in front of him.

**Behavioral signature:** Aaron does not become overtly suicidal. He does not announce, he does not plan. He **stops applying the survival heuristics that have kept him alive for a career**. He takes the shot he should not take, stays in the room he should leave, escalates the gear past safety margins, ignores the warning indicators (the malfunctioning gauntlets in the Ultimate terminal sequence are the literal instance — he keeps using them after he has felt them fault).

The technical term is **passive suicidality via operational disinhibition**. The man does not want to die in any sentence he could speak. He simply ceases to defend the life he has, because the life he has just became untenable in his own eyes and the part of him that would have argued for it has been muted by shame.

**Outcome in Ultimate:** death by his own equipment, which is the most diagnostically perfect ending the character could have been given. The tools of his survival become the agent of his erasure, in the same gesture by which he tried one last time to be too much.

**Outcome in 616 (averted at stage 4):** he is pulled back. The arc demonstrates that stage 5 is **not constitutional**. With the attachment object retained, the collapse terminates at confession rather than at obliteration.

---

### 6.3 The Conditions That Reliably Produce Each Failure Mode

The stages above are the path; the following are the specific environmental and relational configurations that ignite the path and determine its depth.

**Condition A — The Handler.** Any figure who attempts to own Aaron rather than hire him. Scorpion's early treatment of him in Ultimate. The Assessor's coercion in 616. The shared signature is **a coercer who behaves as if Aaron is property**. This produces the fastest escalation Aaron exhibits, because it activates two systems at once: the vulnerable-narcissistic injury (being treated as a thing) and the kin-excommunication template (being told what he is by someone with power over him, the Jefferson-shape). Handlers reliably escalate Aaron from stage 1 directly to stage 3, skipping the leverage-tightening of stage 2 because the leverage is being applied *to* him rather than *by* him.

**Condition B — The Jefferson Echo.** Any context in which the brother is invoked, present, or audible through Miles. Aaron's affect-floor is unstable in any Jefferson-adjacent scene; if the invocation is hostile, he goes to stage 4 with very little intervening pattern. This is the only stimulus class for which Aaron has no working defense. The Section 3 splitting around Miles is partly a function of this: he has had to construct Miles as a separate object from Jefferson, and any collapse of that separation collapses Aaron.

**Condition C — The Witness-of-Self.** Aaron is most vulnerable not to external accusation but to internal recognition. The moments he breaks hardest are not the ones where someone tells him what he is — he has rebuttals prepared — but the ones where he **catches himself** mid-pattern. The 616 reform arc weaponizes this against itself: as Aaron becomes more able to see his own patterns, he becomes more vulnerable to stage-4 collapses, but those collapses now route toward repair instead of toward death.

**Condition D — Equipment Failure.** Materially literal and psychologically symbolic. When the suit faults, Aaron faults. The gauntlets carry a disproportionate weight in his self-concept because they are the visible signature of the Prowler identity, and identity-grade equipment failing during a stress-3 or stress-4 state produces the cascade most likely to terminate in stage 5. Investigators should note: **the Ultimate terminal sequence is not bad luck. It is the convergence of all four conditions simultaneously** — handler pressure (the larger criminal context), Jefferson echo (the relationship with Miles having reached the rupture point), witness-of-self (Aaron has just been confronted by the nephew with what he has been doing), and equipment failure (the gauntlets). Any one of these would have produced a stage-3 incident. Together they produce death.

**Condition E — The Non-Combatant Threshold.** A specific and counterintuitive failure mode. Aaron's hard line on children and the trafficked, established in 616, makes him **operationally unpredictable in scenarios that cross it** — but the unpredictability is not collapse, it is **inversion**. He abandons jobs, betrays employers, exposes himself to retaliation, and accepts losses that the professional baseline would never accept. This is failure of the criminal frame, not failure of the man; it is the one register in which the breakdown of his operational code is a moral upgrade. Investigators should expect him to behave most "out of character" precisely in scenes where a child is at risk, and should not read the deviation as instability — it is the one stable thing.

---

### 6.4 Decompensation Tells — The Granular Index

For surveillance purposes, the following micro-signals reliably index Aaron's stage at any given observation point. They are ordered from earliest-appearing to latest.

- **Gum/mints (616) or cigarettes (Ultimate) — frequency above baseline.** Stage 1.
- **Gauntlet inspection ritual performed outside operational context.** Stage 1, leaning into stage 2.
- **Use of the phrase "I'm just saying" or its variants, repeatedly, in conversation with Miles.** This is his verbal tell for leverage-being-prepared. Stage 2.
- **Unsolicited gift of disproportionate value.** Stage 2.
- **The half-beat-too-long touch.** Stage 2.
- **Acceptance of a job he would have declined the week before.** Stage 3.
- **Skipped meals; visible weight shift across a multi-week observation.** Stage 3.
- **Performative but incomplete room-scan on entry.** Stage 3 — this is the single most reliable index that his competence has gone offline; the body executes the motion but the eyes are not parsing.
- **Use of the suit's offensive capabilities in a scenario the suit's stealth capabilities could have resolved.** Stage 3.
- **Voice drop in register; cessation of the musical cadence.** Stage 4.
- **Palm-down-the-face gesture.** Stage 4.
- **The grin not appearing at a moment where the grin reliably appears.** Stage 4 — its *absence* is the marker, not its presence.
- **Continued use of equipment after a fault has been felt.** Stage 5. Intervention window is very short.
- **Walking toward, not away from, an opponent whose threat profile exceeds his capability.** Stage 5. Intervention window has effectively closed.

---

### 6.5 What His Collapse Looks Like to Others

To Miles: a slow series of small wrongnesses that resolve into the recognition that the uncle he loves is doing something he cannot keep ignoring. Aaron does not break dramatically in front of the nephew until the very end of each cycle; the collapse is mostly inferable from the leverage-pattern, and Miles's own moral development across both continuities is partly a function of having had to learn to read his uncle's stages in real time.

To Jefferson (in the rare scenes where they share a frame): a man Jefferson recognizes immediately. The brother has seen this sequence before, in their shared youth, and his refusal to be in the room with it is the refusal of someone who knows he cannot interrupt it without becoming part of it. Jefferson's distance is not callousness; it is **the survivor's recognition that intervention is not within his power**, which is its own kind of grief.

To a handler: an asset getting more compliant in stages 1–2, then less reliable in stage 3, then unrecoverable in stages 4–5. Coercers who have used Aaron tend to mis-time their pressure because they read stage 2 as control and do not see the inversion coming. The Assessor's miscalculation in 616 is paradigmatic: pressure that would have produced compliance in stage 1 produces betrayal in stage 4.

To himself: largely opaque until stage 4. Aaron has no working introspective access to stages 1–3; he experiences them as situations the world is doing to him. Stage 4 is the first stage at which he can see himself, and the seeing is unbearable enough that stage 5 is the body's solution to the mind's witness — unless, as in 616, someone stays in the room and gives the witness somewhere to terminate other than death.

---

### 6.6 The Diagnostic Summary

Aaron Davis fails along a single axis: **the attachment system, when activated, has nowhere safe to land, and the failure to land cascades through his operational competence until the competence kills him or someone reaches him in time**. He does not fail at being a thief. He fails at being a brother and a nephew's keeper, and the thief-collapse is the symptom.

The intervention principle, for any party who would prefer him alive and useful, follows directly: **do not address the criminality; address the witness**. Keep the attachment object in the room. Let the stage-4 collapse run to confession. Do not let stage 5 begin. The Ultimate continuity is the case where no one was positioned to do this. The 616 continuity is the case where someone was. The difference between the two outcomes is not the man. The man is the same. The difference is whether anyone stayed.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU ANALYTICAL FILE: AARON DAVIS / THE PROWLER
## Section 6 — Trajectory & Forward Assessment

*Prognostic synthesis. Built from the longitudinal behavioral record across both continuities, treated as parallel outcome trials of the same underlying personality structure. The Ultimate timeline is the unmitigated trajectory; the 616 timeline is the mitigated one. Reading them as a paired natural experiment is the most informative analytic move available, because they isolate the variable that matters: whether the attachment to Miles remains an open channel.*

---

### 6.1 The Governing Question

Every forward projection of Aaron Davis reduces to a single binary, and the file should be honest that this is so: **is the attachment to Miles online or severed?** Almost nothing else about him is genuinely predictive in isolation. His criminal opportunism is constant. His craft pride is constant. His charm and his shame are constant. The variable that swings the entire outcome distribution is whether, at any given moment in his life, the boy is taking his calls.

This is not a sentimental finding; it is a structural one. Aaron's affect regulation is action-based and his attachment budget is concentrated on a single object. Strip the object and there is no regulator. Maintain the object and there is a tether strong enough to do work no therapist, no parole officer, no carceral apparatus, and no peer relationship has been able to do.

The Ultimate timeline shows what the severed-channel trajectory looks like in full: escalation, coercion, equipment-mediated self-destruction. The 616 timeline shows what the intact-channel trajectory looks like: relapse, repair, relapse, repair, slow asymptotic approach toward a life that is neither fully reformed nor fully recidivist. Both are stable attractors. Aaron will end his life in one of them.

---

### 6.2 Likely Future Developments — The Base-Rate Trajectory

Assume the 616 conditions hold: Miles is alive, in contact, conditionally trusting; Jefferson is not actively brokering reconciliation but is not actively prosecuting it either; the legitimate work (driving, gig labor) is in place but precarious.

Under these assumptions, the modal forward path over the next decade reads as follows.

**The income problem will resurface every six to eighteen months.** Gig-economy income does not service the lifestyle Aaron is accustomed to, and more importantly, it does not service the **gift-giving** through which he metabolizes love. He cannot be the uncle who shows up with the thing Jefferson can't afford if he is grossing what Jefferson grosses. The financial pressure on the reform is therefore not material — he can in fact live on the driving — it is **expressive**. Every birthday, every Christmas, every milestone in Miles's life that Aaron wants to mark with something tangible is a recurring stressor on the legitimate-income frame. Predict relapse pulses clustering near these dates.

**Old contacts will keep arriving.** A criminal career of his duration leaves a long tail of people who know what he can do and what he owes. The Assessor episode is the template, not the exception. Expect, on a recurring basis, approaches from former clients, former rivals, and ambitious newcomers seeking either his services, his silence, or his demonstrated leverage over a Spider. He cannot opt out of these approaches by being good; he can only opt out by being unreachable, and unreachable conflicts with the uncle frame. The structural impossibility of being both available to Miles and invisible to his past is the central tension of the rehabilitative arc and it does not resolve, it only gets managed.

**He will accumulate a small repertoire of "last jobs."** Aaron is not capable of a single clean exit. The pattern across the 616 record is one of bounded relapses framed internally as exceptions — this one because the target deserves it, this one because the money is needed, this one because someone is leveraging him and the job is the price of de-leveraging. Each of these episodes will be narrated to himself as terminal and to Miles, if at all, as past tense. Over time, the gap between his self-narrative ("retired, with exceptions") and his behavioral record ("active, with intervals") will widen and he will become aware of the widening. Whether that awareness produces collapse, confession, or a harder defense is one of the genuine fork points (see 6.4).

**The mentorship register will deepen and complicate.** As Miles ages out of adolescence, the asymmetric uncle-nephew dynamic becomes harder to sustain in its earlier form. Miles will increasingly read Aaron as a peer-adult rather than a glamorous elder, which means the charm-and-gift apparatus will lose efficacy. Aaron will need to find a register of relationship that is not predicated on Miles being awed by him. He has never had such a register with anyone. Watch for awkwardness, distance, and a temporary period of reduced contact while Aaron retools — and watch for opportunistic reaching during that period (calls when drunk, gifts that overshoot, jobs that he half-hopes Miles will hear about).

**A second attachment object may emerge, and this is the most volatile development to monitor.** Aaron's single-channel attachment economy is a known fragility. If a romantic partner enters the picture seriously — not the surface dalliances visible in the existing record, but someone who reaches him — the system will be forced to redistribute. He has no protocols for this. The new attachment will either stabilize him substantially (a second tether reduces catastrophic load on the first) or destabilize him acutely (jealousy patterns, divided loyalty, the partner reading the Miles-channel as obsessive and demanding renegotiation). The literature on dismissing-avoidant operators forming late-life pair bonds is genuinely mixed and Aaron is exactly the kind of subject for whom outcome is unpredictable in advance.

**Physical decline will arrive earlier than calendar age predicts.** The cumulative trauma load — blunt impacts, the burn-and-electrical injury history, chronic-vigilance cortisol exposure, untreated injuries from the criminal years — will produce orthopedic and cardiovascular consequences by his mid-fifties at outside, late forties at the inside. The Prowler identity is physically expensive; the body will withdraw the line of credit. How he metabolizes the loss of operational capacity is a second-order fork point (6.4). He has never had a self-concept that did not include being the most capable person in the room.

---

### 6.3 Open Questions — Items the File Cannot Yet Resolve

Honesty about prognostic limits is itself diagnostic discipline. The following are unresolved and should be flagged for ongoing observation rather than asserted.

**Whether reconciliation with Jefferson is possible.** The entire 616 reform arc is, in the deep structure, addressed to Jefferson, not to Miles. Miles is the achievable proxy; Jefferson is the actual addressee. But the file has not yet seen a sustained adult conversation between the brothers in which both are willing to occupy the same emotional register. The Ultimate timeline foreclosed the question by killing Aaron before it could be asked. The 616 timeline keeps the question open and unanswered. Aaron's long-term stability is meaningfully higher if reconciliation occurs and meaningfully lower if Jefferson dies first with the channel still closed. The latter scenario would be a catastrophic input and should be modeled as such.

**Whether he can be honest with Miles about an active job.** Every observed disclosure to Miles has been retrospective — about jobs done, not jobs underway. The day Aaron tells Miles in real time that he is being pressured into something and asks for help rather than presenting it as a *fait accompli* is the day the reform becomes structural rather than performative. It is not clear he is capable of this transition. It requires admitting need to the person whose admiration is his primary supply, and his entire defensive architecture is organized against exactly that admission.

**Whether the Prowler suit gets retired, transferred, or destroyed.** The gear is not incidental. The relationship to the suit is the relationship to the operational self. As long as the suit exists and is reachable, the option is live. A genuine retirement requires either destruction or transfer (to a vetted successor, or to law enforcement, or symbolically to Miles in some non-operational capacity). The file should expect Aaron to keep the suit accessible long past the point at which his stated intentions justify it. This is itself prognostic data: the gap between his disposition of the gear and his stated reform measures the actual depth of the reform.

**Whether he ever speaks the foundational wound aloud.** The young-adult robbery, the death (or near-death), the moment Jefferson chose excommunication — none of this has been processed in a setting where processing is the goal. Aaron has discussed it tactically and apologetically; he has not discussed it as the wound it is. A subject who never speaks the structural wound aloud generally does not heal from it; they merely manage around it more or less successfully. Whether Aaron ever has the conversation — with Jefferson, with Miles, with a therapist (improbable but not impossible in the 616 arc given Miles's generation's normalization of such care), or even with a romantic partner — is a major prognostic indicator.

**Whether the trafficking-line conviction holds under sustained pressure.** The 616 record establishes a hard moral line at children and the trafficked. This line has been tested and held in the observed episodes. But it has been tested under conditions where holding the line was operationally compatible with self-interest (the targets of his deviation were already adversarial to him). The line has not yet been tested under conditions where holding it would cost him Miles, cost him his life, or cost him Jefferson's safety. Lines that have not been tested under genuine cost are not yet known to be lines.

---

### 6.4 Fork Points — Discrete Events That Would Reroute the Trajectory

These are the high-leverage inputs. They are the events around which a prognostic file should be most attentive because each one shifts the modal outcome distribution substantially.

**Fork 1 — A Miles-Endangerment Event Aaron Caused.** If a job of Aaron's — direct or indirect, traceable or not — results in serious harm to Miles, the trajectory bifurcates sharply. Path A: Aaron confesses immediately, accepts full consequence, and the relationship survives in damaged form. Path B: Aaron conceals, the concealment is discovered later by Miles independently, and the relationship is destroyed in the worst possible mode — not by the harm but by the lie about the harm. The Ultimate timeline ran a version of Path B and Aaron died. The 616 timeline has not yet faced this fork in maximal form. Which path he chooses depends almost entirely on whether the disclosure window opens within his immediate shame-response (first 24–48 hours), during which his guilt-and-confess reflex is dominant, or after that window, by which time rationalization has had time to consolidate.

**Fork 2 — Jefferson Initiates Repair.** If Jefferson makes the first meaningful overture — and the 616 framing leaves this possible, where the Ultimate framing did not — Aaron's entire defensive structure has to reorganize. He has been the suitor for forty years; being received changes the role. The most likely first response is deflection and self-sabotage, because he does not know how to be the receiver. Past that initial collapse, however, the long-term effect of received fraternal repair would be transformative in a way no other input can match. This is the single most positive possible event in his life trajectory.

**Fork 3 — A Second Attachment Forms.** Addressed in 6.2 but worth restating as a fork. The valence depends almost entirely on whether the new attachment object can tolerate the Miles-channel without contesting it. A partner who joins the Miles-orbit becomes a stabilizer. A partner who competes with it becomes an accelerant.

**Fork 4 — Physical Capacity Loss Before Identity Renegotiation.** If the body fails before he has built a non-operational self, the loss will trigger the kind of severe-stress collapse the file has flagged as his most dangerous state. He does not rage outward in collapse; he turns the violence on the situation, which often means onto himself by proxy. A man whose self-concept is welded to operational capacity and who loses that capacity without warning is at elevated risk of self-destructive recklessness, not in the dramatic suicidal-ideation register but in the quieter "one more job, the body can hold" register that produces the same outcome by other means.

**Fork 5 — A Successor Appears.** If a younger operator emerges who wants the Prowler identity or the Prowler tutelage — and this is not implausible given the Spider-extended ecosystem's tendency to generate inheritors — Aaron faces a choice that is essentially about whether his craft is something he wants to perpetuate or something he wants to terminate with him. The mentor capacity is genuine and the craft pride is genuine; the question is whether he can mentor *out* of the life rather than *into* it. A clean transfer of the identity to someone he turns from crime would be an act of substantial integration. A transfer to an apprentice who continues the work would be a quieter form of relapse — a way to remain operational without operating.

**Fork 6 — Public Exposure of the Past Identity.** If law enforcement, media, or a hostile party makes the Prowler-Aaron Davis link public in a way that cannot be deflected, the legitimate-life frame collapses. Driving work ends. Custody-level access to Miles becomes a question Jefferson would litigate. Aaron has no contingency plan for living as a publicly known former criminal in the civilian register; his entire reform has been predicated on the past being private. Exposure would force a choice between flight (return to full criminal life under a new identity), confrontation (public reckoning, possible incarceration, possible redemption narrative), or collapse. The middle path is the only one that preserves the Miles-channel and it is also the path most against his temperamental grain.

---

### 6.5 Growth Vectors — What Would Push Him Toward Integration

These are not predictions; they are levers. A benevolent surveillance posture identifies them because the point of the file is understanding-toward-help, not understanding-toward-control.

**Sustained, low-stakes, non-instrumental contact with Miles.** The single most therapeutic input available to Aaron is uneventful time with his nephew that does not involve gifts, jobs, advice, or stakes. He has never had this kind of relational time with anyone. Learning that contact can be the point — rather than the medium for something else — would substantially rewire his attachment-as-transaction default. Miles is the only person positioned to provide this, and Miles is young enough that he may not yet know to.

**A non-Miles, non-criminal competence.** Aaron's self-concept needs a second leg. If he develops a skill or practice that he is good at, that is legal, and that does not depend on Miles's admiration — mechanical work on vehicles, cooking, a trade, even a hobby he becomes obsessive about — the brittleness of the single-source self-concept reduces. This is more important than it sounds. A man with two sources of competence-based self-regard is dramatically more stable than a man with one.

**A confession he is not coerced into.** Aaron has confessed many times under pressure. He has not, on the available record, made a voluntary unforced disclosure of the foundational wound to anyone. The act of speaking it without being made to would change his relationship to it. The likely venue is improbable but not impossible — a long drive with Miles, a late conversation with Jefferson, a moment with a partner.

**Reconciliation with Jefferson, in any form.** Already addressed. The single highest-leverage growth input available.

**Being trusted with something he could betray and doesn't.** Aaron's self-concept is built on his competence; he has had less practice with his trustworthiness. Trustworthiness only accumulates by being exercised in conditions where betrayal was available and was declined. The 616 arc has begun this accrual but the deposits are small. Larger trusts — being asked to look after Miles in a real emergency, being given access to information he could sell, being made executor of something — would, if discharged, build the kind of integrated self that the criminal years prevented from forming.

**Therapeutic engagement.** Improbable given his temperament and demographic priors, but not impossible. Miles's generation has substantially normalized care, and Miles himself could be the broker. A clinician working with Aaron would face significant resistance for the first six to twelve months and could, past that point, do real work on the splitting and the shame architecture. The probability of him entering and remaining in care unprompted is low; the probability if Miles requests it as a condition of continued closeness is meaningfully higher.

---

### 6.6 Catastrophe Vectors — What Would Push Him Toward Collapse

The inverse register. These are the inputs that would route him toward the Ultimate-timeline attractor.

**Loss of Miles, by death or by repudiation.** The single highest-magnitude catastrophic input. Aaron's attachment economy cannot survive the loss of its sole object. Death of Miles would produce, within months, a return to operational criminality at a level higher than baseline — not for gain, for affect regulation. Repudiation by Miles would produce the same outcome via the additional pathway of shame-driven self-confirmation: if Miles has decided he is the man Jefferson said he was, then being that man becomes the path of least resistance.

**Death of Jefferson with the channel still closed.** Forecloses the reconciliation question permanently. The wound he has been working around for his entire adult life becomes structurally unhealable. Predict significant decompensation, possibly delayed by months, possibly manifested as recklessness rather than depression.

**Coercion by an operator he cannot betray.** Aaron's adaptive feature in coercive relationships is that he reliably turns on handlers who think they own him. An adversary sophisticated enough to coerce him without producing the betrayal-reflex — one who handles him by proxy, through threats to Miles or Jefferson rather than to him directly — would be able to keep him operational against his will for extended periods. This is the worst kind of relapse because it is involuntary and morally unambiguous to him; it accelerates the shame spiral.

**Physical capacity loss without warning.** Addressed in Fork 4. Worth restating as catastrophe vector.

**Successful seduction by the craft-pride frame.** The most insidious catastrophic input is not external pressure but internal nostalgia. A job offered to him not for money or under coercion but as a pure problem worthy of his abilities — the kind of approach that flatters the craftsman rather than the criminal — is the offer his defenses are weakest against. He can refuse need and refuse threat more easily than he can refuse the implicit assertion that he is the only person who can do the thing.

**Exposure to a non-Miles harm he caused in the past resurfacing.** A historical victim of an old job re-entering his life, particularly a victim whose harm he had managed to forget or minimize, would puncture the craftsman self-concept in a way the current-frame reform cannot absorb. He has organized his shame around Jefferson and around Miles; he has not organized it around the actual ledger of people he hurt across two decades. Confrontation with a single un-rationalized historical harm could produce either a deep integrative reckoning or a collapse-and-flee response, with the latter more probable absent a stable support frame.

---

### 6.7 The Honest Summary

Aaron Davis at the present observational window is a man whose modal outcome is neither full reform nor full relapse but a long, oscillating middle — a life of bounded relapses, partial repairs, accumulating bodily wear, and a slowly deepening but never fully secure relationship with his nephew. He will probably not die in his gauntlets in this timeline. He will probably also never be the man the 616 arc gestures at — the integrated former-thief who became a quiet uncle in full. He will live in the gap between those two figures and the quality of his life will be determined by how wide he lets the gap get and how many people stay in it with him.

The file's prognostic verdict is **guarded-optimistic, conditional on Miles**. The verdict shifts to **guarded-pessimistic** the moment the Miles-channel is interrupted for any reason longer than several months. The verdict shifts to **acute-risk** in the event of Miles's death, Jefferson's death without reconciliation, or sudden capacity loss without identity replacement.

The most actionable single insight for any party with benevolent interest in his trajectory is this: **the protective work is not getting him to stop being a thief; it is keeping the family frame around him intact and load-bearing while he does the slower work of becoming a man who does not need the thief identity to feel real.** Direct interventions against the criminality will fail or backfire. Indirect interventions that strengthen the attachment infrastructure will succeed at rates that look almost implausible from the outside, because they are operating on the actual variable rather than the visible one.

He is, in the end, a man whose entire adult life has been a long letter to his brother written in the only handwriting he knows. The trajectory question is whether the letter ever gets read, whether he ever learns another hand, and whether the boy who became the addressee-by-proxy can stay close enough, long enough, for the writing to slow down and become something other than a request to be let back in.

*— end Section 6 —*

## Relationship Graph
### [[Miles Gonzalo Morales (Spider-Man)]]
- Load-bearing bond; the one piece of his life his defenses cannot fully metabolize
- Sincere avuncular warmth; rapport built without effort, maintained across long absences
- FAILURE MODE: Miles is the leverage point any sophisticated opponent will find first. Aaron will coerce Miles when advantage requires it (Scorpion arc) and rationalize it as mentorship. The closer Miles gets, the more exposed he is to being used. The Spider-Verse outcome — Aaron dying rather than killing him — is the exception that proves the rule; in the modal case, Miles is endangered by proximity to Aaron's life
- LEVERAGE: any actor who can credibly threaten Miles owns Aaron's decision-making for the duration of the threat. Any actor who can credibly *protect* Miles in ways Aaron cannot earns provisional trust

### [[Jefferson Davis (Jefferson Morales)]]
- Estranged brother, mutual grief, the mirror Aaron will not look into
- Childhood bond never fully severed; both men carry the abusive father in different shapes
- FAILURE MODE: the comparison is the wound. Any framing that positions Aaron as the failed brother bypasses every defense. Jefferson knows this and has used it; it never works the way he wants it to — it produces shame-flight, not change
- LEVERAGE: Jefferson is the one person whose opinion Aaron cannot make himself stop tracking. An intelligence operator who can route a message through Jefferson reaches Aaron at a depth no other channel reaches

### [[Rio Morales]]
- Sister-in-law, wary, civil. Knows what he is. Tolerates him for Miles's sake and Jefferson's
- FAILURE MODE: if Rio ever bars him from Miles, Aaron will accept it verbally and circumvent it operationally. He does not respect that boundary because accepting it means accepting the diagnosis
- LEVERAGE: Rio's judgment is a proxy for the family verdict on him; her approval would matter more than he admits

### Hammerhead
- Transactional criminal-ecosystem relationship; Aaron has worked for/around him in 616
- FAILURE MODE: ownership-allergy. Any moment Hammerhead believes he owns Aaron is the moment Aaron begins planning the exit, which will involve betrayal
- LEVERAGE: Hammerhead can task him but cannot retain him; predictable defection window

### Tinkerer
- Tech supplier, occasional partner, professional respect
- FAILURE MODE: Aaron over-trusts gear he didn't audit himself; a compromised Tinkerer build is the single most plausible vector for his death (Ultimate precedent)
- LEVERAGE: anyone who compromises the Tinkerer pipeline compromises Aaron

### [[Peter Benjamin Parker (Spider-Man)]]
- MCU/Homecoming-adjacent: informant relationship, transactional, mutual respect
- FAILURE MODE: Aaron will help Spider-Man when it costs nothing and sell him out when it costs anything
- LEVERAGE: appeals to Miles's safety route through Spider-Man cleanly

### Miles Spider Man Identity
- Aaron learning Miles's secret is the central canonical hinge; in every continuity it ends badly
- FAILURE MODE: the knowledge is incompatible with his architecture — he either weaponizes it (Ultimate) or it kills him (Spider-Verse)
- LEVERAGE: who controls the disclosure controls the trajectory

### The Kingpin Fisk
- Spider-Verse: contract-issuer, ultimately executioner
- FAILURE MODE: Aaron took the Kingpin contract because the math closed; he could not foresee that the target's mask would come off and the architecture would fail in real time. Pattern: he underestimates the probability of his own integration moments
- LEVERAGE: Kingpin demonstrated that a sufficiently large contract gets Aaron in the room; nothing inside Aaron stops him from accepting it, only what happens once he's there
